"Introduction (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p>This deck has taken definitions outlined in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology"">Wikipedia's Glossary of underwater diving terminology</a> and put them into a form which can be easily learnt/revised using <a href=""https://apps.ankiweb.net/"">Anki</a> a cross platform app specifically designed for long term knowledge retention.</p>
<h2>Notes</h2>
<p>Please note the modifications which have been made &amp; where you can find updates.</p>
<ol align=""left"">
<li>The front of every card has ""(Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"" appended to the end so that if you have any other words in your collection, the Wikipedia definition will still be added when importing it.</li>
<li>Any updates or corrections to the deck will be available at <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Underwater-Diving-Terminology-Flashcards""></a><a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Underwater-Diving-Terminology-Flashcards"">https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Underwater-Diving-Terminology-Flashcards</a> so do return periodically to check if you have the latest version.</li>
</ol>
<p>Feel free to share the deck and give the repository a star so more people are likely to see this work and can get the most out of it.</p>

"AA6061 (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><style data-mw-deduplicate=""TemplateStyles:r1033289096"">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/6061_aluminium_alloy"" title=""6061 aluminium alloy"">6061 aluminium alloy</a></span></p>
Aluminium alloy used for manufacture of new diving cylinders exclusively since mid 1988 as it is not susceptible to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sustained_load_cracking"" title=""Sustained load cracking"">sustained load cracking</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Harlow_1999_1-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Harlow_1999-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-PSI_2016_2-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-PSI_2016-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"AA6351 (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aluminium_alloy#Wrought_alloys"" title=""Aluminium alloy"">Aluminium alloy#Wrought alloys</a></span></p>
Aluminium alloy 6351 is subject to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sustained_load_cracking"" title=""Sustained load cracking"">sustained load cracking</a> and requires periodical <span title=""See entry on this page at § eddy current test"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#eddy_current_test"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">eddy current testing</a></span> to identify crack development at an early stage.<sup id=""cite_ref-Harlow_1999_1-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Harlow_1999-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Not used for new cylinder manufacture since 1988, but many cylinders of this alloy are still in service.<sup id=""cite_ref-PSI_2016_2-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-PSI_2016-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"ABLJ (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#adjustable_buoyancy_life_jacket""><span title=""See entry on this page at § adjustable buoyancy life jacket"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">adjustable buoyancy life jacket</span></a></span></p>"
"absolute pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure_measurement#Absolute,_gauge_and_differential_pressures_-_zero_reference"" title=""Pressure measurement"">Pressure measurement#Absolute, gauge and differential pressures - zero reference</a></span></p>
Total static pressure at the reference point: Pressure relative to vacuum.
"
"ACD (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#auto-closure_device""><span title=""See entry on this page at § auto-closure device"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">auto-closure device</span></a></span></p>"
"A-clamp adaptor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § yoke adaptor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#yoke_adaptor"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">yoke adaptor</a></span></span></p>"
"A-clamp fitting (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"A-clamp valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § yoke fitting"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#yoke_fitting"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">yoke fitting</a></span>, and <a href=""#cGA_850""><span title=""See entry on this page at § CGA 850"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">CGA 850</span></a></span></p>"
"active addition (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Active_addition_semi-closed_circuit"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Active addition semi-closed circuit</a></span></p>
System for semi-closed circuit rebreather feed gas addition in which gas is added to the breathing circuit by a mechanism, regardless of current volume, and excess gas is vented to keep the loop volume within limits. Compare with <span title=""See entry on this page at § passive addition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#passive_addition"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">passive addition</a></span>
"
"activated carbon (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"activated charcoal (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Activated_carbon"" title=""Activated carbon"">Activated carbon</a></span></p>
A filter medium used to remove oil, water, and odours from breathing gas.
"
"ADAS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#australian_Diver_Accreditation_Scheme""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme</span></a></span></p>"
"ADCI (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#association_of_Diving_Contractors_International""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Association of Diving Contractors International"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Association of Diving Contractors International</span></a></span></p>"
"adjustable buoyancy life jacket (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""ABLJ"", ""Fenzy"" , or ""horse collar buoyancy compensator""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buoyancy_compensator_(diving)#Adjustable_buoyancy_life_jacket"" title=""Buoyancy compensator (diving)"">Buoyancy compensator (diving)#Adjustable buoyancy life jacket</a></span></p>
An early style of combination  <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buoyancy_compensator_(diving)"" title=""Buoyancy compensator (diving)"">buoyancy compensator</a> and inflatable life jacket worn on the chest and round the neck.<sup id=""cite_ref-BSAC_Manual_1982_3-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BSAC_Manual_1982-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"ADV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href=""#automatic_diluent_valve""><span title=""See entry on this page at § automatic diluent valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">automatic diluent valve</span></a></i> 
2.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href=""#automatic_dump_valve""><span title=""See entry on this page at § automatic dump valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">automatic dump valve</span></a></i>
"
"A-frame (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Part of a <span title=""See entry on this page at § launch and recovery system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#launch_and_recovery_system"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">launch and recovery system</a></span>. A gantry or davit for launching and recovering bells, stages, anchors, or large ROVs.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-Ships_and_Oil_5-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Ships_and_Oil-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Usually deployed by hydraulic rams which swing the frame over the deck or overboard as required. The load is hoisted and lowered by cables from the top of the frame.
"
"AGE (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#arterial_gas_embolism""><span title=""See entry on this page at § arterial gas embolism"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">arterial gas embolism</span></a></span></p>"
"aggressive decompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Conservatism"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Conservatism</a></span></p>
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_schedule"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Decompression schedule"">Decompression schedule</a> tending to shorter overall decompression time for a given pre-ascent dive profile, accepting increased risk of decompression sickness to reduce the overall ascent time.<sup id=""cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_6-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"air dome (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;A section of cave which traps air or other gas at the top. This gas is not directly connected to the atmosphere.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;The upper part of an open <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">diving bell</a> which can be filled with air for divers to breathe.
"
"air integration (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_computer#Additional_functionality_and_features"" title=""Dive computer"">Dive computer#Additional functionality and features</a></span></p>
Feature of some <span title=""See entry on this page at § dive computer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#dive_computer"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">dive computer</a></span>s to measure cylinder pressure  using an integral pressure gauge connected by HP hose to the regulator first stage, or receive data from one or more remote pressure transducers fitted to the HP port of a regulator, and display the pressure on the screen. Other features may also be available using the data.<sup id=""cite_ref-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"airlift (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airlift_(dredging_device)"" title=""Airlift (dredging device)"">Airlift (dredging device)</a></span></p>
A device based on a steeply rising pipe, used by divers to suck small objects, sand and mud from the sea bed and to transport the resulting debris upwards and away from its source. Air is injected into the lower end of the pipe and the rising bubbles entrain water and cause an upward flow which draws the material from the bottom along.
"
"airline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"air line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Airline"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">Surface-supplied diving#Airline</a></span></p>
Simple low pressure hose carrying breathing air from a surface supply to a diver.
"
"airline diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""hooka"", ""hookah""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Airline"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">Surface-supplied diving#Airline</a></span></p>
Surface-supplied diving where the breathing air is supplied to the diver by a simple hose. The diver usually breathes through a mouth held <span title=""See entry on this page at § demand valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#demand_valve"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">demand valve</a></span>.
"
"air top (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"air top-up (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">see: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving#Air_top-up"" title=""Gas blending for scuba diving"">Gas blending for scuba diving#Air top-up</a></span></p> 
1.&#160;&#160;Completing a planned breathing gas mix by topping up the cylinder with compressed air to a calculated pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-Oxyhacker_9-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Oxyhacker-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;Topping up a partly used breathing gas mix with compressed air, providing a different mixture which is analysed after the fill.<sup id=""cite_ref-Oxyhacker_9-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Oxyhacker-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
"
"algal bloom (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algal_bloom"" title=""Algal bloom"">Algal bloom</a></span></p>
A rapid increase or accumulation in the population of algae (typically microscopic) in an aquatic system. Some blooms may be recognized by discoloration of the water resulting from the high density of pigmented cells. Visibility can severely deteriorate over a period of hours to days.

<span class=""anchor"" id=""aLP""></span>"
"ALP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""/w/index.php?title=Articulated_Loading_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Articulated Loading Platform (page does not exist)"">Articulated Loading Platform</a>, a type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_buoy_mooring"" title=""Single buoy mooring"">single buoy mooring</a> consisting of a buoyant upper structure with a lattice leg linked by an articulating joint to a mooring.<sup id=""cite_ref-HSE_terminology_10-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-HSE_terminology-10"">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
"
"alternative air source (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alternative_air_source"" title=""Alternative air source"">Alternative air source</a></span></p>
A secondary supply of air or other breathing gas used by a diver in an emergency. See also <span title=""See entry on this page at § emergency gas supply"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#emergency_gas_supply"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">emergency gas supply</a></span> (EGS)
"
"alternobaric vertigo (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alternobaric_vertigo"" title=""Alternobaric vertigo"">Alternobaric vertigo</a></span></p>
Dizziness caused by different internal pressure in the middle ears.
"
"altitude diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altitude_diving"" title=""Altitude diving"">Altitude diving</a></span></p>
Diving at a location where the water surface is at an altitude which requires modification of decompression schedules.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_11-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> (more than about 300&#160;m (980&#160;ft) above sea level.
"
"ambient pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ambient_pressure"" title=""Ambient pressure"">Ambient pressure</a></span></p>
Pressure of the local surroundings.
"
"anoxia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypoxia_(medical)"" title=""Hypoxia (medical)"">Hypoxia (medical)</a></span></p>
Tissues completely lacking in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen"" title=""Oxygen"">oxygen</a>.
"
"anoxic (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Environment or gas completely lacking in oxygen.
"
"AODC (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""/w/index.php?title=Association_of_Offshore_Diving_Contractors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Association of Offshore Diving Contractors (page does not exist)"">Association of Offshore Diving Contractors</a>, one of the predecessors to the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Marine_Contractors_Association"" title=""International Marine Contractors Association"">International Marine Contractors Association</a> (IMCA).<sup id=""cite_ref-Gibson_OGP_12-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gibson_OGP-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
"
"aphasia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphasia"" title=""Aphasia"">Aphasia</a></span></p>
An impairment of language ability which may range from having difficulty remembering words to being completely unable to speak, read, or write
"
"apnea (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apnea"" title=""Apnea"">Suspension of breathing</a>, breath-hold.
2.&#160;&#160;<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freediving"" title=""Freediving"">Freediving</a>.
"
"appropriate breathing mix (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"appropriate breathing gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Choosing_a_suitable_breathing_gas_mixture"" title=""Scuba gas planning"">Scuba gas planning#Choosing a suitable breathing gas mixture</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving#Atmosphere_control"" title=""Saturation diving"">Saturation diving#Atmosphere control</a></span></p>
A breathing gas mixture that is suitable in composition and temperature, and of adequate pressure, having regard to the system and equipment used in the diving operations, the work undertaken in those operations, and the conditions and depth at which they are to be carried out.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Aqua-lung (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aqua-lung"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Aqua-lung"">Aqua-lung</a></span></p>
Self contained open circuit demand underwater breathing equipment consisting of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder"" title=""Diving cylinder"">diving cylinder</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator"" title=""Diving regulator"">diving regulator</a>.
"
"arterial bubble model (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_decompression_research_and_development#The_arterial_bubble_decompression_model"" title=""History of decompression research and development"">History of decompression research and development#The arterial bubble decompression model</a></span></p>
Decompression model in which the filtering capacity of the lung is assumed to have a threshold radius of the size of a red blood cell and sufficiently small decompression bubbles can pass to the arterial side, especially during the initial phase of ascent.
"
"arterial gas embolism (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arterial_gas_embolism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Arterial gas embolism"">Arterial gas embolism</a></span></p>
Blockage of an artery by a gas bubble. A possible consequence of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lung_overpressure_injury"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Lung overpressure injury"">lung overpressure injury</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a>.
"
"articulated loading platform (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#aLP""><span title=""See entry on this page at § ALP"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">ALP</span></a></span></p>"
"AR vest (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A waistcoat (vest) style <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Jacket_harness"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">harness</a> of heavy cloth with strong adjustable webbing straps so that the diver can not slide out under any reasonably foreseeable circumstance.<sup id=""cite_ref-ARvest_14-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ARvest-14"">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
"
"ascent (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ascending_and_descending_(diving)"" title=""Ascending and descending (diving)"">Ascending and descending (diving)</a></span></p>
Part of the dive profile where the diver is moving upwards towards the surface. An ascent may be interrupted by <span title=""See entry on this page at § stops"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#stops"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">stops</a></span> (q.v.), when the diver maintains a functionally constant depth for the purpose of decompression, and <span title=""See entry on this page at § pulls"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#pulls"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">pulls</a></span> (q.v.), during which periods there is consistently upwards movement (minor variations in the scale of a few seconds are generally ignored).
"
"ascent rate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Ascent_rate"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Ascent rate</a></span></p>
The rate at which depth is reduced at the end of a dive. An important component of decompression.
"
"A.S.S.E.T. (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""/w/index.php?title=Association_of_SCUBA_Service_Engineers_and_Technicians&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Association of SCUBA Service Engineers and Technicians (page does not exist)"">Association of SCUBA Service Engineers and Technicians</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Scuba_engineer_15-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Scuba_engineer-15"">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>

"Association of Diving Contractors International (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also:""ADCI""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""/w/index.php?title=Association_of_Diving_Contractors_International&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Association of Diving Contractors International (page does not exist)"">Association of Diving Contractors International</a></span></p> 
A non-profit organization to promote commercial diving, and establish and encourage observance of safe standards for commercial diving.

"atmospheres absolute (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_atmosphere_(unit)"" title=""Standard atmosphere (unit)"">Standard atmosphere (unit)</a></span></p>
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Units_of_measurement"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Units of measurement"">Unit</a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absolute_pressure"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Absolute pressure"">absolute pressure</a> equivalent to standard <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure"" title=""Atmospheric pressure"">atmospheric pressure</a>.
"
"atmospheric diving suit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"ADS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_diving_suit"" title=""Atmospheric diving suit"">Atmospheric diving suit</a></span></p>
A small one-man articulated submersible of anthropomorphic form which resembles a suit of armour, with elaborate pressure joints to allow articulation while maintaining an internal pressure of one atmosphere.
"
"attack swimmer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#combat_swimmer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § combat swimmer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">combat swimmer</span></a></span></p>"
"attendant (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § diver&#39;s attendant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diver&#39;s_attendant"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diver's attendant</a></span></span></p>
<p><span class=""anchor"" id=""australian_Diver_Accreditation_Scheme""></span>
</p>"
"Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australian_Diver_Accreditation_Scheme"" title=""Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme"">Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme</a></span></p> 
An international commercial and occupational diver certification scheme based in Australia.
"
"auto-closure device (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"automatic closure device (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""ACD""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#Automatic_closure_device"" title=""Diving regulator"">Diving regulator#Automatic closure device</a></span></p>
A mechanism for automatically closing off the inlet opening of a regulator first stage when it is disconnected from a cylinder to seal it against ingress of contamination.<sup id=""cite_ref-ACD_Series_Yoke_16-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ACD_Series_Yoke-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-Buzzacott_2018_17-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Buzzacott_2018-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
"
"automatic diluent valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#Automatic_diluent_valve_(ADV)"" title=""Diving regulator"">Automatic Diluent Valve</a></span></p>
A demand valve set into the breathing loop of a rebreather to inject <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diluent_gas"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diluent gas"">diluent gas</a> into the loop when the loop volume falls and there is not enough gas for inhalation.
"
"automatic dump valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Adjustable spring-loaded overpressure valve with manual override used on a <a href=""#constant_volume_dry_suit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § constant volume dry suit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">constant volume dry suit</span></a> to automatically discharge excess suit inflation gas as it expands during ascent, thereby maintaining a nearly constant volume and buoyancy of the suit.
"
"Autonomous diver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous_diver"" title=""Autonomous diver"">Autonomous diver</a></span></p> 
EN 14153-2 / ISO 24801-2 standard competence for recreational scuba diver. The level 2 ""Autonomous diver"" has sufficient knowledge, skill and experience to make dives, in open water, which do not require in-water decompression stops, to a recommended maximum depth of 20&#160;m with other scuba divers of the same level, only when appropriate support is available at the surface, and under conditions that are equal or better than the conditions in which they were trained, without supervision of a scuba instructor, unless they have additional training or are accompanied by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_leader"" title=""Dive leader"">dive leader</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-EUF_certification_18-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EUF_certification-18"">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
"
"available gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Available_gas"" title=""Scuba gas planning"">Scuba gas planning#Available gas</a></span></p> 
Breathing gas available from a cylinder after taking into account ambient pressure and the pressure needed for correct function of the delivery system at a useful flow rate. This may also take into account a reserve allocation. 
 

"
"back gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">Breathing gas</a> carried by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_diving"" title=""Scuba diving"">scuba diver</a> in <a href=""#backmount""><span title=""See entry on this page at § backmount"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">back mounted</span></a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder"" title=""Diving cylinder"">cylinders</a>. Generally the primary breathing gas for the bottom or longest sector of a dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"back kick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"backward kick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_kick_(finning)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Back kick (finning)"">Back kick (finning)</a></span></p>
A finning technique for moving backwards. Not an easy, powerful or elegant kick, but useful in many situations. The fins are angled outwards in opposite directions with the legs straight, then swept upwards and towards the diver by bending the knees in the power stroke. The knees may move downwards a bit at the same time by bending at the hips for stability. The return stroke feathers the fins by pointing them backwards in line with the body axis, to reduce forward thrust until the legs are straight again
"
"backmount (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"back mount (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The practice of carrying a scuba set on the back of the diver, supported by a harness, <a href=""#backplate""><span title=""See entry on this page at § backplate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">backplate</span></a> or <span title=""See entry on this page at § stabilisor jacket"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#stabilisor_jacket"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">stabilisor jacket</a></span> BCD. Compare with <span title=""See entry on this page at § sidemount"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#sidemount"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">sidemount</a></span>
"
"backpack (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A rigid or semi-rigid structure similar in function to a <a href=""#backplate""><span title=""See entry on this page at § backplate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">backplate</span></a>, usually made of moulded plastic, but sometimes of metal, used either as a stiffener and reinforcement for a jacket style buoyancy compensator, or as the basis of a scuba harness independent of a buoyancy compensator. The backpack supports and stabilises the scuba cylinder on the diver's back.
"
"backplate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backplate_and_wing"" title=""Backplate and wing"">Backplate and wing</a></span></p>
A plate, normally made from metal, which rests against the diver’s back, and to which the primary scuba cylinders are attached. Held to the body by harness straps over the shoulders and round the waist. Sometimes also crotch straps and chest straps. Usually used with a back inflation buoyancy compensator.
"
"backup light (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_light"" title=""Dive light"">Dive light</a> carried as a spare to be used in case of failure of the primary light.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"backup regulator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""secondary regulator""</span></p>
A second complete <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_regulator"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Scuba regulator"">scuba regulator</a> connected to a cylinder or manifolded twin set.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Compare with <span title=""See entry on this page at § octopus regulator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#octopus_regulator"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">octopus regulator</a></span>.
"
"backward roll (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"backward roll entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"back roll entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries"" title=""Scuba skills"">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
Water entry method in which the seated diver rolls backwards off the side of the boat, allowing the scuba cylinders to strike the water first.<sup id=""cite_ref-BSAC_Sport_Diving_1985_19-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BSAC_Sport_Diving_1985-19"">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup class=""reference nowrap""><span title=""Page / location: 125"">&#58;&#8202;125&#8202;</span></sup>
"
"bailout block (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A <span title=""See entry on this page at § gas switching block"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#gas_switching_block"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">gas switching block</a></span> specifically intended for connection of a bailout set to the main gas supply (which may be scuba or surface supply) which allows the diver to switch from main gas supply to emergency gas supply while continuously using the same mouthpiece, regulator second stage, full face mask or helmet. A bailout block is generally used on open circuit breathing apparatus, the equivalent function on a rebreather is provided by a <a href=""#bailout_valve""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bailout valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bailout valve</span></a> (BOV). The bailout block may be mounted on the side of a diving helmet or full-face mask, or may be mounted in a convenient place on the diver's harness, and includes a bailout valve, used to select the gas source, and one or more non-return valves to ensure that the emergency gas supply is directed only to the diver.
"
"bailout bottle (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"bailout cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bailout_cylinder"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Bailout cylinder"">Bailout cylinder</a></span></p>
A scuba cylinder carried by an underwater diver for use as an emergency supply of breathing gas in the event of a primary gas supply failure.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bailout set (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"bailout system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""EGS"", ""emergency gas supply""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bailout_cylinder"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Bailout cylinder"">Bailout cylinder</a></span></p>
An independent breathing gas supply carried by a diver for use in case of failure of the main gas supply. Usually consists of a bailout cylinder with a first stage regulator, and either a second stage regulator or connected to a bailout block or bailout valve (q.v.) A submersible pressure gauge is also usually provided.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_20-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bailout valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<i>Also: ""integrated open-circuit regulator""</i>
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#Bailout_valve_(BOV)"" title=""Diving regulator"">An open circuit demand valve</a> built into a rebreather mouthpiece, or other part of the breathing loop, which can be isolated while the diver is using the rebreather to recycle breathing gas, and opened at the same time as isolating the breathing loop when the diver bails out to open circuit.
2.&#160;&#160;A valve which opens the gas supply from the bailout cylinder of a surface supplied diver, used in case of surface gas failure, usually mounted on the side of a diving helmet or full-face mask, or on a manifold block on the diver's harness.
"
"baited remote underwater video (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baited_remote_underwater_video"" title=""Baited remote underwater video"">Baited remote underwater video</a></span></p>
A system for assessing fish populations using video cameras to record fish attracted to a bait canister.
"
"balanced regulator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechanism_of_diving_regulators#Balancing"" title=""Mechanism of diving regulators"">Mechanism of diving regulators#Balancing</a></span></p>
Regulator designed to provide a consistent demand effort not affected by cylinder gas pressure or depth.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"band mask (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Band_mask"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">Surface-supplied diving#Band mask</a></span></p>
A heavy duty full-face mask with many of the characteristics of a lightweight demand helmet. In structure it is the front section of a lightweight helmet from above the faceplate to below the demand valve and exhaust ports, including the bailout block and communications connections on the sides. This rigid frame is attached to a neoprene hood by a metal clamping band, hence the name.
"
"bands (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#cylinder_bands""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cylinder bands"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cylinder bands</span></a></span></p>"
"bar (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit)"" title=""Bar (unit)"">bar (unit)</a></span></p>
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metric_system"" title=""Metric system"">Metric</a> <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Units_of_measurement"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Units of measurement"">unit</a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure"" title=""Pressure"">pressure</a> commonly used in diving, equal to 100&#160;kiloPascal, and nearly equal to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_atmospheric_pressure"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Standard atmospheric pressure"">standard atmospheric pressure</a>.
"
"barodontalgia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barodontalgia"" title=""Barodontalgia"">Barodontalgia</a></span></p>
Tooth pain caused by pressure change.
"
"barotrauma (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barotrauma"" title=""Barotrauma"">Barotrauma</a></span></p>
Injury caused by pressure difference.
"
"baseline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<i>Also: ""tank factor""</i>. Numeric value computed for a cylinder or manifolded set that relates volume and pressure in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_system_of_units"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Imperial system of units"">imperial system of units</a>. Computed by dividing <span title=""See entry on this page at § nominal capacity"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#nominal_capacity"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">nominal capacity</a></span> (cubic feet) by cylinder working pressure (psi) to express cubic feet of volume per psi of fill pressure (sometimes multiplied by 100 to give cubic feet per 100 psi). Used to convert cylinder pressure to free gas volume.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;A line that is a base for measurement or for construction; see <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Datum_(geodesy)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Datum (geodesy)"">datum</a> (calculations or comparisons)
3.&#160;&#160;A data set which is a point of reference (engineering or science) for later data.
"
"basket (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § diving stage"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_stage"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diving stage</a></span></span></p>"
"BAT wing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Buoyancy and trim wing. A back mounted buoyancy compensator cell used with <span title=""See entry on this page at § sidemount"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#sidemount"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">sidemount</a></span> harness. The buoyancy volume is mostly over the lower back.<sup id=""cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_21-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"BC (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"BCD (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#buoyancy_compensator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § buoyancy compensator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">buoyancy compensator</span></a></span></p>"
"BCD blowup (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Uncontrolled buoyant ascent caused by inability to release gas from the buoyancy compensator faster than it expands due to pressure reduction of ascent.
"
"beach master (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § dive marshall"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#dive_marshall"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">dive marshall</a></span></span></p>
A person on the beach who records when divers enter and exit the water. Typically used during recreational scuba training to keep track of the students, watch the gear, and provide assistance when required.
"
"bell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § diving bell"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_bell"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diving bell</a></span></i>
2.&#160;&#160;<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_communications#Commercial_diving_rope_signals"" title=""Diver communications"">Short tug on a lifeline</a>, used in pairs, for signalling purposes.
"
"bell bounce dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Surface oriented diving operation in which the divers are transported in and deployed from a closed bell, and are either decompressed in the bell at the surface or transferred under pressure to a deck decompression chamber for decompression.
"
"bell cursor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell#Deployment_of_a_modern_diving_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">Diving bell#Deployment of a modern diving bell</a></span></p>
Mechanism or structure for guiding and constraining the motion of a bell when in the close vicinity of the deployment platform to improve handling in bad weather.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bell diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Any diving operation in which the divers travel in or work from a diving bell
2.&#160;&#160;Diving operations in which divers are transported in and deployed from a closed bell, either as a surface oriented (bell bounce) or saturation dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_20-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bell harness (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A safety <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Diver&#39;s_harness"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">harness</a> made of strong webbing, which is fastened around a diver over the exposure suit, and allows the diver to be lifted without risk of falling out of the harness.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bell_harness_22-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bell_harness-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bellman (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell#Deployment_of_a_modern_diving_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">Diving bell#Deployment of a modern diving bell</a></span></p>
Standby diver deployed in the diving bell<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bellows ratio (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The swept volume ratio between the inner and outer bellows of the counterlung of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_rebreather#Concentric_bellows_counterlungs"" title=""Diving rebreather"">passive addition semi-closed rebreather</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-DC55_23-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DC55-23"">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bell run (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The part of a bell dive operation from bell lock-off to bell lock-on (from and back to the life support system)<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bell stage (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A framework extending below a closed bell which keeps the base of the pressure vessel off the bottom sufficiently to provide clearance for the divers to use the bottom hatch when the bell is resting on the bottom or on the clump weight.
"
"bell umbilical (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_cable#Diver"" title=""Umbilical cable"">Umbilical cable#Diver</a></span></p>
The combined supply and return hoses and cables for life-support, power and communications between a diving bell and the support platform
"
"belt slide (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"belt slider (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""triglide"", ""weight slider"", ""weight stop""</span></p> 
Hardware item with two parallel slots which is fitted to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backplate_and_wing#Harness"" title=""Backplate and wing"">harness</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_weighting_system"" title=""Diving weighting system"">weightbelt</a> webbing to prevent other components such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-rings"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""D-rings"">D-rings</a> and weights from sliding along the webbing.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"benign water (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"benign conditions (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benign_water"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Benign water"">Benign water</a></span></p>
Sometimes also referred to as confined water.  Environments of low risk, where it is extremely unlikely or impossible for the diver to get lost or entrapped, or be exposed to hazards other than the basic underwater environment.
"
"bent D-ring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-ring"" title=""D-ring"">D-ring</a> which has been bent about 45° near the straight section on both sides, forcing it to project slightly from the harness when pushed to one side, allowing easier attachment of clips.
"
"bends (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">Decompression sickness</a>: Injury caused by bubble formation in the body tissues after hyperbaric exposure.

"
"BIBS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#built_in_breathing_system""><span title=""See entry on this page at § built in breathing system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">built in breathing system</span></a></span></p>"
"bifin (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"bi-fin (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"bi fin (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<span title=""See entry on this page at § Swimfin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#Swimfin"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">Swimfin</a></span> worn on one foot. One of a pair. The term is usually used in the context of <span title=""See entry on this page at § freediving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#freediving"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">freediving</a></span> and <span title=""See entry on this page at § finswimming"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#finswimming"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">finswimming</a></span> to distinguish the style having a blade mounted on a single <span title=""See entry on this page at § foot pocket"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#foot_pocket"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">foot pocket</a></span> from <span title=""See entry on this page at § monofin"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#monofin"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">monofin</a></span>s, which have a single blade and two foot pockets. In <span title=""See entry on this page at § scuba diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#scuba_diving"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">scuba diving</a></span>, <span title=""See entry on this page at § surface-supplied diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#surface-supplied_diving"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">surface-supplied diving</a></span> and <span title=""See entry on this page at § snorkelling"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#snorkelling"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">snorkelling</a></span> they are usually referred to simply as fins or swimfins.
"
"Billy ring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Three <span title=""See entry on this page at § D-ring"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#D-ring"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">D-ring</a></span>s welded together along their straight sides so that one is perpendicular to the other two, which lie on the same plane. This uses the two flat rings to maintain the third in an upright position when mounted on harness webbing, allowing it to be more easily accessed to clip on stage cylinders. Named after <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Deans_(diver)"" title=""Billy Deans (diver)"">Billy Deans</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"BK hook (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"B.K. hook (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"BK safety hook (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A type of safety <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lifting_hook"" title=""Lifting hook"">lifting hook</a> which is held closed when under load by a lever system where the weight of the load holds the bill of the hook against the safety latch.<sup id=""cite_ref-BK_hook_24-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BK_hook-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
"
"black-water diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">see also: <a href=""#blue-water_diving""><span title=""See entry on this page at § blue-water diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">blue-water diving</span></a></span></p> 
Diving in mid-water at night where the bottom is out of diving range.
"
"blending stick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Mixing tube in which gases are continuously mixed prior to intake by a compressor, usually at atmospheric pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-Oxyhacker_9-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Oxyhacker-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Usually refers to manufacture of nitrox from air with added oxygen, but also used for trimix. Gas mixture is usually continuously analysed at the exit of the blending stick to monitor composition.
"
"blind traverse (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Passing through a cave from one entrance to a different exit which the diver has not used before.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"block adaptor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Screw-in adaptor fitting which is fitted to a 200/240 bar DIN pillar valve to allow connection of a yoke regulator or filling whip.
"
"blowdown (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Procedure of pressurising a diving chamber or saturation habitat.
2.&#160;&#160;Procedure of driving water out of the bottom of an open diving bell by displacing it with air or other breathing gas at ambient pressure.
"
"blowout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blowout_(well_drilling)"" title=""Blowout (well drilling)"">Blowout (well drilling)</a></span></p>
Uncontrolled release of crude oil and/or natural gas from a well after pressure control systems have failed.
"
"blowout preventer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blowout_preventer"" title=""Blowout preventer"">Blowout preventer</a></span></p>
A large, specialized valve used to seal, control and monitor oil and gas wells. Generally operated remotely by hydraulic ram.
"
"blowout preventer stack (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
An assembly of several <a href=""#blowout_preventer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § blowout preventer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">blowout preventer</span></a> rams which may be used to shut off a well.
"
"blue hole (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_hole"" title=""Blue hole"">Blue hole</a></span></p>
A sink hole in a lake or the sea that is often the entrance to a cave. Blue holes in the sea are subject to tides so that their flows regularly reverse.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"blue-water diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_diving#Diving_environment"" title=""Underwater diving"">Underwater diving#Diving environment</a></span></p>
Underwater diving in mid-water where the bottom is not visible and is out of diving range.<sup id=""cite_ref-Haddock_and_Heine_25-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Haddock_and_Heine-25"">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>

"
"bolt snap (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolt_snap"" title=""Bolt snap"">bolt snap</a></span></p>
A metal connector comprising a hook with a spring-loaded axial sliding rod which must be manually retracted to allow the hook to be clipped onto something or removed. May be single- or double-ended, and if single-ended is usually fitted with a swivel ring opposite the jaws.
"
"bomb (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Commercial diver slang for high pressure gas storage cylinder of around 50 litres water capacity, also known as a ""J"".
"
"bondage wing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#bungee_wing""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bungee wing"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bungee wing</span></a></span></p>
Derogatory term for bungee wing based on <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fetishist"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fetishist"">fetishist</a> terminology.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_26-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bonnet (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The upper part of a copper helmet which encloses the diver's head and is sealed to the lower part or <a href=""#corselet""><span title=""See entry on this page at § corselet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">corselet</span></a> (q.v.)
"
"booster (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"booster pump (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Booster_pump"" title=""Booster pump"">Booster pump</a></span></p>
Machine used to increase pressure of a gas. Usually refers to the case where inlet pressure is above ambient pressure already.
"
"BOP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#blowout_preventer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § blowout preventer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">blowout preventer</span></a></span></p>"
"BOP stack (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
