<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#blowout_preventer_stack""><span title=""See entry on this page at § blowout preventer stack"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">blowout preventer stack</span></a></span></p>"
"bottom gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">gas breathed</a> by the diver at the deepest part of the dive. Compare with <span title=""See entry on this page at § travel gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#travel_gas"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">travel gas</a></span> and <span title=""See entry on this page at § decompression gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#decompression_gas"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">decompression gas</a></span>.
"
"bottom time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Time used in calculating decompression obligation from decompression tables. For most tables this is defined as the elapsed time from starting the descent to starting the final ascent to the surface, excluding ascent and decompression time.<sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2001_27-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2001-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bottom timer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Device used to measure and record the total time spent underwater during a dive. They do not generally only record <a href=""#bottom_time""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bottom time"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bottom time</span></a> (q.v.).
"
"bottom out (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A rebreather counterlung becoming completely deflated during inhalation.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_28-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bounce dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"bounce diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Also: ""surface oriented dive""&#160;: In <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_diving"" title=""Commercial diving"">commercial diving</a>, bounce diving is the alternative to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving"" title=""Saturation diving"">saturation diving</a>. Any dive where the diver is decompressed directly after the dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;In <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recreational_diving"" title=""Recreational diving"">recreational diving</a>, a bounce dive is a descent to maximum depth and then a direct ascent back to the surface with minimal bottom time, in a dive profile resembling a spike.
"
"BOV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#bailout_valve""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bailout valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bailout valve</span></a></span></p>"
"bowline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bowline"" title=""Bowline"">Bowline</a></span></p>
Knot used to form a secure, non-slipping loop at the end of a line.
"
"Boyle's law (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boyle%27s_law"" title=""Boyle&#39;s law"">Boyle's law</a></span></p>
Relationship between pressure and volume at constant temperature in an ideal gas.
"
"breakdown room (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
An area in a cave where a large amount of material has fallen from the overhead.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"breakout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The point at which an object being lifted which is partly embedded in the bottom sediments overcomes the adhesion of the sediments and the force required to lift it drops rapidly to the apparent weight of the object.
"
"breakthrough (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The failure of a rebreather scrubber to remove all the carbon dioxide in the gas passing through the absorbent material.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_28-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"breastplate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#corselet""><span title=""See entry on this page at § corselet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">corselet</span></a></span></p>"
"breathing gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"breathing mixture (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">Breathing gas</a></span></p>
Gas supplied to the diver to breathe, either directly to the diver or to the hyperbaric environment of the diving bell, dive chamber or saturation habitat.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_20-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2001_27-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2001-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Colloquially just ""gas"" or ""mix"".
"
"breathing hose (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Large bore hose carrying the breathing gas in a rebreather breathing loop<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_28-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> or a twin-hose demand valve.
"
"breathing loop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The gas flow path in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather"" title=""Rebreather"">rebreather</a> comprising the diver's lungs, the mouthpiece, valves, hoses, counterlungs and scrubber through which gas is rebreathed.
"
"B-ring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A small plate with a slot for a webbing belt and two side by side holes for clipping on equipment, generally used similarly to a <span title=""See entry on this page at § D-ring"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#D-ring"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">D-ring</a></span> in combination with a <a href=""#belt_slider""><span title=""See entry on this page at § belt slider"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">belt slider</span></a> as an alternative to a <a href=""#butterfly_slider""><span title=""See entry on this page at § butterfly slider"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">butterfly slider</span></a>
"
"Broco cutter (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A type of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermal_lance"" title=""Thermal lance"">thermal lance</a> initiated by an electric arc, in common use for underwater cutting work.
"
"BRUV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#baited_remote_underwater_video""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Baited remote underwater video"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Baited remote underwater video</span></a></span></p>"
"BTV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ear_clearing#Methods"" title=""Ear clearing"">Ear clearing#Methods</a></span></p>
<i>Béance tubaire volontaire</i>: Voluntary opening of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eustachian_tube"" title=""Eustachian tube"">Eustachian tubes</a> to equalise the middle ear.

"
"bubble models (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Bubble_models"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Bubble models</a></span></p>
Decompression models based on the assumption that bubbles will form during non-symptomatic decompression.
"
"buccal pumping (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § glossopharangeal insufflation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#glossopharangeal_insufflation"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">glossopharangeal insufflation</a></span></span></p>"
"buddy bottle (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bailout_cylinder"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Bailout cylinder"">Bailout cylinder</a> carried by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_diving"" title=""Scuba diving"">scuba diver</a>, particularly when <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solo_diving"" title=""Solo diving"">diving solo</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-11"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"buddy breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Sharing breathing gas from one demand valve by two or more divers, generally after an out-of-gas emergency.
"
"buddy check (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddy_check"" title=""Buddy check"">Buddy check</a></span></p>
A procedure carried out by scuba divers using the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddy_system"" title=""Buddy system"">buddy system</a> where each diver checks that the other's <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_equipment"" title=""Diving equipment"">diving equipment</a> is configured, fitted, and functioning correctly just before entering the water to dive.
"
"buddy diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddy_diving"" title=""Buddy diving"">Buddy diving</a></span></p>
A safety procedure where two or three divers monitor each other constantly during a dive and provide assistance or rescue when needed.
"
"buddy lights (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Warning lights visible to the diver's buddy that indicate rebreather system status.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_28-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"buddy line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A short line between two divers, used to maintain contact during a dive, generally in poor visibility, or other conditions where the divers might become separated and not be able to quickly locate each other.<sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2001_27-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2001-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
"
"buddy system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddy_diving"" title=""Buddy diving"">Buddy diving</a></span></p>
A procedure where two divers look out for the safety of each other, and give assistance if the other gets into difficulty.
"
"Bühlmann algorithm (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"Bühlmann tables (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%BChlmann_decompression_algorithm"" title=""Bühlmann decompression algorithm"">Bühlmann decompression algorithm</a></span></p>
Diving tables and decompression algorithm on which the tables are based, and some dive computers are programmed, based on the dissolved gas decompression model derived and tested by Dr <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_A._B%C3%BChlmann"" title=""Albert A. Bühlmann"">Albert A. Bühlmann</a>.
"
"built in breathing system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""BIBS""</span></p>
A demand breathing gas supply system with external exhaust used to provide chamber occupants with breathing gases other than the gas used to pressurise the chamber. Used for treatment gases and emergency breathing gas if the chamber is contaminated.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_11-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
"
"bundle (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A set of gas cylinders fastened together for transportation and manifolded for use as a unit,<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS10019:2019_29-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS10019:2019-29"">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> also cylinder bundle.
"
"bungee (sidemount) (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § ring bungee"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#ring_bungee"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">ring bungee</a></span></span></p>
Length of shock cord used to restrain the top end of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Side_mount_diving"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Side mount diving"">side mount cylinders</a> and keep them tucked in at the diver's shoulder while swimming.<sup id=""cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_21-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Usually clipped to a shoulder <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-ring"" title=""D-ring"">D-ring</a> of the harness and looped around the cylinder valve. May be attached to the back of the harness between the shoulder blades, or run continuous from one shoulder D-ring, around the back under the arms to the other shoulder D-ring.
"
"bungee wing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Back inflation <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backplate_and_wing"" title=""Backplate and wing"">buoyancy compensator</a> with shock cord lacing or loops which exert a force on the bladder to oppose expansion during inflation and accelerate deflation.
"
"buoyancy (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buoyancy"" title=""Buoyancy"">Buoyancy</a></span></p>
1.&#160;&#160;Upward force on an object immersed in a fluid due to pressure exerted over the immersed surface.
2.&#160;&#160;Resultant upward force of buoyancy and weight of an object immersed in a fluid.
"
"buoyancy check (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Procedure to test and adjust weights carried by an underwater diver. The diver wears all the personal equipment to be used for the planned dive, with the scuba tank(s) nearly empty, and the buoyancy compensator empty, in shallow water of the same density as expected on the dive, and adds or removes weights until neutrally buoyant. After the buoyancy check it is usual to distribute the weights for safety, trim and convenience.
"
"buoyancy compensator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""ABLJ"", ""BC"", ""BCD"", ""buoyancy compensator device"", ""horse collar"", ""stabilisor jacket"", ""stab jacket"" or ""<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backplate_and_wing"" title=""Backplate and wing"">wing</a>""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buoyancy_compensator_(diving)"" title=""Buoyancy compensator (diving)"">Buoyancy compensator (diving)</a></span></p>
An airtight bladder worn by a diver which can be filled with air and vented to adjust and control the buoyancy of the diver.
"
"buoyancy control (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The skill of maintaining the appropriate <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buoyancy"" title=""Buoyancy"">buoyancy</a> at any time during a dive.
"
"burn tester (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Device for measuring the actual capacity of a battery relative to its nominal capacity, and the associated functional time for the device that the battery is powering.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-12"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"burn time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The effective use time of a battery powered device. Mainly used in reference to dive lights and scooters.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-13"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"burst disk (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rupture_disk"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Rupture disk"">Rupture disk</a></span></p>
A non-reclosing pressure relief device used to protect a diving cylinder from overpressurization.
"
"butterfly clip (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A type of <a href=""#bolt_snap""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bolt snap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bolt snap</span></a> with a tapered guide gate opening formed by a protrusion on both the piston and the fixed sides of the gate.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-14"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"butterfly slider (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"butterfly D-ring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A plate with two D-shaped cutouts on opposite sides of two to four parallel longitudinal slots for webbing. Used at the top back of the <a href=""#crotch_strap""><span title=""See entry on this page at § crotch strap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">crotch strap</span></a> in place of a butt-plate (q.v.) on minimalist <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Side_mount_diving"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Side mount diving"">sidemount</a> harnesses as a clip-on point for equipment.<sup id=""cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_21-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"butt-plate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A rigid or fairly stiff flexible lower extension to a <a href=""#backplate""><span title=""See entry on this page at § backplate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">backplate</span></a> or other scuba harness supporting butt-plate rails, used for clipping off the lower end of sidemount cylinders to the harness.<sup id=""cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_21-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>


"
"cage diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Diving in a cage designed to protect the diver from potentially aggressive large marine animals, usually sharks
"
"calibration gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Gas of known composition used to calibrate <span title=""See entry on this page at § gas sensor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#gas_sensor"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">gas sensors</a></span>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_28-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"CALM (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#catenary_anchor_leg_mooring""><span title=""See entry on this page at § catenary anchor leg mooring"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">catenary anchor leg mooring</span></a></span></p>"
"cam band (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A strap, usually of webbing, with a cam action tensioning buckle, generally used to secure a diving cylinder to a backplate, stabilisor jacket BCD or other form of diving harness.
"
"camel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lifting_bag#Closed_lift_bags_(camels)"" title=""Lifting bag"">Lifting bag#Closed lift bags (camels)</a></span></p> 
A closed lifting bag, for use at or near the surface, which retains air in rough conditions.
"
"canister light (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_light#Canister_light"" title=""Dive light"">Dive light#Canister light</a></span></p> 
Dive light comprising a <span title=""See entry on this page at § light head"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#light_head"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">light head</a></span> connected to a battery canister by a cable.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_26-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
"
"canoe diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canoe_diving"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Canoe diving"">Canoe diving</a></span></p>
Scuba diving from canoes, used when the dive site is beyond convenient swimming distances.
"
"carbon dioxide poisoning (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_poisoning"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Carbon dioxide poisoning"">Carbon dioxide poisoning</a></span></p>
The toxic effects of carbon dioxide, due to incomplete elimination of carbon dioxide resulting from skip breathing, excessive work of breathing, scrubber failure in a rebreather system, or inadequate ventilation in a diving chamber or free flow helmet. Occasionally caused by contaminated gas supply.
"
"carbon monoxide poisoning (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_monoxide_poisoning"" title=""Carbon monoxide poisoning"">Carbon monoxide poisoning</a></span></p>
The toxic effects of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_monoxide"" title=""Carbon monoxide"">carbon monoxide</a> , usually due to contaminated breathing gas supply.
"
"cardio-pulmonary resuscitation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article:— <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardio-pulmonary_resuscitation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cardio-pulmonary resuscitation"">Cardio-pulmonary resuscitation</a></span></p>
An emergency procedure which is performed in an effort to manually preserve intact brain function until further measures are taken to restore spontaneous blood circulation and breathing in a person in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardiac_arrest"" title=""Cardiac arrest"">cardiac arrest</a>
"
"CAS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#critical_air_supply""><span title=""See entry on this page at § critical air supply"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">critical air supply</span></a></span></p>"
"cascade filling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascade_storage_system"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cascade storage system"">Cascade storage system</a></span></p>
Decanting from several storage cylinders in succession, generally using a procedure to maximise charge pressures. Often used in partial pressure <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_blending"" title=""Gas blending"">gas blending</a>.
"
"catenary anchor leg mooring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: CALM</span></p> 
Single point mooring type named for the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catenary"" title=""Catenary"">catenary</a> curve of the anchor cables that hold the buoy in position. Also referred to as single buoy mooring, monobuoy or loading buoy.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"caustic cocktail (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather_diving#Scrubber_failure"" title=""Rebreather diving"">Rebreather diving#Scrubber failure</a></span></p> 
A mixture of water and carbon dioxide absorbent caused by flooding the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_scrubber"" title=""Carbon dioxide scrubber"">scrubber</a> of a diving rebreather, and which may reach the diver's mouth through the breathing loop. The alkalinity depends on the absorbent used, and may injure the diver if aspirated.
"
"cave (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave"" title=""Cave"">Cave</a></span></p> 
A naturally occurring cavity in bedrock, or an underwater passage not illuminated by natural daylight, large enough to be entered by a human. Statute 810.13 of the Florida legislature defines a cave as: <i>any void, cavity, recess, or system of interconnecting passages which naturally occurs beneath the surface of the earth or within a cliff or ledge, including natural subsurface water and drainage systems but not including any mine, tunnel, aqueduct, or other manmade excavation, and which is large enough to permit a person to enter. The word ""cave"" includes any cavern, natural pit, or sinkhole which is an extension of an entrance to a cave</i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-15"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"cave arrow (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Line_marker"" title=""Line marker"">Line marker</a></span></p>
Directional line markers which point the way to an exit.
"
"cave fill (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Filling a scuba cylinder to a pressure significantly above the rated safe working pressure (charging pressure).<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-16"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Illegal in some jurisdictions, and increases risk of catastrophic failure.
"
"cave line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Application: A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distance_line"" title=""Distance line"">distance line</a> laid in a cave for navigation.
2.&#160;&#160;Material: Small diameter braided synthetic cordage used for distance lines in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_diving"" title=""Cave diving"">cave diving</a> .
"
"cave reel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distance_line"" title=""Distance line"">Distance line</a></span></p>
A reel specifically made for cave diving, used to lay and recover large lengths of cave line which is used as a temporary guide line to find the exit or a permanent guide line.
"
"cavern (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Two or more interconnected underground rooms or passages in bedrock, each large enough to be entered by a human.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-17"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;The initial space in an underwater cave system that is illuminated by natural daylight.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-18"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
3.&#160;&#160;A naturally occurring cavity in bedrock or an underwater passage, large enough to be entered by a human, which is illuminated by natural daylight, or in which it is possible from all points to see the exit by natural daylight.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-19"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"cavern dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Defined as a penetration dive under rock where visibility is greater than 40 feet, maximum penetration does not exceed 130 feet, maximum depth does not exceed 70 feet, the diver is always within the area illuminated by ambient sunlight, and does not pass through any <span title=""See entry on this page at § restriction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#restriction"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">restrictions</a></span>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-20"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"C-card (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#certification_card""><span title=""See entry on this page at § certification card"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">certification card</span></a></span></p>"
"CCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#closed_circuit_rebreather""><span title=""See entry on this page at § closed circuit rebreather"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">closed circuit rebreather</span></a></span></p>"
"CCUBA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#closed_circuit_underwater_breathing_apparatus""><span title=""See entry on this page at § closed circuit underwater breathing apparatus"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">closed circuit underwater breathing apparatus</span></a></span></p>"
"ceiling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Solid overhead or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_(diving)"" title=""Decompression (diving)"">decompression</a> restriction to a safe direct vertical ascent to the surface
"
"cenote (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cenote"" title=""Cenote"">Cenote</a></span></p>
A sinkhole in Mexico. Generally with vertical or overhanging walls or shafts with water that open into a cave system.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-21"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"certification card (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A plastic card issued to a diver by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_certification_agency"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diver certification agency"">diver certification agency</a> as evidence of having completed the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_training"" title=""Diver training"">diver training</a> and experience required for the level of certification.
"
"CF (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#clusterfuck""><span title=""See entry on this page at § clusterfuck"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">clusterfuck</span></a></span></p>"
"CGA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#compressed_Gas_Association""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Compressed Gas Association"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Compressed Gas Association</span></a></span></p>"
"CGA 850 (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Compressed Gas Association valve standard CGA 850 is the standard for the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve"" title=""Scuba cylinder valve"">scuba cylinder valve</a> outlet for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoke_connector"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Yoke connector"">yoke connectors</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-HCG_30-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-HCG-30"">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
"
"chain chaser (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Ring or hook shaped components used for installing and recovering conventional mooring systems. The chaser is hooked around the chain and pulled in the direction of the anchor until it slides onto the anchor shank and is stopped by the crown. The chaser is then used to break the anchor out by pulling directly upwards.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"chamber dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Simulated dive in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperbaric_chamber"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hyperbaric chamber"">hyperbaric chamber</a> pressurised to equivalent pressure to the nominal depth of the dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2001_27-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2001-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
"
"chamber operator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Person competent to operate a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_chamber"" title=""Diving chamber"">diving chamber</a><sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_11-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
"
"channeling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"channelling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Formation of void spaces in the granular absorbent in a scrubber which allow gas to bypass close contact with the absorbent material, allowing carbon dioxide to pass through the scrubber.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_28-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"charging pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § working pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#working_pressure"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">working pressure</a></span></span></p> 
Pressure stamped on a container for a permanent gas to indicate the maximum gauge pressure measured at, or corrected to the <span title=""See entry on this page at § reference temperature"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#reference_temperature"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">reference temperature</a></span> (usually 15°C or 20°C) that may be applied at the time of filling.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_31-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-31"">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Charles's law (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles%27s_law"" title=""Charles&#39;s law"">Charles's law</a></span></p>
Relation of volume to temperature at constant pressure of an ideal gas.
"
"charlie foxtrot (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#clusterfuck""><span title=""See entry on this page at § clusterfuck"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">clusterfuck</span></a></span></p>"
"checkout dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"check-out dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A dive done to establish whether a diver's skills are current and responses appropriate and timely, equipment is configured and working correctly, or that team procedures are mutually understood and work as planned.
"
"chicken vest (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Sleeveless neoprene <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wetsuit"" title=""Wetsuit"">wetsuit</a> vest with attached hood.<sup id=""cite_ref-Chicken_vest_32-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Chicken_vest-32"">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-gwi_33-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-gwi-33"">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
"
"chimney (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A section of a cave that is vertical or near vertical and like a shaft.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-22"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Chinese lantern (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Connection between pipeline end manifold (PLEM) and single point mooring buoy (SPM) using two to four separate curved, flexible, underwater hose strings.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"choked flow (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#constant_mass_flow""><span title=""See entry on this page at § constant mass flow"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">constant mass flow</span></a></span></p>"
"choker (sidemount) (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Cylinders"" title=""Sidemount diving"">Sidemount diving#Cylinders</a></span></p>
A strap around the neck of a sidemount cylinder used to hold the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolt_snap"" title=""Bolt snap"">bolt snap</a> closer to the neck so that the head of the cylinder stays closer to the diver's armpit. The choker can be a small webbing strap with a sliding buckle for adjustment, so it can be tightened to bring the clip closer to the neck or slacked off while in use.
"
"chokes (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness#Classification"" title=""Decompression sickness"">Decompression sickness#Classification</a></span></p>
A symptom of decompression sickness manifested by shortness of breath, caused by a large number of venous gas bubbles in the lung capillaries which interfere with gas exchange.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_26-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Christmas tree (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""tree""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christmas_tree_(oil_well)"" title=""Christmas tree (oil well)"">Christmas tree (oil well)</a></span></p>
An assembly of valves, spools, and fittings installed on top of the wellhead and used primarily to control the flow, usually oil or gas, out of the well.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Christmas tree ladder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A boarding <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ladder"" title=""Ladder"">ladder</a> which has a single central rail with rigid <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cantilever"" title=""Cantilever"">cantilevered</a> rungs to each side, allowing use while wearing <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swimfins"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Swimfins"">swimfins</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-ladders_34-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ladders-34"">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Christo-lube (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Usually Christo-lube MCG111, an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility"" title=""Oxygen compatibility"">oxygen compatible</a> lubricant suitable for use in breathing apparatus in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_service"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Oxygen service"">oxygen service</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-23"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>"
"circuit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Cave dive route in which there is a one-way segment. The circuit can be simple or complex depending on the number of jumps involved.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-24"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"civils (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § inshore diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#inshore_diving"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">inshore diving</a></span></span></p>"
"closed bell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""dry bell""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell#Structure_of_a_typical_closed_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">Diving bell#Structure of a typical closed bell</a></span></p>
A closed or dry bell is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure_vessel_for_human_occupancy"" title=""Pressure vessel for human occupancy"">pressure vessel for human occupancy</a> which is lowered into the sea to the workplace, equalised in pressure to the environment, and opened to allow the divers in and out. Divers may be <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_(diving)"" title=""Decompression (diving)"">decompressed</a> in the bell or <a href=""#transfer_under_pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § transfer under pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">transferred under pressure</span></a> to a hyperbaric chamber at the surface.
"
"closed circuit rebreather (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"closed-circuit rebreather (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather_diving#Closed_circuit_rebreather"" title=""Rebreather diving"">Rebreather diving#Closed circuit rebreather</a></span></p>
Underwater breathing apparatus in which exhaled gas is scrubbed to remove carbon dioxide, and the oxygen is replenished to maintain a specific partial pressure, before returning it to the diver as breathing gas. <i>See also</i> <span title=""See entry on this page at § ECCR"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#ECCR"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">ECCR</a></span> and <span title=""See entry on this page at § MCCR"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#MCCR"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">MCCR</a></span>.
"
"closed circuit underwater breathing apparatus (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Military alternative term for <a href=""#closed_circuit_rebreather""><span title=""See entry on this page at § closed circuit rebreather"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">closed circuit rebreather</span></a>.
"
"clump weight (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A weight used to keep the guide wires of a diving bell aligned and tensioned.
"
"clusterfuck (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""CF"", ""charlie foxtrot""</span></p>
Occasion when the situation diverges notably and usually uncontrollably from the plan, sometimes involving immediate hazard to life and limb, and often involving poor judgement.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_26-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>"
"cobra guard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § rams head"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#rams_head"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">rams head</a></span></span></p>"
"code of practice (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A systematic set of professional standards or written guidelines and rules of procedures to be followed by members of a profession, trade, occupation or organization. A code of practice may be compiled and agreed on by members of a particular profession or written guidelines issued by an official body or a professional association to its members to help them comply with its ethical standards. A code of practice does not normally have the force of law, but is often required or compulsory practice for members of an organisation.
"
"coded welder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Welder who is trained and qualified and assessed as competent for a specified type of welding under specified conditions.
"
"combat swimmer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combat_swimmer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Combat swimmer"">Combat swimmer</a></span></p>
Person trained in scuba diving or swimming underwater in a military capacity which can include combat
"
"command signal (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_communications#Hand_signals"" title=""Diver communications"">signal</a> from a diver in a team that requires a response from the other diver. There are three: ""Are you OK"", ""Hold"", and ""Surface"" (terminate the dive).<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-25"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"commercial diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_diving"" title=""Commercial diving"">Commercial diving</a></span></p>
Working under pressure: Occupational activity where gas is breathed while immersed at pressure in excess of atmospheric pressure, usually underwater.
"
"completion (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Completion_(oil_and_gas_wells)"" title=""Completion (oil and gas wells)"">Completion (oil and gas wells)</a></span></p>
The process of making a well, that has been drilled, ready for production.
"
"competent person (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Person who is able to perform a task or operation safely and according to required procedures. Recognition of competence may require formal assessment or accreditation, or registration with government body.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_31-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-31"">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
"
"compressed air (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Air at a pressure greater than ambient.
"
"Compressed Gas Association (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compressed_Gas_Association"" title=""Compressed Gas Association"">Compressed Gas Association</a></span></p>
An American <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_association"" title=""Trade association"">trade association</a> for the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_gas"" title=""Industrial gas"">industrial</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medical_gas_supply"" title=""Medical gas supply"">medical gas supply</a> industries.<sup id=""cite_ref-35"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-35"">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The CGA publishes standards and practices that codify industry practices.  In cases where government regulation is not specific, CGA documents are considered authoritative. CGA V-1 Standard for Compressed Gas Cylinder Valve Outlet and Inlet Connections covers <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder"" title=""Diving cylinder"">diving cylinder</a> valve outlets.<sup id=""cite_ref-CPC_Int_36-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-CPC_Int-36"">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Safety devices like <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burst_disk"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Burst disk"">burst disk</a> overpressure protection are specified by the CGA Standard S1.1.
"
"compressed neoprene (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Foam neoprene that has been compressed to reduce volume. Used for dry suits and hot water suits which are less affected by depth induced buoyancy changes.
"
"compression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The process of increasing the ambient pressure on a diver by descending into the water or pressurising the chamber.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_20-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
"
"compression arthralgia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compression_arthralgia"" title=""Compression arthralgia"">Compression arthralgia</a></span></p>
Pain in the joints caused by exposure to high ambient pressure at a relatively high rate of compression
"
"compressor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compressor"" title=""Compressor"">Compressor</a></span></p>
Machine which pressurises gas. Generally intake gas is at ambient pressure, outlet gas at higher pressure. High pressure breathing air compressor output pressure is usually 200 to 330 bar. Machines which compress gas at higher intake pressures are called <a href=""#booster""><span title=""See entry on this page at § booster"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">boosters</span></a>
"
"compressor log (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Book or file containing records of compressor operation, filling of cylinders and maintenance records.
"
"compressor operator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Person who operates a compressor, either to fill cylinders, or to provide breathing air to surface supplied divers.
"
"condensate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Condensation"" title=""Condensation"">Condensation</a></span></p>
Liquid resulting from phase change from gas due to cooling, pressure increase, or both.
"
"conduit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Tunnel or passage in a cave system.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-26"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"confined water (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Water that is enclosed and bounded sufficiently for safe training purposes. Generally implies that conditions are not affected by geographic or weather conditions, and that divers cannot get lost.<sup id=""cite_ref-Class_IV_37-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Class_IV-37"">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
"
"conservative (decompression) (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism_(diving)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Conservatism (diving)"">Conservatism (diving)</a></span></p>
Decompression profile tending to minimise risk of decompression sickness at the cost of more decompression time for a given pre-ascent dive profile.<sup id=""cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_6-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"constant depth blackout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"constant pressure blackout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""isobaric blackout""</span></p>
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freediving_blackout"" title=""Freediving blackout"">Freediving blackout</a> which occurs while the diver maintains a near constant shallow depth, where reduction of oxygen partial pressure due to ascent is not a factor. Usually induced by pre-dive hyperventilation. Also referred to as <span title=""See entry on this page at § shallow water blackout"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#shallow_water_blackout"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">shallow water blackout</a></span>, which is an ambiguous term
"
"constant mass flow (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""choked flow""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choked_flow"" title=""Choked flow"">Choked flow</a></span></p>
Sonic flow through an orifice – the maximum possible flow rate for the gas through the orifice for a given absolute upstream pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_28-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"constant volume dry suit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Dry suit with an <a href=""#automatic_dump_valve""><span title=""See entry on this page at § automatic dump valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">automatic dump valve</span></a>.
"
"constriction (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § restriction"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#restriction"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">restriction</a></span></span></p>"
"containment grip (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § whip sock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#whip_sock"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">whip sock</a></span></span></p>"
"contents gauge (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § submersible pressure gauge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#submersible_pressure_gauge"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">submersible pressure gauge</a></span></span></p>"
"continuous decompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Continuous_decompression"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Continuous decompression</a></span></p>
Decompression without stops. Instead of a fairly rapid ascent rate to the first stop, followed by a period at static depth during the stop, the ascent is slower, but without officially stopping. Ascent rate may vary with depth, usually slowing as the depth reduces.
"
"contra-indications to diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Conditions (usually medical) that indicate that a person should not dive.
"
"control compartment (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Tissue_compartment"" title=""Decompression theory"">tissue compartment</a> that dictates the ascent profile of a given dive because it is theoretically the highest risk compartment for DCS.<sup id=""cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_6-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"controlled buoyant lift (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Controlled_buoyant_lift"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Controlled buoyant lift"">Controlled buoyant lift</a></span></p>
A rescue technique used by scuba divers to raise an incapacitated diver to the surface from depth.
"
"controlled emergency swimming ascent (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""CESA""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Controlled_emergency_swimming_ascent"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Controlled emergency swimming ascent"">Controlled emergency swimming ascent</a></span></p>
An emergency technique for surfacing, usually when no breathable gas is available at depth. The diver fins upward while gently exhaling to keep expanding air in the lungs from causing lung expansion injuries.<sup id=""cite_ref-Scuba_travel_38-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Scuba_travel-38"">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
"
"cookie (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Line_marker"" title=""Line marker"">Line marker</a></span></p>
Personal non-directional line markers that mark specific locations, or the direction of one's own exit at line intersections.
"
"copper hat (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"copper helmet (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_diving_dress"" title=""Standard diving dress"">Standard diving dress</a></span></p>
A diving helmet of traditional design and construction, usually made from spun or beaten copper, with brass or bronze fittings. There are usually two main sub-assemblies; the bonnet is the roughly spherical part which covers the head and is provided with viewports, valves and various other fittings, and the corselet, which rests on the upper torso of the diver, and to which the bonnet is connected when in use, and which may be sealed to the suit and ballasted to compensate for the buoyancy of the airspace inside the helmet.
"
"corselet (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""breastplate""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_diving_dress#General_description"" title=""Standard diving dress"">Standard diving dress#General description</a></span></p>
Lower part of a standard copper helmet and some other heavy helmets, which clamps to the diving suit, rests on the diver's shoulders, and to which the helmet upper part, or <a href=""#bonnet""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bonnet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bonnet</span></a>, is clamped, screwed or bolted.
"
"counterlung (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Counterlungs"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Counterlungs</a></span></p>
Flexible bag or bellows in a rebreather which compensates for the changes in volume of gas in the loop during the breathing cycle.
"
"CPR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#cardio-pulmonary_resuscitation""><span title=""See entry on this page at § cardio-pulmonary resuscitation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">cardio-pulmonary resuscitation</span></a></span></p> "
"cracking pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Pressure required to open a spring-loaded valve. Often applied to the difference in pressure over the diaphragm of a demand valve required to open the valve to start flow. This may differ significantly from the pressure difference required to keep the valve open once flow has been initiated, and the pressure required to keep the valve open may vary with flow rate.
"
"critical air supply (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Critical_pressures"" title=""Scuba gas planning"">critical pressure</a></span></p>
The amount of breathing air required to safely exit a penetration dive. When the available air supply reaches the calculated critical pressure the dive has reached a planned turning point.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-27"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"critical difference hypothesis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Critical_difference_hypothesis"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Critical difference hypothesis</a></span></p>
Hypothesis that bubble formation during decompression will not occur if a critical pressure difference between tissue inert gas tension and ambient pressure is not exceeded.
"
"critical flicker-fusion frequency (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: CFFF</span></p>
The frequency at which a flickering light is perceived as continuous, a measurement used to evaluate visual temporal processing as an indicator of alertness and arousal in humans, including use as an experimental indicator of inert gas narcosis in divers, using a simple uncomplicated, non-invasive and objective methodology.<sup id=""cite_ref-39"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-39"">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
"
"critical pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Critical_pressures"" title=""Scuba gas planning"">Scuba gas planning#Critical pressures</a></span></p>
Cylinder gas pressure which determines a safe limit to an underwater activity on scuba, such as start of ascent or turnaround during a penetration.
"
"critical ratio hypothesis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Critical_ratio_hypothesis"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Critical ratio hypothesis</a></span></p>
Hypothesis that bubble formation during decompression will not occur if a critical ratio of tissue inert gas tension and ambient pressure is not exceeded.
"
"critical volume hypothesis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#The_critical_volume_approach"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#The critical volume approach</a></span></p>
Hypothesis that symptoms of decompression sickness will not be evident if a critical volume of tissue gas bubbles is not exceeded.
"
"crotch strap (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
