<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backplate_and_wing#Harness"" title=""Backplate and wing"">Harness</a> strap that passes from the lower part of the harness at the back, through between the diver's legs, to the waistbelt in front of the harness, effectively securing the harness from sliding up along the torso. In <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_diving#Bell_harness"" title=""Commercial diving"">commercial diving safety harness</a> this is often in two parallel parts and allows the diver to be lifted by the harness without risk of falling out.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-28"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"crushed neoprene (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Proprietary material for dry suits manufactured by DUI in a process where the foam neoprene suit material is degassed by exposure to high hydrostatic pressure to reduce the volume after assembly. There is less buoyancy variation with depth as the material is less compressible after the treatment.<sup id=""cite_ref-Barsky_Long_and_Stinton_2006_40-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Barsky_Long_and_Stinton_2006-40"">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>"
"cuff dump (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A spring loaded over-pressure <span title=""See entry on this page at § dump valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#dump_valve"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">dump valve</a></span> mounted on a dry suit sleeve near the cuff, usually relatively small and non-adjustable, which dumps excess gas from the suit if it is raised sufficiently.
"
"current limited (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electro-galvanic_oxygen_sensor#Failure_modes"" title=""Electro-galvanic oxygen sensor"">Electro-galvanic oxygen sensor#Failure modes</a></span></p>
Common failure mode of an oxygen sensor cell in which an increase of oxygen partial pressure above the limiting level does not produce an increase in output current. Such a failure would prevent the control system from recognising an excessive partial pressure of oxygen.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_28-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"current shear (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
Variation in flow velocity along an axis othogonal to the direction of flow. Current shear may be vertical, where shallow water flows at a different velocity to deeper water, horizontal, where flow velocity varies across the width of the current, or mixed. Wind induced current displays vertical shear and directional variation with depth in an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ekman_spiral"" title=""Ekman spiral"">Ekman spiral</a>.
"
"cyalume (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diphenyl_oxalate"" title=""Diphenyl oxalate"">Diphenyl oxalate</a></span></p>
Trademark name Cyalume is a solid ester whose oxidation products are responsible for the chemiluminescence in a glowstick.
"
"cyanosis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyanosis"" title=""Cyanosis"">Cyanosis</a></span></p>
The appearance of a blue or purple coloration of the skin or mucous membranes due to the tissues near the skin surface being low on oxygen.
"
"cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder</a>: Refillable compressed gas container of water capacity between 0,5 L and 150 L used to supply gas for underwater diving.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_31-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-31"">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;That part of a reciprocating compressor or booster in which the piston is moved to compress the gas. The internal space is cylindrical with a circular section. The external surface is usually finned for air cooling.
"
"cylinder boot (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Cylinder_boot"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Cylinder boot</a></span></p>
Rubber or plastic cover for the base of a scuba cylinder to protect it from abrasion, and in the case of domed end cylinders, to allow it to stand upright.
"
"cylinder bundle (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#bundle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § bundle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">bundle</span></a></span></p>"
"cylinder neck (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Cylinder_neck"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Cylinder neck</a></span></p>
The part of the cylinder end which is shaped as a narrow concentric cylinder, and internally threaded to fit a cylinder valve.
"
"cylinder shoulder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#The_pressure_vessel"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#The pressure vessel</a></span></p>
The domed top of the cylinder between the parallel section and the neck with the cylinder valve.
"
"cylinder valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#The_cylinder_valve"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#The cylinder valve</a></span></p>
Valve fitted to a compressed gas cylinder to control gas flow into and out of the cylinder. Also <b>pillar valve</b>.
"
"Dalton's law (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><style data-mw-deduplicate=""TemplateStyles:r1033289096"">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalton%27s_law"" title=""Dalton&#39;s law"">Dalton's law</a></span></p>
Gas law describing the relation of component pressures of gases in a mixture to the total pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DAN (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#divers_Alert_Network""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Divers Alert Network"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Divers Alert Network</span></a></span></p>"
"dangly (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
(Derogatory) Any part of a diver's equipment that dangles in a position that might impact the bottom or get caught on the surroundings.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DCAP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Decompression Computation and Analysis Program: Decompression planning software by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_William_Hamilton_Jr."" title=""Robert William Hamilton Jr."">Bill Hamilton</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dcCCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"DCCCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""manual CCR"" (mCCR)</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_rebreather#Control_of_the_breathing_gas_mix"" title=""Diving rebreather"">Diving rebreather#Control of the breathing gas mix</a></span></p>
Diver-controlled closed-circuit rebreather. A closed circuit rebreather which requires the diver to monitor oxygen levels and manually inject oxygen or diluent as needed to maintain an appropriate partial pressure in the loop.
"
"DCIEM (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DRDC_Toronto"" title=""DRDC Toronto"">DRDC Toronto</a></span></p>
Defence and Civil Institute of Environmental Medicine (Toronto, Canada).
"
"DCIEM tables (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_decompression_research_and_development#DCIEM_model_and_tables"" title=""History of decompression research and development"">History of decompression research and development#DCIEM model and tables</a></span></p>
Decompression tables based on the Kidd-Stubbs model, developed and published by the Defence and Civil Institute of Environmental Medicine.
"
"DCI (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#decompression_illness""><span title=""See entry on this page at § decompression illness"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">decompression illness</span></a></span></p>"
"DCS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#decompression_sickness""><span title=""See entry on this page at § decompression sickness"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">decompression sickness</span></a></span></p>"
"DDC (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#deck_decompression_chamber""><span title=""See entry on this page at § deck decompression chamber"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">deck decompression chamber</span></a></span></p>"
"dead man anchor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lifting_bag#Breakout"" title=""Lifting bag"">Lifting bag#Breakout</a></span></p>
A heavy weight used to control the rise of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lifting_bag"" title=""Lifting bag"">lifting bag</a> after <span title=""See entry on this page at § breakout"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#breakout"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">breakout</a></span>, or to capsize it to prevent a runaway lift
"
"dead space (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"dead volume (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dead_space_(physiology)"" title=""Dead space (physiology)"">Dead space (physiology)</a></span></p>
1.&#160;&#160;The volume of a breathing apparatus which holds exhaled air, which is subsequently inhaled directly. without passing through a scrubber to remove carbon dioxide and without oxygen addition.
2.&#160;&#160;The volume of inhaled air, which does not take part in gas exchange either because it remains in the conducting airways or in alveoli that are poorly perfused.
"
"decant (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascade_filling_system"" title=""Cascade filling system"">Cascade filling system</a></span></p>
To transfer gas between cylinders by differential pressure. No energy is input, flow will stop when pressures are equalised.
"
"deck decompression chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deck_decompression_chamber"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Deck decompression chamber"">Deck decompression chamber</a></span></p>
A twin-lock <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperbaric_chamber"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hyperbaric chamber"">hyperbaric chamber</a> suitable for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface_decompression"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Surface decompression"">surface decompression</a> and emergency recompression. Large enough to hold at least two occupants, one of them lying down.
"
"decompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_(diving)"" title=""Decompression (diving)"">Decompression (diving)</a></span></p>
Reduction in ambient pressure experienced by the diver during the ascent at the end of a dive or hyperbaric exposure, and the process of allowing dissolved inert gases to be eliminated from the body tissues during this reduction in pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"decompression algorithm (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Decompression_algorithms"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Decompression algorithms</a></span></p>
Specified step-by step procedures used to calculate the decompression stops needed for a given dive profile. The algorithm can be used to generate decompression schedules for a particular dive profile, decompression tables for more general use, or be implemented in dive computer software to perform real-time analysis of decompression status of the diver.
"
"decompression bar (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#decompression_trapeze""><span title=""See entry on this page at § decompression trapeze"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">decompression trapeze</span></a></span></p>"
"decompression buoy (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#dSMB""><span title=""See entry on this page at § DSMB"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">DSMB</span></a></span></p>"
"decompression chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_chamber#Decompression_chamber"" title=""Diving chamber"">Diving chamber#Decompression chamber</a></span></p>
Hyperbaric chamber used for decompressing divers and emergency <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Therapeutic_recompression"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Therapeutic recompression"">therapeutic recompression</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_3-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"decompression computer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#dive_computer""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dive computer"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dive computer</span></a></span></p>"
"decompression gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Accelerated_decompression"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Accelerated decompression</a></span></p>
Gas breathed during decompression. Commonly implies a composition chosen to accelerate decompression by using an increased oxygen content.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_3-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"decompression illness (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_illness"" title=""Decompression illness"">Decompression illness</a></span></p>
Illness caused by decompression. Includes <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arterial_gas_embolism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Arterial gas embolism"">arterial gas embolism</a> due to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lung_overexpansion_injury"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Lung overexpansion injury"">lung overexpansion injury</a>.
"
"decompression obligation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Decompression"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Decompression</a></span></p>
Calculated theoretical requirement to make decompression stops during ascent based on the dive profile, breathing gases, and the decompression model in use.
"
"decompression schedule (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Decompression_schedule"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Decompression schedule</a></span></p>
A specific ascent rate and series of increasingly shallower decompression stops that a diver uses to allow inert gases to be eliminated from the body tissues during ascent after a specific hyperbaric exposure, to reduce the risk of decompression sickness.
"
"decompression sickness (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">Decompression sickness</a></span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""the bends"", ""caisson disease"", ""DCS"", or ""divers' disease""</span></p>
A condition arising from dissolved inert gases coming out of solution during decompression as bubbles in the tissues, organs and blood vessels of the body causing symptoms ranging from rashes to death.
"
"decompression status (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Theoretical tissue inert gas loading after a given dive history according to the chosen decompression model. It is a measure of whether, and how much, decompression is recommended by the algorithm.
"
"decompression stop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Decompression_stops"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Decompression stops</a></span></p>
A pause during the ascent phase of a dive that a diver spends at a constant relatively shallow depth to allow safe release of inert gases from the body tissues to avoid <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_3-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"decompression stress (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
An indicator of risk for decompression sickness associated with the excess (supersaturation) of inert gas dissolved in the various tissues throughout the body, driving bubble formation and growth.
"
"decompression tables (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Decompression_tables"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Decompression tables</a></span></p>
Printed cards or booklets that allow divers to determine a decompression schedule for a particular dive profile and breathing gas.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_3-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"decompression trapeze (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""decompression bar""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Decompression_trapezes"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Decompression trapezes</a></span></p>
A horizontal bar or bars suspended at the depth of intended decompression stops by buoys, used to make decompression stops more comfortable and more secure and provide the divers' surface cover with a visual reference for the divers' position.
"
"deep-sea diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"deep sea diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A term originally referring to diving with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_diving_dress"" title=""Standard diving dress"">standard diving dress</a>, where the helmet is sealed to the watertight diving suit, as contrasted with a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shallow-water_diving_helmet"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Shallow-water diving helmet"">shallow-water diving helmet</a>, which is open at the bottom and was used for work in shallow water where the diver could ditch the helmet and make a free ascent in an emergency. Several incompatible definitions or usages have been published, including diving in the deeper parts of the ocean, but the only technology that can withstand those pressures is specialised submersibles.
"
"deep stops (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Thermodynamic_model_and_deep_stops"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Thermodynamic model and deep stops</a></span></p>
Decompression stops which are deeper than the deepest stops required by decompression algorithms using dissolved phase models.
"
"deep water blackout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Freediving: An ambiguous alternative term for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freediving_blackout#Ascent_blackout"" title=""Freediving blackout"">blackout of ascent</a> following a deep breath-hold dive, in which loss of consciousness occurs as the surface is approached, or at the surface, caused by cerebral hypoxia arising from the rapid drop in the partial pressure of oxygen in the lungs during ascent as the ambient pressure drops and the gas in the lungs expands to surface volume.<sup id=""cite_ref-Lindholm_2006_4-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Lindholm_2006-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;Scuba and surface-supplied diving: Loss of consciousness in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_diving#Ultra_deep_air"" title=""Deep diving"">deep air diving</a> at depths below 50&#160;m with no clear primary cause, associated with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis"" title=""Nitrogen narcosis"">nitrogen narcosis</a>, a neurological impairment with anaesthetic effects caused by high partial pressure of nitrogen dissolved in nerve tissue, and possibly acute <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_toxicity"" title=""Oxygen toxicity"">oxygen toxicity</a>. The term is not in widespread use at present.<sup id=""cite_ref-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dehydration (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dehydration"" title=""Dehydration"">Dehydration</a></span></p>
A condition where the water content of the body is reduced.
"
"delta P (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"ΔP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"δp (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Environments where a pressure difference causes flow. Usually refers to cases where the flow is likely to entrain and pull the diver into an enclosed space or through an opening.
"
"demand helmet (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See; <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Lightweight_demand_helmets"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">Surface-supplied diving#Lightweight demand helmets</a></span></p>
Diving helmet which provides breathing gas supply flow only when the diver inhales, triggered by the pressure drop.
"
"demand valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#Demand_valve"" title=""Diving regulator"">Diving regulator#Demand valve</a></span></p>
Mechanism for providing the user with breathing gas flow only when required. The valve may be triggered by a reduction of pressure across the actuator diaphragm to below ambient due to inhalation, or by pressing a manual override (Purge button).
"
"depth gauge (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depth_gauge"" title=""Depth gauge"">Depth gauge</a></span></p>
A pressure gauge calibrated to measure depth as a function of ambient pressure.
"
"descending line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § jackstay"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#jackstay"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">jackstay</a></span>, <a href=""#downline""><span title=""See entry on this page at § downline"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">downline</span></a> and <span title=""See entry on this page at § shotline"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#shotline"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">shotline</a></span></span></p>
A substantial heavily weighted line attached to a secure point at the surface, such as a boat or buoy, which can be used by a diver to control position and depth during descent an ascent.<sup id=""cite_ref-USN_training_6-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USN_training-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"developed pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Developed_pressure"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Developed pressure</a></span></p>
The pressure of the compressed gas in a cylinder at a temperature other than the nominal temperature at which charging pressure is specified. Usually refers to pressure when fully charged at a variation from the reference temperature.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DGPS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_Global_Positioning_System"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Differential Global Positioning System"">Differential Global Positioning System</a></span></p>
An enhancement to Global Positioning System that provides improved location accuracy. DGPS uses a network of fixed, ground-based reference stations to broadcast the difference between the positions indicated by the satellite systems and the known fixed positions."
"Diamond Reef System (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diamond_Reef_System"" title=""Diamond Reef System"">Diamond Reef System</a></span></p>
A diving skills program that uses a set of standardized portable obstacles to train and evaluate buoyancy skills and educate scuba divers on how to interact with coral reefs.
"
"differential pressure hazard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"delta P hazard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Situation where water flows from a region of higher pressure to one of lower pressure, and where obstructing the flow will induce a large force on the obstruction. A type of diving hazard.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diffusion limited (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Diffusion_limited_tissues_and_the_&quot;Tissue_slab&quot;,_and_series_models"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Diffusion limited tissues and the ""Tissue slab"", and series models</a></span></p>
Decompression hypothesis that the uptake and elimination of inert gas is limited by diffusion rates in the tissues. Compare with <span title=""See entry on this page at § perfusion limited"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#perfusion_limited"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">perfusion limited</a></span>.
"
"diluent (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""dil""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Gas_sources"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Gas sources</a></span></p>
Gas mixture used to dilute the oxygen in the loop of a closed circuit rebreather to a partial pressure suited to the depth.
"
"diluent flush (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""flush"", ""dil flush"", ""loop flush""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather_diving#Diluent_flush"" title=""Rebreather diving"">Rebreather diving#Diluent flush</a></span></p> 
Replacing the gas within the breathing loop of a rebreather by injecting diluent gas while venting the previous gas mix. Usually done to get a breathable mixture of known composition in the loop to check calibration of the oxygen cells.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_9-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DIN fitting (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""DIN valve"", ""DIN regulator"", ""DIN thread""</span></p>
Usually refers to G5/8"" x 14 tpi<sup id=""cite_ref-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-10"">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> parallel <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Screw_thread"" title=""Screw thread"">thread</a> fittings used to connect a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Connection_to_the_regulator"" title=""Diving cylinder"">cylinder valve</a> to a filling connection or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#First_stage"" title=""Diving regulator"">regulator first stage</a>. Available in 200 bar and 300 bar versions which should only be inter-connectable in safe combinations. 232 bar DIN (5-thread, G5/8) Outlet/Connector #13 to DIN 477 part 1, and 300 bar DIN (7-thread, G5/8) Outlet/Connector #56 to DIN 477 part 5 - these are similar to 5-thread DIN fitting but are rated to 300 bar working pressures. The 300 bar pressures are common in European diving and in US cave diving.<sup id=""cite_ref-Scuba_Doctor_11-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Scuba_Doctor-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DIN plug (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Connection_to_the_regulator"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Connection to the regulator</a></span></p>
Screw in adaptor which can be used with many recent 200/240 bar <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsches_Institut_f%C3%BCr_Normung"" title=""Deutsches Institut für Normung"">DIN</a> cylinder valves to allow connection of Yoke regulators or filling whips.
"
"DIR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#doing_It_Right""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Doing It Right"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Doing It Right</span></a></span></p>"
"direct ascent (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Uninterrupted vertical ascent to the water's surface without decompression stops, usually also without a safety stop
"
"display integrated vibratory alarm (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""DIVA""</span></p>
Display integrated vibrating alarm – A <span title=""See entry on this page at § head-up display"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#head-up_display"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">head-up display</a></span> module which produces a warning vibration to draw the attention of the diver, generally mounted on the diver's mask or the rebreather mouthpiece.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_9-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
"
"distance line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""penetration line"" or ""guideline""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distance_line"" title=""Distance line"">Distance line</a></span></p>
A line used by scuba divers as a means of returning to a safe starting point in conditions of low visibility, water currents or where pilotage is difficult.
"
"DIVA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#display_integrated_vibratory_alarm""><span title=""See entry on this page at § display integrated vibratory alarm"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">display integrated vibratory alarm</span></a></span></p>"
"dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
(legal) A human activity in which a person enters water or any other liquid, or a chamber in which they are subject to a pressure greater than 100 millibars above atmospheric pressure and, while in such an environment, they breathe air or other gas at a pressure greater than atmospheric pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2009_12-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2009-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dive computer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""decompression computer""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_computer"" title=""Dive computer"">Dive computer</a></span></p>
A device used by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_diving"" title=""Scuba diving"">scuba diver</a> to measure the time and depth of a dive so that a safe ascent profile can be calculated and displayed so that the diver can avoid <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-aaus_13-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-aaus-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dive factor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Factor used in gas consumption estimates which allows for increased breathing rate due to conditions other than depth. Values range from 1.1 for relaxed, stress free conditions to more than 3.0 for heavy work.<sup id=""cite_ref-SDI_Solo_IG_14-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SDI_Solo_IG-14"">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dive flag (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Flag used to indicate that there are divers in the water. There are two versions: the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_maritime_signal_flags"" title=""International maritime signal flags"">international code letter flag 'Alpha'</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ICS_Alpha.svg"" class=""image""><img alt=""ICS Alpha.svg"" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/ICS_Alpha.svg/15px-ICS_Alpha.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""15"" height=""15"" class=""thumbborder"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/ICS_Alpha.svg/23px-ICS_Alpha.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/ICS_Alpha.svg/30px-ICS_Alpha.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""600"" data-file-height=""600"" /></a>, and the red flag with white diagonal bar, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ICS_Diver.svg"" class=""image""><img alt=""ICS Diver.svg"" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ICS_Diver.svg/15px-ICS_Diver.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""15"" height=""15"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ICS_Diver.svg/23px-ICS_Diver.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ICS_Diver.svg/30px-ICS_Diver.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""600"" data-file-height=""600"" /></a>.
"
"dive ladder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"diver ladder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_factors_in_diving_equipment_design#Diver_ladders"" title=""Human factors in diving equipment design"">Human factors in diving equipment design#Diver ladders</a></span></p>
A ladder suitable for divers dressed for the specific dive to climb up and down between the surface deployment area and the water.
"
"Dive Leader (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
EN 14153-3 / ISO 24801-3 standard competence for recreational scuba diver. A level 3 ""Dive Leader"" has sufficient knowledge, skill and experience to plan, organise and conduct their dives and lead other recreational scuba divers in open water, to conduct any specialised recreational scuba diving activities for which they have received appropriate training, plan and execute emergency procedures appropriate for the diving environment and activities. If diving and environmental conditions are significantly different from those previously experienced, they require an appropriate orientation with regard to local environmental conditions, and must have appropriate specialised training and experience to lead on dives which have more demanding operational parameters.<sup id=""cite_ref-EUF_level_3_15-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EUF_level_3-15"">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dive location (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
(Professional) The vessel, structure, or base from which occupational dives are conducted and supported. More specifically, the point from which the actual dive is controlled.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dive marshall (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Recreational and club diving equivalent of a diving supervisor. The person who organizes and plans a group dive outing for recreational divers, assesses risk, logs divers into and out of the water and is available at the site to manage incident response.<sup id=""cite_ref-Crabbsac_16-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Crabbsac-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"divemaster (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divemaster"" title=""Divemaster"">Divemaster</a></span></p>
A professional level recreational diver who leads a group of less experienced or visiting divers underwater.
"
"dive platform (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Recreational: Fixed or movable platform on a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_boat"" title=""Dive boat"">dive boat</a> which divers use to more easily enter and leave the water.
2.&#160;&#160;Commercial: Structure on which the <a href=""#diving_spread""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diving spread"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diving spread</span></a> is established. Usually a vessel or an offshore or waterside structure.
"
"dive profile (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_profile"" title=""Dive profile"">Dive profile</a></span></p>
The variation of depth with elapsed time during a dive, often depicted as a graph.
"
"dive site (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_site"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dive site"">Dive site</a></span></p>
The place at which the dive occurs. Also, more broadly, a place at which diving occurs, has occurred, or is planned to occur, and the general locality, with extent depending on context. Professional divers may also refer to a work site, or search area if relevant.
"
"dive skins (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lycra"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Lycra"">lycra</a> suit worn by a diver in warm water or under a wet suit.
"
"dive station (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The site from which a professional diving operation is directly controlled.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dive tables (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#decompression_tables""><span title=""See entry on this page at § decompression tables"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">decompression tables</span></a></span></p>"
"dive time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The total elapsed time spent underwater during a dive.
"
"dive timer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_timer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dive timer"">Dive timer</a></span></p>
An automatically operated electronic timer which records the elapsed time from the start of a dive.
"
"diver lift (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_boat#Diver_lifts"" title=""Dive boat"">Dive boat#Diver lifts</a></span></p>
A mechanism used to lower one or more divers into the water to a shallow depth, and to lift them out again.
"
"diver training manual (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Training_manual"" title=""Training manual"">Training manual</a>, <a href=""/w/index.php?title=Diving_manual&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Diving manual (page does not exist)"">Diving manual</a></span></p>
A publication containing instructional material for diver training. This may relate to a specific certification or a range of certifications, and is usually published either by a certification agency or a diving school for their own use, but may also be published and sold for general consumption.
"
"diver transfer chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Hyperbaric chamber connecting other component chambers of a saturation life support system which may be at different pressures.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_3-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diver umbilical (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"diver's umbilical (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_cable#Diver"" title=""Umbilical cable"">Umbilical cable#Diver</a></span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § umbilical cable"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#umbilical_cable"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">umbilical cable</a></span></span></p> 
Bundle of life-support hoses, communication cable, pneumofathomer hose and strength member between the surface control point and a surface-supplied diver.
"
"Divers Alert Network (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""DAN""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divers_Alert_Network"" title=""Divers Alert Network"">Divers Alert Network</a></span></p>
A non-profit organization for assisting divers in medical and travel emergencies, advising divers on medical matters, and medical research on recreational diving safety.
"
"diver's attendant (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""dive tender"" and ""line attendant""<sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2001_17-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2001-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></span></p>
A person who assists the working diver to prepare for a dive, get in and out of the water, and to undress from the diving equipment, and who tends the lifeline or umbilical while the diver is in the water.<sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2001_17-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2001-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diver's slate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: wrist slate</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § wet notes"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#wet_notes"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">wet notes</a></span></span></p>
Piece of opaque white or pale coloured rigid plastic sheet with matte finish that is easily marked with a graphite pencil, used for taking notes, making sketches and written communication underwater.
"
"dive/surface valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Dive/Surface_valve"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Dive/Surface valve</a></span></p> 
Valve on the mouthpiece of a rebreather which can be switched between the loop and ambient air at the surface. It seals the breathing loop on the surface setting to prevent flooding the loop and is used for this purpose if the mouthpiece is removed from the mouth in the water. Compare with <span title=""See entry on this page at § bailout valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bailout_valve"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">bailout valve</a></span> (BOV).
"
"diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Underwater activity and related recompression facility operations where personnel are subjected to elevated ambient pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving basket (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A diver deployment device similar to a <a href=""#diving_stage""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diving stage"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diving stage</span></a>, normally designed with an open cage.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving bell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">Diving bell</a></span></p>
A rigid chamber suspended from a cable and used to transport divers to depth and back to the surface.
"
"diving chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;A simple form of submersible vessel to take divers underwater and to provide a temporary base and retrieval system in the depths (<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">diving bell</a>).
2.&#160;&#160;A land or ship-based <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_chamber"" title=""Diving chamber"">hyperbaric chamber</a> to artificially reproduce the hyperbaric conditions under the sea.
"
"diving contractor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Legal persona responsible for commercial diving operations.<sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2009_12-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2009-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving depth (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Generally the maximum depth to which the diver is exposed during a dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving heavy (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § overweighting"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#overweighting"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">overweighting</a></span></span></p>
Practice of carrying significantly more ballast weight than necessary to neutralise buoyancy. Common in professional diving operations where the diver needs to remain in firm contact with the bottom to work effectively, and is tethered by a lifeline or umbilical to a control point at a place of safety, which is managed by a tender.
"
"diving manual (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § operations manual"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#operations_manual"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">operations manual</a></span></i> 
2.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href=""#diver_training_manual""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diver training manual"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diver training manual</span></a></i>
"
"Diving Medical Advisory Council (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""DMAC""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_Medical_Advisory_Council"" title=""Diving Medical Advisory Council"">Diving Medical Advisory Council</a></span></p> 
An independent body of diving medical specialists from Northern Europe which provides advice about medical and certain safety aspects of commercial diving.<sup id=""cite_ref-DMAC_18-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DMAC-18"">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving medical technician (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""DMT""</span></p>
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paramedic"" title=""Paramedic"">paramedic</a> specialising in diving related conditions, and medically fit to dive in a hyperbaric chamber.
"
"diving method (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"diving mode (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_mode"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diving mode"">Diving mode</a></span></p>
The combination of diving equipment, breathing medium and compression/decompression used for a diving operation, e.g. breathhold, open circuit scuba, nitrox rebreather, surface-supplied air, heliox saturation, etc.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving operation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_operation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diving operation"">Diving operation</a></span></p>
A portion of a diving project that can be safely supervised by one person, which can be a single dive or a number of dives.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving procedure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Sequence of actions used to achieve a specific outcome during a diving operation. Often standardised, and based on experience of the procedure being safe and efficient. May be specified, recommended, or authorised by a training manual, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operations_manual"" title=""Operations manual"">operations manual</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_of_practice"" title=""Code of practice"">code of practice</a>, and may have to be adapted to suit circumstances, while remaining essentially similar. See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_operating_procedure"" title=""Standard operating procedure"">Standard operating procedure</a>.
"
"diving project (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The overall diving job by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_contractor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diving contractor"">diving contractor</a> under a specific contract or plan, regardless of duration.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2009_12-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2009-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving regulator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § regulator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#regulator"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">regulator</a></span></span></p>"
"diving response (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"diving reflex (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_reflex"" title=""Diving reflex"">Diving reflex</a></span></p>
The involuntary physiological response to immersion which exists in all air-breathing vertebrates. It is a series of autonomic responses to apnea which are strengthened by facial cooling and hypoxia. It consists of peripheral vasoconstriction and associated hypertension, vagally induced bradycardia and reduction of cardiac output. This appears to preferentially supply oxygen to the brain. Another aspect is splenic contraction which increases haemoglobin content of the blood.<sup id=""cite_ref-Lindholm_and_Lundgren_2009_19-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Lindholm_and_Lundgren_2009-19"">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving safety officer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_safety_officer"" title=""Diving safety officer"">Diving safety officer</a></span></p>
The person who administers a United States university's research diving safety program.<sup id=""cite_ref-sio2003_20-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-sio2003-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving signals (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_communications"" title=""Diver communications"">Diver communications</a></span></p>
Hand sign and light sign system used by scuba divers to communicate when underwater.
"
"diving stage (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""basket""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Diving_stages_and_wet_bells"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Diving stages and wet bells</a></span></p>
A platform on which a diver stands which is hoisted into the water, lowered to the workplace at the bottom, and then hoisted up again to return the diver to the surface and lift them out of the water. The diving stage is particularly effective for controlling rate of descent and ascent.<sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2001_17-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2001-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving superintendent (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Person with overall responsibility for commercial diving operations at a large installation.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving supervisor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_supervisor"" title=""Diving supervisor"">Diving supervisor</a></span></p>
Person in charge of, and responsible for safety of a commercial diving operation. Usually trained, assessed as competent, certified and registered. Formally appointed by the diving contractor.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"diving support vessel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""DSV""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_support_vessel"" title=""Diving support vessel"">Diving support vessel</a></span></p> 
A ship or boat used as a base for diving operations, particularly if designed or fitted out for that purpose.
"
"diving system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The complete set of equipment necessary to support a diving operation.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The equipment and facilities required to execute the planned diving activity, including compression, decompression, rescue and recovery.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DMAC (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § Diving Medical Advisory Council"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#Diving_Medical_Advisory_Council"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">Diving Medical Advisory Council</a></span></span></p>"
"DMT (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#diving_medical_technician""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Diving medical technician"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Diving medical technician</span></a></span></p>"
"Doing It Right (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""DIR""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doing_It_Right_(scuba_diving)"" title=""Doing It Right (scuba diving)"">Doing It Right</a></span></p>
A holistic approach to scuba diving, which encompasses several essential elements, including fundamental diving skills, teamwork, physical fitness, strictly defined standard procedures, and the use of standardised, streamlined and minimalistic equipment configurations.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_22-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dome port (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A domed window of optical quality glass or plastic which covers the front of an underwater camera or video housing.
"
"donating the octopus (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#donating_the_secondary""><span title=""See entry on this page at § donating the secondary"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">donating the secondary</span></a></span></p>"
"donating the primary (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Rescue technique where the donor of breathing gas provides it via the primary second stage – the one from which the donor was breathing – as it is known to be working and providing the correct gas. The donor then switches to their backup DV, often stowed under the chin by a bungee necklace with a breakaway connection.
"
"donating the secondary (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Rescue technique where the donor of breathing gas provides it via the secondary, or octopus, second stage, and continues to breathe off the primary.
"
"donkey dick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Slang term for the corrugated buoyancy compensator inflation and deflation hose.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Doppler bubble detection (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Doppler_ultrasonic_bubble_detection"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Doppler ultrasonic bubble detection</a></span></p>
Ultrasonic signals reflected from bubble surfaces to identify and quantify gas bubbles present in venous blood.
"
"Dorf arrow (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""line arrow""</span></p>
Triangular plastic line marker with two slots which is mounted on a cave guide line to indicate the direction of the exit.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"downline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"down line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
