A rope leading from the surface down to the underwater workplace which allows a commercial diver to travel directly to and from the job site and to control rate of descent and ascent in the same way as using a shotline. Also sometimes called a jackstay.<sup id=""cite_ref-Barsky_and_Christensen_2004_23-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Barsky_and_Christensen_2004-23"">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> A downline used for open ocean diving is much the same as a shotline (q.v.), but does not reach all the way to the bottom. An open-ocean downline is weighted at the bottom, and attached to a substantial float at the surface, which may be tethered to the boat. It may be marked at intervals by knots or loops, and may be attached to decompression trapeze system. In some cases a sea anchor may be used to limit wind drift, particularly if attached to a boat with significant windage.<sup id=""cite_ref-NOAA_12.6_24-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-NOAA_12.6-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
"
"downstream (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
In the direction of flow. Displaced from the reference point in the direction of flow
"
"downstream valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#Upstream_vs_downstream"" title=""Diving regulator"">Diving regulator#Upstream vs downstream</a></span></p>
Valve in which the closure is downstream of the orifice. Pressure in the line tends to assist in opening the valve. When spring-loaded a downstream valve may open automatically if the pressure difference is excessive, thus functioning as a pressure relief valve
"
"down time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Period when planned activities can not be done due to unforeseen or uncontrollable circumstances.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DP alert (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Status of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_positioning"" title=""Dynamic positioning"">dynamic positioning</a> system regarding positional accuracy and reliability. Green indicates normal operation, yellow indicates degraded operation and red indicates emergency.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DP footprint (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_positioning"" title=""Dynamic positioning"">Dynamic positioning</a> footprint: The area around the nominal position to which a dynamically positioned vessel is constrained by the DP system.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"DPV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""#diver_propulsion_vehicle""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diver propulsion vehicle"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diver propulsion vehicle</span></a>
2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""#dynamically_positioned_vessel""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dynamically positioned vessel"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dynamically positioned vessel</span></a>
"
"D-ring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A ring shaped like a capital D, usually of stainless steel or plastic, stitched or buckled to a diver's harness and used as an attachment point for lifeline, cylinders or other equipment.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_22-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Dräger tube (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"Draeger tube (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Indicator tube used for testing breathing gas quality.
"
"drift diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drift_diving"" title=""Drift diving"">drift diving</a></span></p>
Any dive where the diver is transported significantly by drifting with currents during the dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_22-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
"
"drillship (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Ship built or converted for offshore well drilling, using dynamic positioning to maintain position in deep water.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"drop cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § stage cylinder"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#stage_cylinder"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">stage cylinder</a></span></span></p>"
"drop weight (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Weight used during descent and ascent, but left on the bottom at the guideline during the deep part of the dive when it is not needed due to suit compression.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"drowning (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drowning"" title=""Drowning"">Drowning</a></span></p>
The process of experiencing respiratory impairment from submersion/immersion in liquid.
"
"dry bag (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_bag"" title=""Dry bag"">Dry bag</a></span></p>
Bag which seals in a watertight manner. Used for keeping clothes and other equipment dry in a wet environment.
"
"dry bell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § closed bell"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#closed_bell"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">closed bell</a></span></span></p>"
"dry filling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Temperature_change_during_filling"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Temperature change during filling</a></span></p>
Filling scuba cylinders without the use of a water bath for cooling.<sup id=""cite_ref-Dry_filling_25-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Dry_filling-25"">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dry suit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_suit"" title=""Dry suit"">Dry suit</a></span></p>
A watertight suit worn to keep the diver dry and to provide protection from the environment. Thermal insulation may be provided by the suit or garments worn under the suit.
"
"dry suit blowup (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_suit#Over-inflation"" title=""Dry suit"">Dry suit#Over-inflation</a></span></p>
Uncontrolled ascent due to over-inflation of a dry suit.
"
"DSV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""#dive/surface_valve""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dive/surface valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dive/surface valve</span></a> 
2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""#diving_support_vessel""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diving support vessel"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diving support vessel</span></a>
"
"DSMB (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""delayed surface marker buoy"" and ""decompression buoy""</span></p>
An inflatable marker buoy deployed from underwater to indicate the position of a diver and to control ascent rate. Can also be used to mark a position or signal an emergency."
"duckbill valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duckbill_valve"" title=""Duckbill valve"">Duckbill valve</a></span></p>
A non-return valve, manufactured from rubber or synthetic elastomer, and shaped somewhat like the beak of a duck. Used as exhaust valve in some twin-hose diving regulators
"
"dump line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A rope attached to the dump valve on a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lift_bag"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Lift bag"">lift bag</a> which is used by a diver to operate the dump valve to release air for control and adjustment of the bag buoyancy.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dump valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Valve used to release excess gas from a dry suit, buoyancy compensator, rebreather, or lift bag. Usually manually operated in buoyancy compensators and lift bags, and <a href=""#automatic_dump_valve""><span title=""See entry on this page at § automatic dump valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">automatic</span></a> in dry suits and rebreathers. May also function as an <span title=""See entry on this page at § overpressure valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#overpressure_valve"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">overpressure valve</a></span>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dwell time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""/w/index.php?title=Dwell_time_(filtration)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Dwell time (filtration) (page does not exist)"">Dwell time (filtration)</a></span></p> 
Time that the breathing gas passing through a filter stack or absorbent canister remains in contact with the <a href=""/w/index.php?title=Active_filtration&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Active filtration (page does not exist)"">active filtration</a> medium where the absorption of impurities can occur.<sup id=""cite_ref-26"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dynamically positioned vessel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_positioning"" title=""Dynamic positioning"">Dynamic positioning</a></span></p>
Vessel which maintains position and heading using thrusters and positional feedback <sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_22-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dynamic positioning (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_positioning"" title=""Dynamic positioning"">Dynamic positioning</a></span></p>
Method of keeping a floating platform in position without anchoring, using thrusters and positional feedback.
"
"dynamic setpoint (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""floating setpoint""</span></p>
A target value for oxygen partial pressure in a rebreather loop which varies as a function of depth. Generally a setpoint that changes to optimize gas use, no stop time and other dive variables.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_9-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
"
"dysbarism (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dysbarism"" title=""Dysbarism"">Dysbarism</a></span></p>
Medical conditions resulting from changes in ambient pressure.


"
"EAD (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""#equivalent_air_depth""><span title=""See entry on this page at § equivalent air depth"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">equivalent air depth</span></a></span></p>"
"EAN (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""#enriched_Air_Nitrox""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Enriched Air Nitrox"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Enriched Air Nitrox</span></a></span></p>"
"ear beer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A home made mixture of alcohol and acetic acid in water used as a drying agent and disinfectant to rinse the ears after diving, to prevent ear infections.
"
"ear clearing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ear_clearing"" title=""Ear clearing"">Ear clearing</a></span></p>
Equalising the pressure in the middle and external ear by opening the Eustachian tubes. Several techniques are used.<sup id=""cite_ref-NOAA_4th_ed_27-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-NOAA_4th_ed-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
"
"ECCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"ECCCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_rebreather#Control_of_the_breathing_gas_mix"" title=""Diving rebreather"">Diving rebreather#Control of the breathing gas mix</a></span></p>
Electronic closed circuit <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather"" title=""Rebreather"">rebreather</a>. Sometimes ECCCR for electronically controlled closed circuit rebreather, which is the same thing.
"
"eddy current test (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddy-current_testing"" title=""Eddy-current testing"">Eddy-current testing</a></span></p>
Method of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-destructive_testing"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Non-destructive testing"">non-destructive testing</a> using electromagnetic induction to detect flaws in conductive materials. It is used to detect cracks in parallel neck threads of aluminium cylinders. Also called <span title=""See entry on this page at § Visual Plus inspection"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#Visual_Plus_inspection"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">Visual Plus inspection</a></span>. Required for cylinders of <span title=""See entry on this page at § AA6351"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#AA6351"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">AA6351</a></span> alloy.
"
"EDTC (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""#european_Diving_Technology_Committee""><span title=""See entry on this page at § European Diving Technology Committee"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">European Diving Technology Committee</span></a>
"
"EGS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#emergency_gas_supply""><span title=""See entry on this page at § emergency gas supply"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">emergency gas supply</span></a></span></p>"
"E-L algorithm (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#vVAL18""><span title=""See entry on this page at § VVAL18"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">VVAL18</span></a></span></p>"
"electro-galvanic oxygen sensor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electro-galvanic_oxygen_sensor"" title=""Electro-galvanic oxygen sensor"">electro-galvanic oxygen sensor</a></span></p> 
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electro-chemical_fuel_cell"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Electro-chemical fuel cell"">Electro-chemical fuel cell</a> which produces a voltage proportional to the partial pressure of oxygen.
"
"emergency gas supply (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § bailout cylinder"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bailout_cylinder"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">bailout cylinder</a></span></span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bailout_bottle"" title=""Bailout bottle"">Bailout bottle</a>,  also <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Bailout_gas_supply"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">Surface-supplied diving#Bailout gas supply</a></span></p>
Breathing gas supply to a diver that is intended for use in a failure of primary, and where applicable, secondary, breathing gas supply systems. More than one emergency gas supply may be available, of which at least one is usually carried by the diver (scuba).
"
"emergency position indicating radio beacon (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"emergency position indicating radiobeacon (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""emergency beacon"" or ""EPIRB""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergency_position-indicating_radiobeacon_station"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Emergency position-indicating radiobeacon station"">Emergency position-indicating radiobeacon station</a></span></p>
Tracking transmitters which aid in the detection and location of boats and people in distress at sea.
"
"emergency swimming ascent (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""ESA"", ""Controlled emergency swimming ascent"", ""CESA""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergency_swimming_ascent"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Emergency swimming ascent"">Emergency swimming ascent</a></span></p>
Emergency procedure where the diver makes an ascent at approximately neutral buoyancy from depth after a breathing gas supply failure.
"
"encapsulation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Using a diving suit which completely isolates the diver from direct contact with the environment.<sup id=""cite_ref-encapsulation_28-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-encapsulation-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"END (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#equivalent_Narcotic_Depth""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Equivalent Narcotic Depth"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Equivalent Narcotic Depth</span></a></span></p>"
"Enriched Air Nitrox (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § nitrox"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#nitrox"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">nitrox</a></span></span></p>"
"EPIRB (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#emergency_position_indicating_radio_beacon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § emergency position indicating radio beacon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">emergency position indicating radio beacon</span></a></span></p>"
"equalise (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Balance pressure of a gas filled space with the ambient pressure, by adding or venting gas, to prevent barotrauma or pressure damage.
"
"equivalent air depth (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""EAD""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equivalent_air_depth"" title=""Equivalent air depth"">Equivalent air depth</a></span></p>
Depth at which partial pressure of nitrogen in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrox"" title=""Nitrox"">nitrox</a> mixture at a given depth is equal to the partial pressure of nitrogen in air. Used for approximating the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_(diving)"" title=""Decompression (diving)"">decompression</a> requirements of nitrox mixtures by finding the depth at which air would require the same decompression. Based on exposure to equal partial pressures of nitrogen at maximum depth.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_3-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"equivalent narcotic depth (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"equivalent nitrogen depth (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""END""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equivalent_narcotic_depth"" title=""Equivalent narcotic depth"">Equivalent narcotic depth</a></span></p>
A way of expressing the narcotic effect of a breathing gas mixture at depth by comparison with the depth at which air would have a similar effect. Used to choose nitrogen content of a Trimix breathing gas for a planned dive profile to limit <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis"" title=""Nitrogen narcosis"">nitrogen narcosis</a>. Based on limiting the partial pressure of nitrogen during the dive by diluting the breathing gas with helium.
"
"eSCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Electronic semi-closed circuit rebreather, where an electronic control system monitors the partial pressure of oxygen and adds gas to maintain a <a href=""#floating_setpoint""><span title=""See entry on this page at § floating setpoint"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">floating setpoint</span></a> to optimise gas use and compensate for variations in diver exertion.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_9-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
"
"European Diving Technology Committee (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Diving_Technology_Committee"" title=""European Diving Technology Committee"">European Diving Technology Committee</a></span></p>
International committee of European representatives promoting good standards for diving and co-ordinating, where possible, differing standards with the aim of making European professional diving safer.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2010_29-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2010-29"">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
"
"exceptional exposure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A dive in which the risk of decompresssion sickness, oxygen toxicity, and/or exposure to the elements is substantially greater than on a normal working dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDMR6_9-3.23_30-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDMR6_9-3.23-30"">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
"
"excursion (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"excursion dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Saturation diving where the divers work at a depth deeper or shallower than the saturation depth, after which they are returned to the original saturation pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"excursion tables (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Tables for use in saturation diving that specify the limit upward and downward of excursions from the nominal depth, and provide a zone in which the diver can move freely without regard to the number of excursions or their duration without incurring a decompression penalty.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-11"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"excursion umbilical (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_cable#Diver"" title=""Umbilical cable"">Umbilical cable#Diver</a></span></p>
The combined supply and return hoses and cables for life-line, life-support, heating, power and communications between a diving bell and the diver
"
"exhaust valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A valve controlling the venting of gas from any higher pressure source such as a diving chamber, diver’s helmet, dry suit, buoyancy system, volume tank, lift bag etc. For some of these applications, also known as a <a href=""#dump_valve""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dump valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dump valve</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-12"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"extraction ratio (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""ventilation/oxygen extraction ratio""</span></p>
Ratio between minute ventilation and oxygen uptake, the volume rate of gas breathed to the amount of oxygen taken up in the bloodstream. A typical surface extraction ratio of 20 would mean that for every 20 litres of gas breathed, 1 litre of oxygen would be absorbed in the lungs.


"
"faceplate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<span title=""See entry on this page at § viewport"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#viewport"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">Viewport</a></span> of a full-face mask or helmet. The transparent window through which the diver can see the surroundings.
"
"failure modes and effects analysis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""FMEA""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Failure_mode_and_effects_analysis"" title=""Failure mode and effects analysis"">Failure mode and effects analysis</a></span></p>
A methodology used to identify potential failure modes, determine their effects and identify actions to mitigate the potential failures.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-13"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"failure modes, effects, and criticality analysis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""FMECA""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Failure_mode,_effects_and_criticality_analysis"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Failure mode, effects and criticality analysis"">Failure mode, effects and criticality analysis</a></span></p>
An extension to FMEA of a criticality analysis, which combines the probability of failure modes with the severity of their consequences to identify relative risk of each mode, allowing remedial effort to be directed where it is likely to produce the greatest effect.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-14"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"farmer john (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wet_suit"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Wet suit"">Wet suit</a> that covers the torso and legs only; it resembles a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bib_overall"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Bib overall"">bib overall</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salopettes"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Salopettes"">salopettes</a>.
"
"fatigue cracking (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatigue_(material)"" title=""Fatigue (material)"">Fatigue (material)</a></span></p>
Cracking in a material resulting from multiple stress cycles below the ultimate or yield strength. Usually refers to large number of cycles.

"
"feather breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Skills"" title=""Sidemount diving"">Sidemount diving#Skills</a></span></p>
Technique for emergency breathing from a free-flowing demand valve where the diver manually controls air flow by opening and closing the cylinder valve.
"
"feet sea water (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feet_sea_water"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Feet sea water"">feet sea water</a></span></p>
Unit of pressure equal to 1/33 atm. Not a linear measure of depth. Generally defined as the pressure exerted by a foot depth of seawater having a specific gravity of 1.027 and is approximately equal to 0.445 pounds per square inch.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-15"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"FFM (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#full-face_mask""><span title=""See entry on this page at § full-face mask"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">full-face mask</span></a></span></p>"
"ffw (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"FFW (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feet_fresh_water"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Feet fresh water"">Feet fresh water</a></span></p>
Feet fresh water. Unit of pressure equal to 1/34 atm. Not a linear measure of depth."
"filling ratio (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Ratio of the mass of gas in a cylinder to the internal volume of the cylinder (water capacity), usually expressed in kilograms per litre, or pounds per cubic foot.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS10019:2019_31-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS10019:2019-31"">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
"
"filling whip (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_air_compressor#Filling_diving_cylinders"" title=""Diving air compressor"">Diving air compressor#Filling diving cylinders</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Filling"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Filling</a></span></p>
High pressure flexible hose used to connect a cylinder to the storage cylinder, filling panel, booster or compressor, through which high pressure gas flows to fill the cylinder.
"
"filtration (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filtration"" title=""Filtration"">Filtration</a></span></p>
Process for removing impurities from a fluid. Particulates are commonly removed by passing the fluid through porous material with pore size small enough to trap the particles (e.g. micron filters). Liquids and gases are commonly absorbed or adsorbed by the surface of the filter medium (e.g. activated carbon, molecular sieve, silica gel), or may be chemically combined with the medium (e.g. Sodalime) or catalytically converted (e.g. Hopcalite) into a less objectionable substance.
"
"fin keepers (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"fin retainers (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""fin holders"", ""fin fasteners"", ""fin grips"", ""fin keeps"", ""fin guards"", ""flipper fixers"", ""Y-straps"", ""ankle straps"", ""accessory safety straps"", ""fix fins"", ""grip fins"" and, in recognition of their French origin, ""fixe-palmes"".</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swimfin#Attachment"" title=""Swimfin"">Swimfin#Attachment</a></span></p>
Y-shaped elastic rubber straps worn over the arch, the heel and the instep of each foot to help prevent swim-fins from falling off the diver's feet. Mainly used with full-foot-pocket fins.
"
"first stage (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#First_stage"" title=""Diving regulator"">Diving regulator#First stage</a></span></p>
Diving regulator component which reduces gas pressure from storage pressure in the cylinder to interstage pressure for supply to the second stage and for suit and buoyancy compensator inflation.
"
"five nines (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"five nines purity (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
99.999% pure gas. Usually referring to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">breathing grade</a> oxygen or helium for blending.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"fixed diving system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A <a href=""#diving_system""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diving system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diving system</span></a> (q.v.) installed permanently on a vessel or structure.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-16"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"floating setpoint (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#dynamic_setpoint""><span title=""See entry on this page at § dynamic setpoint"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">dynamic setpoint</span></a></span></p>"
"flood-up valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: bell flooding valve<sup id=""cite_ref-32"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-32"">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></span></p>
A valve in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">diving bell</a> which allows air to escape and internal water level to rise. This can be useful to assist the <span title=""See entry on this page at § bellman"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bellman"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">bellman</a></span> in recovering an incapacitated diver through the bottom hatch.<sup id=""cite_ref-33"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-33"">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-34"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-34"">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
"
"flow (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Movement of water through a cave or ducting system. Similar in meaning to current in open water.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"fluorocarbon elastomers (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fluoroelastomer"" title=""Fluoroelastomer"">Fluoroelastomer</a></span></p>
Synthetic elastomers (rubber) with good performance in high partial pressures of oxygen. Preferred material for o-rings in diving regulators for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_service"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Oxygen service"">oxygen service</a>.
"
"flush (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#diluent_flush""><span title=""See entry on this page at § diluent flush"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">diluent flush</span></a></span></p>"
"flutter kick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finning_techniques#Flutter_kick"" title=""Finning techniques"">Finning techniques#Flutter kick</a></span></p>
finning style where the fins are alternately moved up and down by movements of the full leg.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Thrust is developed on both up and down strokes. Vortices shed move both upwards and downwards. See also <span title=""See entry on this page at § modified flutter kick"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#modified_flutter_kick"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">modified flutter kick</a></span>.
"
"FMEA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#failure_modes_and_effects_analysis""><span title=""See entry on this page at § failure modes and effects analysis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">failure modes and effects analysis</span></a></span></p>"
"FMECA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#failure_modes,_effects_and_criticality_analysis""><span title=""See entry on this page at § failure modes, effects and criticality analysis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">failure modes, effects and criticality analysis</span></a></span></p>"
"fogging (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-fog"" title=""Anti-fog"">Anti-fog</a></span></p>
Condensation of water vapour on the inside surface of a mask or helmet faceplate, reducing visibility.
"
"forward roll entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries"" title=""Scuba skills"">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
Water entry technique used by scuba divers from a boat or platform too high or unsuitable for <span title=""See entry on this page at § backward roll entry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#backward_roll_entry"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">backward roll entry</a></span>. The diver bends forward at the hips and waist and falls forward into the water, making a partial somersault and breaking the water with the cylinder, back and shoulders. Not suitable for heights more than about 2&#160;m, and can be problematic if the diver is carrying several heavy items like stage cylinders or large cameras.
"
"four-wire system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Voice communications using separate wire pairs for each direction.
"
"frame (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Transportable assemblies of gas cylinders connected by a manifold and securely mounted to a structural framework.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> See also <span title=""See entry on this page at § quad"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#quad"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">quad</a></span> and <span title=""See entry on this page at § kelly"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#kelly"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">kelly</a></span>.
"
"free air (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <a href=""#free_gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § free gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">free gas</span></a></span></p>
Air at normal atmospheric pressure.
"
"free-diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free-diving"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Free-diving"">Free-diving</a></span></p>
Underwater diving that does not involve the use of external breathing apparatus, but relies on a diver's ability to hold their breath until resurfacing. See also <span title=""See entry on this page at § breath-hold diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#breath-hold_diving"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">breath-hold diving</a></span>, and <span title=""See entry on this page at § apnea"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#apnea"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">apnea</a></span> (q.v.)
"
"free-flow (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Constant flow rate air supply
2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechanism_of_diving_regulators#Free-flow"" title=""Mechanism of diving regulators"">Mechanism of diving regulators#Free-flow</a> <br />
Malfunction of a demand regulator where the valve sticks in the open position, causing a continuous flow.
"
"free-flow helmet (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_helmet#Free-flow_helmets"" title=""Diving helmet"">Diving helmet#Free-flow helmets</a></span></p>
A helmet where the breathing air supply is supplied at an adjustable, but approximately constant rate regardless of the diver's instantaneous breathing rate.
"
"free-flow valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Valve on the side of a <a href=""#demand_helmet""><span title=""See entry on this page at § demand helmet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">demand helmet</span></a> or full-face mask which opens a continuous flow of breathing gas into the helmet interior, usually directed over the interior of the viewport, hence alternative term defogging valve, as it is often used to blow condensation from the inside of the viewport.
"
"free gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Gas at normal atmospheric pressure. Usually refers to the volume of some amount of compressed gas when allowed to expand to atmospheric pressure at constant temperature
"
"free gas volume (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Equivalent volume of a compressed gas if expanded to  standard atmospheric pressure at constant temperature.<sup id=""cite_ref-engineering_toolbox_35-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-engineering_toolbox-35"">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Frenzel maneuver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ear_clearing"" title=""Ear clearing"">Ear clearing</a></span></p>
Technique for equalising the middle ear by pinching the nose closed and moving the back of the tongue upwards.
"
"frog kick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frog_kick"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Frog kick"">Frog kick</a></span></p>
Finning technique where thrust is developed by sweeping the fins horizontally toward each other with the fins twisted into a nearly vertical plane, with the soles facing each other, followed by a recovery stroke which develops negligible thrust where the fin blades are feathered. The legs are fairly straight during the power stroke. See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § modified frog kick"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#modified_frog_kick"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">modified frog kick</a></span>.
"
"frogman (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frogman"" title=""Frogman"">Frogman</a></span></p>
A scuba diver, particularly a military diver on an undercover mission.
"
"fsw (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#feet_sea_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § feet sea water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">feet sea water</span></a></span></p>"
"full duplex (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duplex_(telecommunications)#Full_duplex"" title=""Duplex (telecommunications)"">Duplex (telecommunications)#Full duplex</a></span></p>
Voice communication system where both users can transmit and receive at the same time. Compare with <a href=""#full_duplex"">half duplex</a>
"
"full-face mask (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full-face_diving_mask"" title=""Full-face diving mask"">Full-face diving mask</a></span></p>
Diving mask covering the eyes, nose and mouth, and which provides the diver with breathing gas


"
"gap (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § jump"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#jump"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">jump</a></span></span></p> 
The space between two cave guidelines. Usually between a main guideline and the start tie-off of a branch line.
"
"gap spool (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distance_line#Spools"" title=""Distance line"">Distance line#Spools</a></span></p>
A relatively short length of cave line on a spool used to bridge a gap between lines when making an excursion from the main guideline to a branch guideline. The line is left in place during the excursion, and usually retrieved on the way out
"
"gaiter (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""gator"" (US)</span></p> Textile legging wrapped around the calf and ankle area over a dry suit to restrict the amount of air that can get into the lower leg area. Also can reduce drag of the suit in this area by smoothing over creases and folds."
"gas blender (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Person who mixes breathing gases for diving, filling <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder"" title=""Diving cylinder"">diving cylinders</a> with gas mixes such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrox"" title=""Nitrox"">nitrox</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)"" title=""Trimix (breathing gas)"">trimix</a>.
2.&#160;&#160;Certification of competence to mix breathing gases for diving.<sup id=""cite_ref-ISO13293_36-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ISO13293-36"">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
"
"gas blending (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving"" title=""Gas blending for scuba diving"">Gas blending for scuba diving</a></span></p>
Mixing breathing gases for diving, filling <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder"" title=""Diving cylinder"">diving cylinders</a> with gas mixes such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrox"" title=""Nitrox"">nitrox</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)"" title=""Trimix (breathing gas)"">trimix</a>.
"
"gas block (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#gas_switching_block""><span title=""See entry on this page at § gas switching block"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">gas switching block</span></a></span></p>"
"gas embolism (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_embolism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Gas embolism"">Gas embolism</a></span></p>
Blockage of a blood vessel by a bubble of gas.
"
"gas extender (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Carbon dioxide scrubber used to allow partial recirculation of surface-supplied or scuba breathing gas to reduce waste. A form of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Semi-closed_circuit_rebreathers"" title=""Rebreather"">semi-closed circuit rebreather</a>.
"
"gaseous impurities (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Contaminants in the compressed breathing air or gas mixture which are in gaseous form. Compare with particulate and condensate impurities.
"
"gas integration (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"gas-integrated dive computer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas-integrated_dive_computer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Gas-integrated dive computer"">Gas-integrated dive computer</a></span></p>
Technology to display gas pressure in a scuba cylinder on a dive computer, and in some cases make further use of the information for gas management.
"
"gas fraction (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_composition"" title=""Gas composition"">Gas composition</a></span></p>
The fraction by molecular count, volume or pressure (they all come to the same thing) of a specific gas in a mixture of gases.
"
"gas matching (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Gas_matching"" title=""Scuba gas planning"">Scuba gas planning#Gas matching</a></span></p>
The calculation of reserve and turn pressures for divers using different cylinder volumes on the same dive, allowing each diver to ensure that sufficient gas is retained at all times to allow for foreseeable contingencies based on each diver's cylinder volumes, and both divers' individual gas consumption rates.<sup id=""cite_ref-37"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-37"">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
"
"gas narcosis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § inert gas narcosis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#inert_gas_narcosis"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">inert gas narcosis</a></span></span></p>"
"gas panel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Gas_panel"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">Surface-supplied diving#Gas panel</a></span></p>
The control equipment for providing breathing gas to surface supplied divers via umbilicals. Primary and reserve gas is supplied to the panel through shutoff valves from low pressure compressors or high pressure storage cylinders.
"
"gas reversal point (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The depth during an ascent or decompression when the intake of dissolved gas is exceeded by outgassing.
"
"gas sensor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A component that produces a signal in the presence of a specific gas, often in proportion to the concentration of the gas.
"
"gas switching (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_switching"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Gas switching"">Gas switching</a></span></p>
The procedure of changing from one breathing gas mixture to another during a dive. This may be done to avoid oxygen toxicity, hypoxia, or nitrogen narcosis, to accelerate decompression, or to avoid running out of breathing gas. Generally applied to open circuit breathing equipment, where a physical change-over of gas source is made. In closed circuit systems the gas composition is continuously controlled to follow the chosen <span title=""See entry on this page at § set-point"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#set-point"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">set-point</a></span>.
"
"gas switching block (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A valve set used for switching from one breathing gas to another during a dive. The most common application is a <span title=""See entry on this page at § bailout block"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bailout_block"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">bailout block</a></span>, but also used to switch gases for decompression on a full face mask, and to switch between deep and shallow gases on a semi-closed rebreather.
"
"gauge mode (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_computer#Additional_functionality_and_features"" title=""Dive computer"">Dive computer#Additional functionality and features</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_computer#Management_of_violations"" title=""Dive computer"">Dive computer#Management of violations</a></span></p>
Operating mode for a personal dive computer where the decompression calculation is disabled, and the unit operated only as a timer and depth gauge. Typically used when diving with gas mixtures not supported by the algorithm, in which case decompression tables are used to monitor and control the decompression schedule. Some dive computers will automatically switch to gauge mode if the diver violates a depth limit, leaving the diver without decompression information.
"
"gauge pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure_measurement#Absolute,_gauge_and_differential_pressures_-_zero_reference"" title=""Pressure measurement"">Pressure measurement#Absolute, gauge and differential pressures - zero reference</a></span></p>
Gauge pressure is zero-referenced against ambient air pressure, so it is equal to absolute pressure minus atmospheric pressure
"
"gauge snubber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Needle_valve"" title=""Needle valve"">needle valve</a> or small bore orifice between the pressure supply and the gauge which damps pressure fluctuations.
"
"Gay-Lussac's law (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gay-Lussac%27s_law"" title=""Gay-Lussac&#39;s law"">Gay-Lussac's law</a></span></p>
Relation between temperature and pressure in an ideal gas for a constant volume."
"general gas equation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"general gas law (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Relation between the variables pressure, volume and temperature for a given mass of a given mixture of an ideal gas.
2.&#160;&#160;Thermodynamic equation of state for gases for the variables volume, pressure, temperature and number and atomic weight of molecules.
"
"giant stride entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § stride entry"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#stride_entry"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">stride entry</a></span></span></p>"
"glossopharangeal insufflation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""buccal pumping"", ""lung packing""</span></p>
A method used by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freediving"" title=""Freediving"">freedivers</a> for filling the lungs with more air than maximal inspiration to normal total lung capacity (TLC). After a full inhalation, the diver fills the mouth with air, while the glottis remains closed, then opens the glottis and forces this air into the lung using the cheeks and tongue to reduce the mouth volume. This may be repeated several times.<sup id=""cite_ref-Potkin_et_al_2007_38-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Potkin_et_al_2007-38"">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
"
"glowstick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A single-use, translucent plastic tube containing isolated substances that, when combined, make light through chemiluminescence
"
"gnarly (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A general purpose adjective to denote a particularly difficult section of a cave, which may be low, tight, silty, etc. or a combination.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>"
"go into decompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Incur a decompression obligation. Generally refers to having a theoretical tissue inert gas concentration that requires the diver to make staged decompression stops during ascent to avoid an unacceptable risk of symptomatic decompression sickness according to the decompression model, algorithm, tables or dive computer in use.
"
"golden rule (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The convention in cave diving that anyone can turn the dive at any time for any reason.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-11"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"gold line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The permanent main guideline in a cave system, that usually starts well inside the cave. Often yellow or gold in colour.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-12"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Goodman handle (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A handle used to carry the primary dive light head comprising a rigid slot through which the fingers and palm of the hand are extended, so that the light rests on the back of the hand, facing the direction of the extended fingers.
"
"GPS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Positioning_System"" title=""Global Positioning System"">Global Positioning System</a></span></p>
A satellite navigation system that provides location and time information in all weather, anywhere on or near the Earth, where there is an unobstructed line of sight to four or more GPS satellites
"
"gradient factor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Gradient_factors"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Gradient factors</a></span></p>
A way of modifying the <span title=""See entry on this page at § M-value"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#M-value"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">M-values</a></span> of a decompression algorithm to more conservative values in proportion to depth. Often used to bias the algorithm towards deeper stops by using a smaller value for the deeper value.
"
"guide line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#distance_line""><span title=""See entry on this page at § distance line"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">distance line</span></a></span></p>
"
"habitat (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><style data-mw-deduplicate=""TemplateStyles:r1033289096"">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_habitat"" title=""Underwater habitat"">Underwater habitat</a></span></p> 
An underwater structure inside which divers can carry out dry welding or which is fitted out with life support facilities.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Haldanean (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"Haldanian (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
