<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Critical_ratio_hypothesis"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Critical ratio hypothesis</a></span></p>
Decompression models based on the principles described by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Scott_Haldane"" title=""John Scott Haldane"">John Scott Haldane</a>.
"
"half+200 (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"half+15 (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_gas_management#Rule_of_thumb_gas_planning"" title=""Scuba gas management"">Scuba gas management#Rule of thumb gas planning</a></span></p>
An alternative reserve calculation strategy to the <span title=""See entry on this page at § rule of thirds"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#rule_of_thirds"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">rule of thirds</a></span> for breathing stage cylinders. The cylinder is breathed down to half of its starting pressure plus 200&#160;psi (or 15 bar), so that a stage cylinder filled to 3000&#160;psi would be breathed down to 1700 psi before being dropped.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_2-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> This is a less conservative strategy for pressures greater than 1200&#160;psi.
"
"half duplex (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duplex_(telecommunications)#Half_duplex"" title=""Duplex (telecommunications)"">Duplex (telecommunications)#Half duplex</a></span></p>
Voice communications system where users take turns to send and receive.
"
"half mask (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_mask"" title=""Diving mask"">Diving mask</a></span></p> 
Diver's mask which covers the eyes and nose but not the mouth.
"
"half times (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § tissue half times"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#tissue_half_times"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">tissue half times</a></span></span></p>"
"halocline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halocline"" title=""Halocline"">Halocline</a></span></p>
A strong variation in salinity over a small depth range within a body of water. Often visible as a blurred or shimmering region due to uneven refractive index.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hand-off cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A diving cylinder, complete with regulator, which can be handed off (manually transferred) to another diver in an emergency, so that the two divers are not obliged to remain in close proximity during the exit and ascent. Transfer of a hand-off cylinder should not compromise either diver's buoyancy to the extent that they cannot make a normal, controlled ascent at neutral buoyancy.
"
"hang (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
To remain stationary at a specific depth and location, particularly when decompressing.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_2-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hang-off (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"hang off (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_profile#Hang-off_profile"" title=""Dive profile"">Dive profile#Hang-off profile</a></span></p>
Commercial diving procedure where the diver ascends to a shallower depth to minimise in-gassing during periods of waiting for surface support. The diver generally ascends to 30 ft waiting depth, and bottom time at that depth is not counted towards decompression obligation. When the support is ready, the diver returns to working depth and time elapsed from leaving hang-off depth accumulates towards decompression obligation. The profile appearance approximates a square wave form, or yo-yo profile.<sup id=""cite_ref-Overland_1999_4-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Overland_1999-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hard hat diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface_supplied_diving"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Surface supplied diving"">Surface supplied diving</a>, generally in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional_diving"" title=""Professional diving"">professional diving</a>, either wearing a modern <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_helmet"" title=""Diving helmet"">diving helmet</a> or the old-style <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_diving_dress"" title=""Standard diving dress"">standard diving dress</a> with copper helmet.
"
"hardwire communications (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Voice communications using a cable for transmission.
"
"harness (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Straps and webbing with associated buckles, D-rings and other accessories used to support the breathing apparatus and secure it to the diver. The harness often has other functions such as supporting weighting and buoyancy control systems and for recovery of the diver from the water. In professional diving the harness is used as a strong point to attach the lifeline or umbilical to the diver.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hat (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Commercial diver term for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_helmet"" title=""Diving helmet"">diving helmet</a>.
"
"HAZID (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazard_identification"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hazard identification"">Hazard identification</a> study: A systematic qualitative assessment of potential hazards and threats to health, safety, equipment, property, environment, production, or reputation. May be followed by a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Risk_assessment"" title=""Risk assessment"">risk assessment</a>.
"
"hazmat diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hazmat_diving"" title=""Hazmat diving"">Hazmat diving</a></span></p>
Diving in a known hazardous materials environment. The environment may be contaminated by hazardous materials, the diving medium may be inherently a hazardous material, or the environment in which the diving medium is situated may include hazardous materials with a significant risk of exposure to these materials to members of the diving team. Special precautions, equipment and procedures are associated with hazmat diving.

"
"head-up display (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""HUD""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head-up_display"" title=""Head-up display"">Head-up display</a></span></p>
A visual display mounted where it is normally in the diver's field of vision.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Health and Safety Executive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""HSE""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_and_Safety_Executive"" title=""Health and Safety Executive"">Health and Safety Executive</a></span></p> 
UK government department responsible for occupational diver safety in UK.
"
"heavy gear (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § standard diving dress"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#standard_diving_dress"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">standard diving dress</a></span></span></p>"
"heliair (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)"" title=""Trimix (breathing gas)"">Trimix (breathing gas)</a></span></p>
Trimix blends made by topping up helium with air.<sup id=""cite_ref-Scuba_engineer_6-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Scuba_engineer-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"helicopter turn (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Manoeuver in which a horizontally trimmed diver uses small fin movements to rotate on the spot on a vertical axis.
"
"heliox (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliox"" title=""Heliox"">Heliox</a></span></p>
Mixtures of helium and oxygen for use as a breathing gas.<sup id=""cite_ref-ISO13293_7-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ISO13293-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-Scuba_engineer_6-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Scuba_engineer-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"helium (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helium"" title=""Helium"">Helium</a></span></p>
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inert_gas"" title=""Inert gas"">inert gas</a> which is used as a component of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">breathing gas</a> mixtures for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_diving"" title=""Deep diving"">deep diving</a>.
"
"helium analyzer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helium_analyzer"" title=""Helium analyzer"">Helium analyzer</a></span></p>
An instrument used to identify the presence and concentration of helium in a mixture of gases
"
"helium unscrambler (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"helium speech unscrambler (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § speech unscrambler"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#speech_unscrambler"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">speech unscrambler</a></span></span></p>"
"helmet diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#hard_hat_diving""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hard hat diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hard hat diving</span></a></span></p>"
"Henry's law (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Description of the changes in solubility of a given gas in a given liquid as pressure varies.

"
"HID light (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_intensity_discharge"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""High intensity discharge"">High intensity discharge</a> light: Used in cave diving <a href=""#light_head""><span title=""See entry on this page at § light head"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">light heads</span></a> (q.v.).
"
"HIRA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Hazard Identification and Risk Analysis: A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Risk_management"" title=""Risk management"">risk management</a> procedure for identifying hazards and assessing the risk associated with them and ways to reduce the risk to an acceptable level.

"
"Hogarthian configuration (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A scuba combination of backplate, wing, one-piece harness with crotch-strap, regulator arrangement including long-hose primary with a necklaced secondary demand valve, and, if used with twin cylinders, an isolation manifold. Named after <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Hogarth_Main"" title=""William Hogarth Main"">William Hogarth Main</a>, a developer and proponent of the system.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Hog looped (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A scuba configuration where the primary demand valve has a <a href=""#long_hose""><span title=""See entry on this page at § long hose"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">long hose</span></a> which is routed under the right arm, usually tucked under a light battery canister on the waist belt of the harness, and around behind the neck to reach the mouth from the right hand side. Part of the <a href=""#hogarthian_configuration""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Hogarthian configuration"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Hogarthian configuration</span></a> (q.v.).<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hold-back line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"hold-back rigging (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Rigging provided to restrain excessive buoyancy of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lifting_bag"" title=""Lifting bag"">lifting bag</a> when it is attached to the load and inflated.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"homebrew (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Amateur blended <a href=""#mixed_gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mixed gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mixed gas</span></a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hood (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Close-fitting thermal head protection, usually neoprene foam, but also latex on some dry suits.
"
"hook breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § recovery breathing"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#recovery_breathing"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">recovery breathing</a></span></span></p>"
"hooka (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"hookah (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § airline diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#airline_diving"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">airline diving</a></span></span></p>"
"hopcalite (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hopcalite"" title=""Hopcalite"">Hopcalite</a></span></p>
Catalyst sometimes used in breathing air compressor filters to oxidise carbon monoxide to carbon dioxide. Hopcalite is a mixture of manganese oxide, copper oxide and a small amount of silver oxide.
"
"horse collar (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § adjustable buoyancy life jacket"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#adjustable_buoyancy_life_jacket"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">adjustable buoyancy life jacket</a></span><sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></span></p>"
"hose dash size (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Number indicating the bore of a hose in multiples of 1/16"" preceded by a dash. for example a –04 hose, typically used for a pneumofathometer hose would have a nominal bore of <style data-mw-deduplicate=""TemplateStyles:r1020198016"">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class=""frac"" role=""math""><span class=""num"">1</span>&#8260;<span class=""den"">4</span></span> inch (6.4&#160;mm).
"
"hose organiser (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: hose tidy</span></p>
Equipment to position and stabilise a hose, particularly in the context of sidemount or sling mounted scuba cylinders, where the regulator air hoses are stored against the cylinder when not in use.
"
"hot mix (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A breathing gas mixture with a high percentage of oxygen for the depth at which it is used. Using a gas mixture with a high partial pressure of oxygen.
"
"hot water suit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_suit#Hot_water_suits"" title=""Diving suit"">Diving suit#Hot water suits</a></span></p>
A loose fitting wetsuit supplied with heated water through a hose in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver%27s_umbilical"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diver&#39;s umbilical"">diver's umbilical</a>, which links the diver to the surface support. The diver controls the flow rate of the water, allowing them to vary the warmth of the suit.
"
"HP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
High pressure, generally gas pressures in excess of 30&#160;bar. In most of the world a high pressure diving cylinder is a 300&#160;bar cylinder, but in the US it may refer to anything over 3000&#160;psi working pressure. In a diving context gas working pressures do not frequently exceed 300&#160;bar, but pressures in hydraulic systems and high pressure water jetting equipment may be considerably higher.
"
"HPNS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"high-pressure nervous syndrome (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-pressure_nervous_syndrome"" title=""High-pressure nervous syndrome"">High-pressure nervous syndrome</a></span></p>
A neurological and physiological diving disorder that occurs when a diver descends below about 500 feet (150&#160;m) while breathing a helium–oxygen mixture.
"
"HRC (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""#hyperbaric_rescue_capsule""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hyperbaric rescue capsule"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hyperbaric rescue capsule</span></a> 
2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""#hyperbaric_rescue_chamber""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hyperbaric rescue chamber"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hyperbaric rescue chamber</span></a>
"
"HRU (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#hyperbaric_rescue_unit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hyperbaric rescue unit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hyperbaric rescue unit</span></a></span></p>"
"HSE (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#health_and_Safety_Executive""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Health and Safety Executive"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Health and Safety Executive</span></a></span></p>
"
"HUD (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#head-up_display""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Head-up display"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Head-up display</span></a></span></p>"
"H-valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Dual_outlet_valves"" title=""Scuba cylinder valve"">Scuba cylinder valve#Dual outlet valves</a></span></p>
Cylinder valve body with two outlets and two valve mechanisms which can be independently controlled so that two regulator first stages can be fitted. Similar to Y-valve but in configuration where the second valve is parallel to the primary, though the secondary valve can sometimes be swivelled.
"
"hydro (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Slang/abbreviation for <a href=""#hydrostatic_test""><span title=""See entry on this page at § hydrostatic test"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">hydrostatic test</span></a> (q.v.)<sup id=""cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_3-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hydrophobic membrane (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A membrane that is freely permeable to gas but does not allow the passage of water at low pressure differentials.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hydrostatic pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrostatic_pressure"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hydrostatic pressure"">Hydrostatic pressure</a></span></p>
Pressure due to the weight of the water column above a point at depth.
"
"hydrostatic test (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrostatic_test"" title=""Hydrostatic test"">Hydrostatic test</a></span></p>
Non-destructive test to revalidate pressure vessels which uses water as a test medium. The vessel is pressurised to the <span title=""See entry on this page at § test pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#test_pressure"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">test pressure</a></span> (q.v.) and measured for permanent set.
"
"hydreliox (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydreliox"" title=""Hydreliox"">Hydreliox</a></span></p>
Deep diving <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">breathing gas</a> mixture of hydrogen, helium and oxygen.
"
"hydrox (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrox_(breathing_gas)"" title=""Hydrox (breathing gas)"">Hydrox (breathing gas)</a></span></p>
Deep diving <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">breathing gas</a> mixture of hydrogen and oxygen.
"
"hyperbaric evacuation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Evacuation of divers under pressure from a saturation chamber to a hyperbaric rescue craft via a pressurised transfer system.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hyperbaric evacuation system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
System for evacuating divers under pressure from a saturation system in an emergency.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_8-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The whole system set up to provide hyperbaric evacuation, including planning, procedures, equipment used for evacuation, reception facility, contingency plans, possible safe havens and anything else requited for a successful hyperbaric evacuation.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hyperbaric lifeboat (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A lifeboat with a hyperbaric chamber and life support system built into it for evacuating saturation divers in an emergency.
"
"hyperbaric rescue capsule (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A self contained buoyant hyperbaric chamber intended for emergency evacuation of saturation divers under pressure from a platform which has become so dangerous that it is considered safer to put the divers into the sea in the HRC to be picked up by a rescue vessel for transfer to another hyperbaric system for decompression.
"
"hyperbaric rescue chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Normally a pressure vessel adapted to function as a means of hyperbaric evacuation with buoyancy chambers and lifting points, but not fitted in a lifeboat hull.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hyperbaric evacuation unit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"hyperbaric rescue unit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""HEU"", ""HRU""</span></p>
Generic term for the unit provided to evacuate divers from a saturation system. It may be an <a href=""#hRC""><span title=""See entry on this page at § HRC"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">HRC</span></a> or a <span title=""See entry on this page at § SPHL"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#SPHL"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">SPHL</a></span> or some other suitable pressure vessel.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hypercapnia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypercapnia"" title=""Hypercapnia"">Hypercapnia</a></span></p>
Excessive level of carbon dioxide in the body.
"
"hyperfilter (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving"" title=""Gas blending for scuba diving"">Gas blending for scuba diving#</a></span></p>
Additional filter to produce air of oxygen compatible quality, usually for partial pressure gas blending. This may be built into the filling system or temporarily connected when required.
"
"hyperoxic linearity (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Property of an oxygen sensor to produce linear output at partial pressures above the highest calibration point.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"hyperventilation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;A deliberate <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperventilation"" title=""Hyperventilation"">deep breathing</a> to reduce blood carbon dioxide level to extend the duration of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_diving"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Free diving"">free dive</a>.
2.&#160;&#160;<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperventilation"" title=""Hyperventilation"">Rapid breathing</a> as the body's response to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypercapnia"" title=""Hypercapnia"">hypercapnia</a>.
3.&#160;&#160;Rapid, often shallow breathing, associated with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panic"" title=""Panic"">panic</a>.
"
"hyperventilation-induced blackout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § underwater blackout syndrome"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#underwater_blackout_syndrome"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">underwater blackout syndrome</a></span>
"
"hypocapnia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypocapnia"" title=""Hypocapnia"">Hypocapnia</a></span></p>
Abnormally low tissue and blood carbon dioxide concentration.
"
"hypothermia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypothermia"" title=""Hypothermia"">Hypothermia</a></span></p>
A lowering of core body temperature, usually due to heat loss.
"
"hypoxia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypoxia_(medical)"" title=""Hypoxia (medical)"">Hypoxia (medical)</a></span></p>
Abnormally low tissue oxygen concentration: Insufficient oxygen in the body to support normal activities or consciousness.
"
"hypoxic training (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
prolonged underwater distance swimming or extended breath-hold intervals.<sup id=""cite_ref-Boyd_et_al_2015_9-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Boyd_et_al_2015-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>


"
"IAOGP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#international_Association_of_Oil_and_Gas_Producers""><span title=""See entry on this page at § International Association of Oil and Gas Producers"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">International Association of Oil and Gas Producers</span></a></span></p>"
"ICD (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#isobaric_counterdiffusion""><span title=""See entry on this page at § isobaric counterdiffusion"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">isobaric counterdiffusion</span></a></span></p>"
"IDRCF (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"IDRF (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Diving_Regulators_and_Certifiers_Forum"" title=""International Diving Regulators and Certifiers Forum"">International Diving Regulators and Certifiers Forum</a>, previously International Diving Regulators Forum. A voluntary group of diving regulators and certifying agencies formed to work together toward mutual recognition and to identify and implement best practices in diver training with the object of harmonizing cross border diver training standards outside Europe. Members include Australia, Canada, France, Norway, South Africa and United Kingdom.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2010b_10-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2010b-10"">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
"
"IDSA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Diving_Schools_Association"" title=""International Diving Schools Association"">International Diving Schools Association</a>: Formed with the primary purpose of developing common internationional diving standards for all occupational divers, Offshore, Inshore and Inland, and specialist related non-diving qualifications e.g. Supervisor, DMT and LST.<sup id=""cite_ref-IDSA_11-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IDSA-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
"
"IMCA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Marine_Contractors_Association"" title=""International Marine Contractors Association"">International Marine Contractors Association</a>.</span></p>
International trade association for the marine contracting industry.
"
"inert gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Inert_gas_uptake_(Ingassing)"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Inert gas uptake (Ingassing)</a></span></p>
A gas which is not metabolically active, used to dilute the breathing gas.
"
"ingassing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Inert_gas_uptake_(Ingassing)"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Inert gas uptake (Ingassing)</a></span></p>
Inert gas uptake in body tissues during a dive or other hyperbaric exposure.
"
"inherent unsaturation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Inherent_unsaturation"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Inherent unsaturation</a></span></p>
Metabolic reduction of total gas pressure in the tissues.
"
"inshore diver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Colloquial term for a diver who works on inland dive sites or coastal waters not associated with the oil and gas industry. Also referred to as ""civils"" as much of this work is connected with civil engineering works.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_12-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
"
"integrated weight system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Any system for carrying dive weights on the buoyancy compensator or diving safety harness, avoiding the use of a separate weight harness or weightbelt.
"
"internal condition of cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The state of the internal surface of a cylinder regarding corrosion, contamination and cracking.
"
"interstitial emphysema (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Gas trapped in the spaces between organs after lung <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barotrauma"" title=""Barotrauma"">barotrauma</a>.
"
"International Association of Oil and Gas Producers (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Association_of_Oil_and_Gas_Producers"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""International Association of Oil and Gas Producers"">International Association of Oil and Gas Producers</a></span></p>
The international forum of the oil and gas producing industry.
"
"inverter line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § tripping line"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#tripping_line"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">tripping line</a></span></span></p>"
"in-water recompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In-water_recompression"" title=""In-water recompression"">In-water recompression</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperbaric_treatment_schedules#In-water_recompression_schedules"" title=""Hyperbaric treatment schedules"">Hyperbaric treatment schedules#In-water recompression schedules</a></span></p>
Recompression of a diver by returning to a specified depth in the water, followed by decompression on a specified gas, commonly oxygen, as treatment for decompression sickness or as prophylaxis for incomplete or missed decompression after a dive.
"
"IP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Intermediate Pressure, or Interstage Pressure. The reduced pressure between the first and second stages of a diving regulator. Also referred to as LP (Low Pressure) in this context.
"
"isobaric blackout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § constant depth blackout"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#constant_depth_blackout"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">constant depth blackout</a></span></span></p>"
"isobaric counterdiffusion (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isobaric_counterdiffusion"" title=""Isobaric counterdiffusion"">Isobaric counterdiffusion</a></span></p>
The diffusion of gases in opposite directions caused by a change in the composition of the external ambient gas or breathing gas without change in the ambient pressure.
"
"isolation manifold (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Connection between two scuba cylinders which when open allows free flow of gas in both directions between the cylinders, but has an isolation valve to block this flow.
"
"isolation valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
valve in an isolation manifold (q.v.) used to close the gas passage through the manifold and isolate the contents of the two cylinders. Used to prevent a leak on one cylinder from causing the other cylinder to also lose gas.


"
"jackstay (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jackstay#Diving_jackstay"" title=""Jackstay"">Jackstay#Diving jackstay</a></span></p>
A line secured at both ends to serve as a support<sup id=""cite_ref-Oxford_Jackstay_13-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Oxford_Jackstay-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> or guide.
"
"jackstay search (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See:<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_searches#Jackstay_search"" title=""Underwater searches"">Underwater searches#Jackstay search</a></span></p>
Underwater search techniques using one or more jackstays to guide the searcher.
"
"jack-up rig (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jackup_rig"" title=""Jackup rig"">Jackup rig</a></span></p>
A type of mobile platform that consists of a buoyant hull fitted with a number of movable legs, capable of raising its hull over the surface of sea. The buoyant hull enables transportation of the unit and all attached machinery to a desired location. Once on location the hull is raised to the required elevation above the sea surface on its legs supported by the sea bed.
"
"J-cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Bulk gas storage cylinder with internal volume 50 litres.

"
"Jersey upline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § upline"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#upline"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">upline</a></span></span></p>
"
"JIC fitting (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JIC_fitting"" title=""JIC fitting"">JIC fitting</a></span></p>
A type of pipe and hose fitting with a 37-degree flare seating surface. Commonly used in umbilical hose connections.
"
"JIM suit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JIM_suit"" title=""JIM suit"">JIM suit</a></span></p>
An atmospheric diving suit manufactured by <a href=""/w/index.php?title=Underwater_Marine_Equipment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Underwater Marine Equipment (page does not exist)"">Underwater Marine Equipment</a> Limited.

"
"jocking strap (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
webbing strap system used with diving helmets to hold the helmet assembly down on the diver to prevent buoyancy lifting it when underwater.
"
"Jonline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonline"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Jonline"">Jonline</a></span></p>
A short line used to connect to a shotline or anchor line, allowing the diver to move a short horizontal distance away to decompress. The line helps compensate for vertical movement in the anchor line or shot line due to waves.<sup id=""cite_ref-shipwreckexpo_14-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-shipwreckexpo-14"">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
"
"job safety analysis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"JSA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Job_safety_analysis"" title=""Job safety analysis"">Job safety analysis</a></span></p>
A procedure to integrate health and safety principles and practices into a particular task or job. Each basic step of the job analysed to identify potential hazards and controls for each hazard.
"
"J-search (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_searches#Variations_on_the_jackstay_search"" title=""Underwater searches"">Underwater searches#Variations on the jackstay search</a></span></p>
A variation on the movable jackstay search suitable for a single diver.

"
"jump (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A path from a main guideline to another which is not in contact
"
"jump camera (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A camera mounted on a frame, which when lowered to the bottom of a body of water, takes a photograph, usually of the bottom under the camera. The frame constrains the camera to a fixed camera to subject distance, resulting in photographs of uniformly sized areas of bottom, equivalent to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrat"" title=""Quadrat"">quadrats</a>.
"
"Jump jacket (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Harness_with_buoyancy_compensation"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">harness</a> with integral buoyancy jacket specifically designed for commercial diving work with helmets and bells.<sup id=""cite_ref-Jump_Jacket_15-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Jump_Jacket-15"">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
"
"jump line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_diving"" title=""Cave diving"">Cave diving</a></span></p>
A short <span title=""See entry on this page at § "" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">error: non-alphabetic term</span> used to connect between two permanent lines that are not in contact. May also be used to search for the other end of a break in a cave line and repair the break
"
"jump reel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"jump spool (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A reel or spool with a relatively short line intended to be used as a jump line (q.v.).
"
"J-valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Reserve_valves"" title=""Scuba cylinder valve"">Scuba cylinder valve#Reserve valves</a></span></p>
Scuba cylinder valve with lever operated reserve mechanism.<sup id=""cite_ref-Basic_Scuba_16-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Basic_Scuba-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>


"
"kayak diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kayak_diving"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Kayak diving"">Kayak diving</a></span></p>
Diving from a special purpose kayak used to get to the site where the distance from a suitable entry and exit point is inconvenient for shore diving.
"
"K-cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Bulk high pressure gas storage cylinder size designation (approximately 50 litres internal volume)
"
"Kelly (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"Kelly tube (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#tube""><span title=""See entry on this page at § tube"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">tube</span></a></span></p>"
"K-valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Plain_valves"" title=""Scuba cylinder valve"">Scuba cylinder valve#Plain valves</a></span></p>
Scuba cylinder valve without reserve mechanism.


"
"lanyard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lanyard"" title=""Lanyard"">Lanyard</a></span></p>
A piece of cordage used to secure or lower things; usually it is used where there is a risk of losing the object
"
"LARS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#launch_and_Recovery_System""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Launch and Recovery System"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Launch and Recovery System</span></a></span></p>"
"laryngospasm (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laryngospasm"" title=""Laryngospasm"">Laryngospasm</a></span></p>
An uncontrolled or involuntary muscular contraction (spasm) of the laryngeal cords which causes a partial blocking of breathing in, while breathing out remains easier.
"
"latent hypoxia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
While freediving, an arterial oxygen partial pressure which is sufficient to sustain consciousness at depth, but when ascending drops to hyoxic levels due to the reduction of ambient pressure, associated with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freediving_blackout#Blackout_on_ascent"" title=""Freediving blackout"">ascent blackout</a>.
"
"launch and recovery system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Mechanised system for lowering a diving bell, diving stage, submersible or ROV from a vessel, offshore platform, dockside or other platform, and lifting it back on board.
"
"lay barge (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: <b>pipelay barge</b></span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pipe-laying_ship"" title=""Pipe-laying ship"">Pipe-laying ship</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Submarine_pipeline"" title=""Submarine pipeline"">Submarine pipeline</a></span></p>
Barge on which pipeline sections are assembled, welded and laid on the seabed as the barge is moved forward.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_12-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
"
"lay line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"laying line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_diving#Line_management"" title=""Cave diving"">Cave diving#Line management</a></span></p>
To run line (unreel under light tension while advancing) and <a href=""#placement""><span title=""See entry on this page at § placement"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">place it</span></a>
"
"lazy shot (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_shot#Lazy_shot"" title=""Diving shot"">Diving shot#Lazy shot</a></span></p>
A <span title=""See entry on this page at § shot line"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#shot_line"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">shot line</a></span> (q.v.) which does not reach the bottom
"
"LDS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Local dive shop. A retailer of recreational diving equipment, which may also sell cylinder fills, service equipment, provide training or book or organise recreational dives for customers.

"
"LED (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_emitting_diode"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Light emitting diode"">Light emitting diode</a></span></p> 
A semiconductor device for producing light from an electrical current commonly used in dive lights.
"
"lens port (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
Transparent window on an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_camera_housing"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Underwater camera housing"">underwater camera housing</a> through which light reaches the lens.

"
"LID (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#low_impact_diving""><span title=""See entry on this page at § low impact diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">low impact diving</span></a></span></p>"
"lifeline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lifeline_(diving)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Lifeline (diving)"">Lifeline (diving)</a></span></p>
A line connected securely to the diver at one end and anchored at the other end at the diving control point, which is handled by a line tender, and is used to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_communications#Rope_signals"" title=""Diver communications"">communicate</a> with the diver and provide a means of finding the diver for a surface standby diver, and for assisting the diver to the surface and back to the control point if necessary.
"
"life support (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"life support system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life-support_system#Underwater_and_saturation_diving_habitats"" title=""Life-support system"">Life-support system#Underwater and saturation diving habitats</a></span></p>
Equipment vital to the short term survival of the diver. Most notably the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">breathing gas</a> supply, and for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving"" title=""Saturation diving"">saturation diving</a>, equipment for providing a correctly pressurised environment. In some cases thermoregulatory equipment is also considered life support, and in saturation diving, all of the peripheral systems essential to maintaining a habitable saturation system.
"
"life support package (LSP) (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""fly-away package""</span></p>
A collection of equipment and supplies kept in a suitable location such that when a hyperbaric rescue chamber or self-propelled hyperbaric lifeboat arrives at the safe haven it is available to support or complete decompression by using the LSP components to maintain the decompression environment by way of power, gas mixtures, heating and cooling.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"life support supervisor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A senior life support technician (q.v.) appointed by the diving contractor to supervise the operation of saturation life-support systems.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_8-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"life support technician (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""LST""</span></p>
A person who operates and maintains the life support systems of a saturation diving system.
"
"lift bag (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"lifting bag (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lifting_bag"" title=""Lifting bag"">Lifting bag</a></span></p>
A robust and air-tight bag with straps, which is used to lift heavy objects underwater by means of the bag's buoyancy when filled with air.
"
"light (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Alternative term for a <span title=""See entry on this page at § viewport"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#viewport"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">viewport</a></span> of a <span title=""See entry on this page at § standard diving helmet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#standard_diving_helmet"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">standard diving helmet</a></span>.
"
"light head (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The part of a <span title=""See entry on this page at § canister light"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#canister_light"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">canister light</a></span> (q.v.) which emits light, and is held in the hand or mounted on the helmet.
"
"lightweight helmet (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_helmet#Lightweight_demand_helmets"" title=""Diving helmet"">Diving helmet#Lightweight demand helmets</a></span></p>
Low volume, close fitting diving helmet, usually with demand valve. Neutrally buoyant, and moves with the diver's head.
"
"line marker (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Line_arrows"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Line arrows"">Line arrows</a>, <span title=""See entry on this page at § cookies"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#cookies"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">cookies</a></span> and sometimes clothes pegs. Tags used to indicate the direction to an exit, midway point between exits, jumps and personal markers to identify divers on a guide line in an <a href=""#overhead_environment""><span title=""See entry on this page at § overhead environment"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">overhead environment</span></a>.
"
"line tender (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § diver&#39;s attendant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diver&#39;s_attendant"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diver's attendant</a></span></span></p>"
"line trap (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Narrow gap where the guide line passes but divers can not get through.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_2-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"lipid pneumonia (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lipid_pneumonia"" title=""Lipid pneumonia"">Lipid pneumonia</a></span></p>
A lung inflammation (pneumonia) that develops when lipids enter the bronchial tree
"
"live-aboard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liveaboard"" title=""Liveaboard"">Liveaboard</a></span></p>
A large boat which provides transport, accommodation and services for vacationing recreational divers
"
"live-boating (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Diving from a boat which is under way (not moored). The major implication is that the engines will be running and propellers or thrusters may be engaged while divers are in the water, a significant hazard.
2.&#160;&#160;(offshore diving) Diving from a vessel underway, making way, but not using dynamic positioning. In offshore diving, diving from a DPV is not considered live-boating.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>

"
"lock (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""air-lock"", ""airlock"" and ""air lock""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airlock"" title=""Airlock"">Airlock</a></span></p>
Compartment of a hyperbaric habitat or chamber which can be entered through two or more openings which can be closed and sealed, and the pressure adjusted relative to the adjacent chambers. Used to transfer personnel or equipment between areas of different pressure.
"
"lock-in (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Enter a pressurised environment through an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airlock"" title=""Airlock"">airlock</a>
"
"lock-off (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Disconnect a mobile hyperbaric chamber from another hyperbaric chamber after sealing the doors between them and venting the connection space.
"
"lock-off time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The time at which a diving bell under pressure is locked off (disconnected) from the compression chamber(s) on deck.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"lock-on (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Connect a mobile hyperbaric chamber to another hyperbaric chamber so that the pressures can be equalised to allow <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transfer_under_pressure"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Transfer under pressure"">transfer under pressure</a> between them.
"
"Lock-on time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The time at which a diving bell under pressure is locked on (reconnected) ready for equalisation to the compression chamber(s) on deck.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"lock-out (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Exit from a pressurised environment through an air-lock
"
"lockout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lockout%E2%80%93tagout"" title=""Lockout–tagout"">Lockout–tagout</a></span></p>
Safety procedure when working on a hazardous energy source.<sup id=""cite_ref-OSHA_Lockout_17-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-OSHA_Lockout-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
"
"lockout mode (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_computer#Lockout_mode"" title=""Dive computer"">Dive computer#Lockout mode</a></span></p> 
Factory set function of some dive computers which disables the computer from decompression calculation after a violation of a factory set limit for depth, decompression ceiling or other violation of approved operating range for a period sufficient for tissues to fully desaturate if the diver survives uninjured. Some models will lockout immediately, usually to gauge mode which provides depth and time data but no decompression information, leaving the diver without some safety-critical information, others will continue to provide the diver with best estimate decompression information until the end of the dive.
"
"log book (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Record of dives kept as proof of experience. Optional for recreational divers, but legally required for professional divers in many jurisdictions.
"
"long hose (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
5 ft to 7 ft interstage hose used on one of the regulators used by cave and other technical divers, which allows gas sharing through narrow spaces where the divers must pass through in single file.
"
"longshore current (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Longshore_current"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Longshore current"">Longshore current</a></span></p>
Mass transport of water along a shoreline, often due to wave action at an angle to the shoreline.
"
"loop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""breathing loop""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Concentric_bellows_counterlungs"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Concentric bellows counterlungs</a></span></p>
The circuit in a rebreather through which the breathing gas passes during a breathing cycle.
"
"loop mix (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"loop mixture (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
1.&#160;&#160;The breathing gas in the loop of a rebreather. 
2.&#160;&#160;Composition of the breathing gas in the loop of a rebreather, usually after passing through the scrubber, where it is analysed for oxygen partial pressure.
"
"loop volume (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Volume of the breathing loop of a rebreather.
"
"loop vent valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
An over-pressure relief valve in a rebreather loop.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"lost buddy drill (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"lost buddy procedure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
