standardised procedure followed when a diver realises that their buddy is not where they should be. Procedures may vary depending on the circumstances and training organisations.
"
"lost line drill (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"lost line procedure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Standardised procedure to be followed when the guideline to the surface is lost in a penetration dive, often in conditions of low visibility and darkness.
"
"low impact diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_impact_diving"" title=""Low impact diving"">Low impact diving</a></span></p>
Diving with low environmental impact. Diving in a way that avoids contact with or disturbance of sensitive organisms and adversely affecting the environment. Usually applied to recreational diving.
"
"low pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Also: ""intermediate pressure""<br />
In diving, low pressure usually refers to the gas pressure provided from the first stage regulator to the demand valve for reduction to ambient pressure, the pressure provided by a low-pressure breathing air compressor to the gas panel for supply to the diver's umbilical or airline, or the pressure supplied to buoyancy compensator, dry suit or supply for lift bag inflation gas or pneumatic tools. These pressures are generally less than 30 bar, and in the case of scuba regulators are usually about 9 to 11 bar above ambient pressure.
2.&#160;&#160;In the context of diving cylinders, in the US, a low pressure cylinder has a working pressure below 2,500 pounds per square inch (170&#160;bar)
"
"low visibility (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"low viz (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_vision#Low_visibility"" title=""Underwater vision"">Underwater vision#Low visibility</a></span></p>
Water where, regardless of illumination, the distance over which objects can be seen is small. It is a term with highly variable and often relative meaning, but it would be almost universally accepted that less than 0.5 metres (1.6&#160;ft) visibility would be considered low visibility. For operational purposes NOAA define it as ""When visual contact with the dive buddy can no longer be maintained"", and DAN Southern Africa  suggest less than 3 metres (9.8&#160;ft).<sup id=""cite_ref-Christou_18-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Christou-18"">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-NOAA_Low_visibility_19-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-NOAA_Low_visibility-19"">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
"
"LP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#low_pressure""><span title=""See entry on this page at § low pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">low pressure</span></a></span></p>"
"LP compressor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Low-pressure compressor. Used for breathing air supply for surface supplied air diving.
"
"LP cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Low-pressure cylinder (US) with working pressure less than 2,500 pounds per square inch (170&#160;bar).
"
"LP port (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Opening on the first stage of a regulator through which regulated gas is supplied at low/intermediate pressure.
"
"LST (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#life_support_technician""><span title=""See entry on this page at § life support technician"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">life support technician</span></a></span></p>
"
"lung packing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"lung-packing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § glossopharangeal insufflation"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#glossopharangeal_insufflation"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">glossopharangeal insufflation</a></span></span></p>

"
"mammalian diving reflex (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""diving response""</span></p>
A reflex response to breathhold and chilling of the face diving response expressed by the cardiovascular system, which exhibits hypertension, bradycardia, oxygen conservation, arrhythmias, and contraction of the spleen.<sup id=""cite_ref-Lindholm_and_Lundgren_2009_20-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Lindholm_and_Lundgren_2009-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
"
"manifold (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § twin cylinder manifold"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#twin_cylinder_manifold"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">twin cylinder manifold</a></span></span></p>"
"manifold (breathing gas supply) (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_panel"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Gas panel"">gas panel</a>""</span></p>
Panel for the distribution of diver breathing gas.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-11"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"manifold operator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""gas man""</span></p>
A person such as a life support technician (LST), diving supervisor, or mixed-gas diver, who is designated to perform the duties of gas distribution on a surface-supplied mixed gas (HeO<sub>2</sub>) diving operation, who is competent in the operation of the manifold and whose primary responsibility is to operate the manifold.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-12"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"manual bypass valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A valve that allows the diver to manually inject gas into the breathing loop of a rebreather, bypassing the valve operated by the control system.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"manual closed circuit rebreather (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""mCCR"", ""MCCR"". See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § diver controlled closed circuit rebreather"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diver_controlled_closed_circuit_rebreather"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diver controlled closed circuit rebreather</a></span></span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Closed_circuit_mixed_gas_rebreathers"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Closed circuit mixed gas rebreathers</a></span></p>
A closed circuit rebreather which relies on the diver to monitor and control the gas mixture in the loop.
"
"manufacturing standard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""manufacturing code""</span></p>
Set of design and manufacturing rules intended to produce uniform and safe products by several manufacturers in an industry.
"
"Marsh Marine connector (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
One of the popular underwater plug connector systems for diver communications cables.<sup id=""cite_ref-Marsh_Marine_21-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Marsh_Marine-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Martini's law (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Rough rule of thumb for estimating <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis"" title=""Nitrogen narcosis"">nitrogen narcosis</a> effects based on equivalence to consumption of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_martini"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Dry martini"">dry martinis</a>: Variously quoted as one martini per 10&#160;m or one martini per 50&#160;ft depth.
"
"master link (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
(<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rigging_(material_handling)"" title=""Rigging (material handling)"">Rigging</a>): The large heavy duty link to which the legs of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chain_sling"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Chain sling"">chain sling</a> are attached, and which is the attachment point on the sling for the lifting hook or shackle
"
"maze cave (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Cave structure characterised by multiple branches and changes in direction.
"
"mCCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"MCCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#manual_closed_circuit_rebreather""><span title=""See entry on this page at § manual closed circuit rebreather"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">manual closed circuit rebreather</span></a></span></p>
"
"metres sea water (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metres_sea_water"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Metres sea water"">metres sea water</a></span></p>
Unit of pressure equal to 1/10 bar. Not a linear measure of depth.<sup id=""cite_ref-NORSOK_U100_22-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-NORSOK_U100-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>

"
"microbubbles (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Microscopic bubbles which are not detectable by ultrasound or Doppler ultrasound, yet can affect the likelihood of DCS by slowing off-gassing.<sup id=""cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_23-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-23"">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
"
"micronuclei (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Microscopic cavities that function as bubble seeds by absorbing dissolved gas.<sup id=""cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_23-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-23"">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
"
"mid-water (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" "
"midwater (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Significantly distant from both the bottom and the surface.
"
"medical lock (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Small <a href=""#lock""><span title=""See entry on this page at § lock"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">lock</span></a> on a decompression chamber used for transfer of medical equipment and other supplies into and out of the chamber while the chamber remains under pressure.
"
"mix (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Short for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)"" title=""Trimix (breathing gas)"">trimix</a> breathing gas
"
"mixed gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">Breathing gas</a> for diving other than air, but usually implies a helium based mixture.
"
"mixed mode diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A mixed mode dive team is a buddy team where the divers use different modes of diving on the same dive, such as one diver on open circuit and the other on rebreather<sup id=""cite_ref-Seymour_2016_24-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Seymour_2016-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> 
"
"mixed platform diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Mixed platform rebreather diving refers to the use of different makes or models of rebreather on the same dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-Seymour_2016_24-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Seymour_2016-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>

"
"mobile diving system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""portable diving system""</span></p>
A <span title=""See entry on this page at § diving system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_system"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diving system</a></span> (q.v.) which is installed on a vessel or installation on a temporary basis and that is not fixed, i.e. can be demobilised, transported and re-sited. Includes surface supplied air, nitrox, heliox and saturation diving systems.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-13"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"mobile offshore drilling unit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A generic term for several classes of self-contained floatable or floating drilling rigs such as drilling vessels, semisubmersibles, submersibles, jack-ups, and similar facilities that can be moved without substantial effort. These facilities may have self-propulsion equipment on board and may require dynamic positioning equipment or mooring systems to maintain their position.<sup id=""cite_ref-MODU_25-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-MODU-25"">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
"
"MOD (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximum_operating_depth"" title=""Maximum operating depth"">Maximum operating depth</a>:  Limiting depth for safety based on <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partial_pressure"" title=""Partial pressure"">partial pressure</a> of oxygen of a breathing gas mixture.
"
"modified flutter kick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Version of the <span title=""See entry on this page at § flutter kick"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#flutter_kick"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">flutter kick</a></span> finning style which reduces risk of silting by directing thrust more directly backwards. Two techniques exist: One version has the legs bent at the knees so that the fins are placed relatively high and on average are aligned more horizontally. The other version has one fin stationary below the moving fin to deflect downwash.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_2-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Leg movement is restrained, and ankle movement used for precision manoeuvring.
"
"modified frog kick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Version of the <span title=""See entry on this page at § frog kick"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#frog_kick"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">frog kick</a></span> finning style which reduces risk of silting by directing thrust more directly backwards. Performed with bent knees and fins raised above the line of the torso.
"
"MODU (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#mobile_offshore_drilling_unit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § mobile offshore drilling unit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">mobile offshore drilling unit</span></a></span></p>"
"monofin (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monofin"" title=""Monofin"">Monofin</a></span></p>
A type of swimfin typically used in finswimming and free-diving. It consists of a single surface attached to footpockets for both of the diver's feet.
"
"molecular sieve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_sieve"" title=""Molecular sieve"">Molecular sieve</a></span></p>
Material containing tiny pores of a precise and uniform size that is used as an adsorbent for gases and liquids. Molecules small enough to pass through the pores are absorbed while larger molecules are not. It is different from a common filter in that it operates on a molecular level.
"
"monkey diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Terminology"" title=""Sidemount diving"">Sidemount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
The use of <span title=""See entry on this page at § sidemount"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#sidemount"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">sidemount</a></span> configuration and procedures with a single cylinder.
"
"moonpool (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moonpool"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Moonpool"">Moonpool</a></span></p>
An opening in the floor or base of the hull, platform, underwater habitat, or chamber, giving access to the water below.
"
"msw (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#metres_sea_water""><span title=""See entry on this page at § metres sea water"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">metres sea water</span></a></span></p>
"
"multi-level dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""multilevel dive"", ""multi level dive""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-level_dive"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Multi-level dive"">Multi-level dive</a></span></p>
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_profile"" title=""Dive profile"">dive profile</a> in which the diver remains in more than one distinct depth ranges (excluding decompression stops) for a significant period before beginning final ascent to the surface.
"
"multiple stage compressor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compressor#Reciprocating_compressors"" title=""Compressor"">Compressor#Reciprocating compressors</a></span></p>
Compressor in which gases are compressed more than once, usually with cooling between stages. Used to improve efficiency and reduce temperatures.
"
"mung (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A brown organic deposit usually found on the ceilings of caves which is easily dislodged by diver's exhaust bubbles and then drifts down through the water.
"
"mushroom valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A rubber non-return valve flap which is circular or oval, with a stem in the middle to attach it to the holder in the centre of the grating over the orifice.
"
"M-value (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#M-values"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#M-values</a></span></p>
At a given ambient pressure, the M-value is the maximum theoretical value of absolute inert gas pressure that a tissue compartment can take without presenting symptoms of decompression sickness.


"
"NACD (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Association_for_Cave_Diving"" title=""National Association for Cave Diving"">National Association for Cave Diving</a>
"
"narcs (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#nitrogen_narcosis""><span title=""See entry on this page at § nitrogen narcosis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">nitrogen narcosis</span></a></span></p>"
"Navy Experimental Diving Unit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navy_Experimental_Diving_Unit"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Navy Experimental Diving Unit"">Navy Experimental Diving Unit</a></span></p> 
The United States Navy Experimental Diving Unit, the primary source of diving and hyperbaric operational guidance for the US Navy, located in Florida
"
"Navy SEAL (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Navy_Seals"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""U.S. Navy Seals"">U.S. Navy Seals</a></span></p>
A US Navy trained combat diver.
"
"NDL (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#no_decompression_limit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § No decompression limit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">No decompression limit</span></a></span></p>
"
"neck dam (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The lower part of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_helmet#Lightweight_demand_helmets"" title=""Diving helmet"">lightweight diving helmet</a> which includes a neoprene or latex neck seal similar to the neck seal on a dry suit, to prevent ingress of water. The alternative is to clamp the helmet to the diver's <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drysuit"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Drysuit"">drysuit</a>.
"
"necklace (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Bungee loop attached to the secondary regulator second stage, worn around the neck to store the secondary close under the chin, where it is protected and the diver is immediately aware of a free-flow. With a little adjustment and practice it is possible to pick it up by head and mouth movement alone, not needing use of a hand. The bungee is attached to the second stage by a breakaway connection, often a close-fitting loop over the mouthpiece, so that it can be moved away from the diver's head in an emergency without disturbing the primary second stage or the mask.
"
"neck thread (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Cylinder_neck"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Cylinder neck</a></span></p>
Internal screw thread in the bore of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#cylinder_neck"" title=""Diving cylinder"">cylinder neck</a> to fit a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#The_cylinder_valve"" title=""Diving cylinder"">cylinder valve</a>, which controls flow of gas into and out of the cylinder.
"
"NEDU (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#navy_Experimental_Diving_Unit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Navy Experimental Diving Unit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Navy Experimental Diving Unit</span></a></span></p>"
"negative buoyancy (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: just ""negative"" in context</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also <span title=""See entry on this page at § diving heavy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_heavy"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diving heavy</a></span></span></p> 
Buoyancy less than weight. Insufficient upward force due to buoyancy to keep afloat or remain at constant depth
"
"negative buoyancy entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"negatively buoyant entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"negative entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries_and_exits"" title=""Scuba skills"">Scuba skills#Entries and exits</a></span></p>
Entry into the water in a buoyancy condition that will sink by default. When intentional, generally after reducing buoyancy of BC and, if applicable, dry suit by venting to ensure that the diver will not float back to the surface, but will continue to descend.
"
"negative pressure breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"negative static lung load (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_physiology_of_underwater_diving#Positive_and_negative_pressure_breathing"" title=""Human physiology of underwater diving"">Human physiology of underwater diving#Positive and negative pressure breathing</a></span></p>
Breathing against an external pressure slightly less than the relaxed pressure in the lungs. More effort is needed to inhale, less to exhale. This can occur when using back mounted counterlungs on a rebreather, in a steep head up position with a single-hose demand valve, or when snorkelling.
"
"neo-Haldanian (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""neo-Haldanean""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Critical_difference_hypothesis"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Critical difference hypothesis</a></span></p>
Decompression models based on later modifications of the principles described by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Scott_Haldane"" title=""John Scott Haldane"">John Scott Haldane</a>.
"
"neoprene (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neoprene"" title=""Neoprene"">Neoprene</a></span></p>
Synthetic elastomer used in the form of foamed sheets as the material for most <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wetsuit"" title=""Wetsuit"">wetsuits</a> and some <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drysuit"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Drysuit"">drysuits</a>.
"
"neutral buoyancy (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buoyancy"" title=""Buoyancy"">Buoyancy</a></span></p>
Having a fully immersed buoyancy exactly equal to weight, so that the forces are balanced and the person or object statically remains at a constant depth. Effectively average density is equal to that of the surrounding fluid medium. The state of neutral buoyancy is typically <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metastable"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Metastable"">metastable</a> for a compressible system.
"
"Newtsuit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newtsuit"" title=""Newtsuit"">Newtsuit</a></span></p>
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_diving_suit"" title=""Atmospheric diving suit"">atmospheric diving suit</a> designed and originally built by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phil_Nuytten"" title=""Phil Nuytten"">Phil Nuytten</a>.
"
"net cutter (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A handle with a hooked blade used to cut netting or cordage to free the diver from entanglement
"
"NFCI (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-freezing_cold_injury"" title=""Non-freezing cold injury"">Non-freezing cold injury</a>: Permanent tissue damage due to low temperature exposure without any freezing damage.

"
"niggles (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness#Signs_and_symptoms"" title=""Decompression sickness"">Decompression sickness#Signs and symptoms</a></span></p>
Minor symptoms characteristic of mild decompression sickness.
"
"night diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Night_diving"" title=""Night diving"">Night diving</a></span></p>
Diving during the hours of darkness.
"
"NiMH (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nickel-metal_hydride"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Nickel-metal hydride"">Nickel-metal hydride</a>. A technology for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rechargeable_battery"" title=""Rechargeable battery"">rechargeable battery</a> cells.
"
"nitrile (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrile_rubber"" title=""Nitrile rubber"">Nitrile rubber</a></span></p>
A synthetic <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elastomer"" title=""Elastomer"">elastomer</a> used for most standard <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/O-ring"" title=""O-ring"">O-ring</a> seals.
"
"nitrogen (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen"" title=""Nitrogen"">Nitrogen</a></span></p>
The major component gas of air and many <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">breathing gas</a> mixtures used in diving. Important in diving as an active agent in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis"" title=""Nitrogen narcosis"">nitrogen narcosis</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a>.
"
"nitrogen narcosis (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis"" title=""Nitrogen narcosis"">Nitrogen narcosis</a></span></p>
Also known as narcs, inert gas narcosis, raptures of the deep, Martini effect: A reversible alteration in consciousness that occurs while breathing gases containing nitrogen under elevated partial pressure similar to alcohol intoxication or nitrous oxide inhalation, and can occur during shallow dives, but usually does not become noticeable until greater depths, beyond 30 meters.
"
"nitrox (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""Enriched Air Nitrox (EAN)""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrox"" title=""Nitrox"">Nitrox</a></span></p>
Mixture of nitrogen and oxygen for use as breathing gas. Usually with oxygen percentage higher than air.
"
"nitrox stick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving#Mixing_the_gases"" title=""Gas blending for scuba diving"">Gas blending for scuba diving#Mixing the gases</a></span></p>
A mixing tube used to blend oxygen with air before compressing to make nitrox breathing gas.
"
"NOAA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration"" title=""National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration"">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (US)
"
"no decompression limit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#No_decompression_limit"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#No decompression limit</a></span></p>
No decompression limit. The maximum time which a diver can remain at a specified depth without incurring a stage decompression obligation in terms of the specified decompression tables or algorithm.
"
"nominal capacity (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Volume of <span title=""See entry on this page at § free gas volume"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#free_gas_volume"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">free gas</a></span> contained by a scuba cylinder when filled to <span title=""See entry on this page at § charging pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#charging_pressure"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">charging pressure</a></span> at constant temperature.
"
"No-mount diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Side_mount_diving#Terminology"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Side mount diving"">Side mount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
A specialized overhead-environment strategy for dealing with particularly tight restrictions which may involve divers wearing a very basic harness or simply hand-carrying cylinders.
"
"normoxic (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;A breathing gas mixture with oxygen content approximating atmospheric air.
2.&#160;&#160;A breathing gas for diving which contains sufficient oxygen to minimise risk of hypoxia at atmospheric pressure.
"
"NSS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Speleological_Society"" title=""National Speleological Society"">National Speleological Society</a>
"
"nystagmus (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nystagmus"" title=""Nystagmus"">Nystagmus</a></span></p>
An oscillation of the eyes alternating a slow eye movement in one direction, and a fast eye movement in the other direction.


"
"octopus breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Sharing air using an octopus regulator
"
"octopus regulator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""octo reg"", ""safe second""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#Octopus"" title=""Diving regulator"">Diving regulator#Octopus</a></span></p>
A secondary demand valve fitted to a diving first stage for use as an alternative air source for another diver in case of an emergency. Also occasionally useful as a backup in case of some kinds of malfunction of the primary
"
"offboard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Not an integral part of the scuba unit. Usually applied to gas cylinders carried additional to the <a href=""#onboard_gas""><span title=""See entry on this page at § onboard gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">onboard gas</span></a> of a rebreather.
"
"offboard gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Gas carried in cylinders not integrally mounted on a rebreather, but plumbed into the unit.
"
"off-gassing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#outgassing""><span title=""See entry on this page at § outgassing"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">outgassing</span></a></span></p>"
"offshore (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;A significant distance away to seaward from the shoreline.
2.&#160;&#160;Outside the national maritime border, in international waters, though generally still inside the exclusive economic zone.<sup id=""cite_ref-Offshore_ACOP_2014_26-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Offshore_ACOP_2014-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
"
"offshore diver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_offshore_diving"" title=""Commercial offshore diving"">Commercial offshore diving</a></span></p> 
Colloquial term for a diver who works in the offshore oil and gas industry.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_12-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> A professional diver who works in regions outside the jurisdiction of national occupational health and safety and labour laws.
"
"O-lay (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Method for installation of sub-sea pipeline for the oil and gas industry. The pipe is constructed in an onshore construction yard, moved into the water and bent into a spiral without causing plastic deformation of the material. When the pipeline is sufficiently long it is transported with the help of tugs to the installation area. At the installation area the pipeline is unwound and pulled over a simple lay barge with stinger and installed on the bottom.<sup id=""cite_ref-O-lay_27-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-O-lay-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
"
"OLED (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OLED"" title=""OLED"">OLED</a></span></p>
Organic light-emitting diode: A low energy high contrast light source commonly used on instrument displays such as later generation dive computers.
"
"omitted decompression procedure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"omitted decompression protocol (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Procedure for managing a diver who surfaces without completing required decompression. If a chamber is available, the diver is recompressed in it, otherwise if no symptoms have presented, the diver may be recompressed as soon as practicable in the water. Various schedules for further decompression depend on the dive history.
"
"onboard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Mounted directly onto the unit as an integral component. Usually applied to gas cylinders mounted on a rebreather frame or housing, or emergency gas supply cylinders mounted on a diving bell or stage.
"
"onboard gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Gas carried in cylinders mounted as part of a unit, usually a rebreather or diving bell or stage.
"
"on-gassing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § ingassing"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#ingassing"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">ingassing</a></span></span></p>"
"onshore (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § inshore"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#inshore"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">inshore</a></span></span></p>"
"open circuit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Breathing apparatus which discharges exhaled gas into the environment, without any further use.
"
"open water (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_diving_environments_by_type#Environments_by_confinement"" title=""List of diving environments by type"">List of diving environments by type#Environments by confinement</a></i>. 
Water where there is no physical obstruction to a direct ascent to the surface.<sup id=""cite_ref-open_water_28-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-open_water-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;Water which is open to influences by weather and climatic conditions.<sup id=""cite_ref-Class_IV_29-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Class_IV-29"">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
"
"optode (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"optrode (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optode"" title=""Optode"">Optode</a></span></p>
Optical sensor device to measure a specific substance, usually with the aid of a chemical transducer.
"
"OOA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Out of air. An emergency situation where the supply of breathing gas to the diver has stopped.
"
"OPV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Over-pressure valve. A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure_relief_valve"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pressure relief valve"">pressure relief valve</a> which automatically opens at a set pressure to allow excess gas to escape.
"
"O-ring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/O-ring"" title=""O-ring"">O-ring</a></span></p>
A mechanical gasket in the shape of a torus; a loop of elastomer with a circular cross-section, designed to be seated in a groove and compressed during assembly between two or more parts, creating a seal at the contact surfaces.
"
"oro-nasal mask (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"ori-nasal mask (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
A breathing mask that covers the mouth and nose only. It may be an independent item, such as an oxygen mask or <span title=""See entry on this page at § BIBS"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#BIBS"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">BIBS</a></span> mask, or it may be a component inside a full face diving mask or helmet to reduce the amount of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dead_space_(physiology)"" title=""Dead space (physiology)"">dead space</a>
"
"OTU (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#oxygen_toxicity_unit""><span title=""See entry on this page at § oxygen toxicity unit"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">oxygen toxicity unit</span></a></span></p>"
"outgassing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Outgassing_of_tissues"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Outgassing of tissues</a></span></p>
Diffusion of gas out of the tissue into the blood, and transport to the lungs where it diffuses into the lung gas and is eliminated by exhalation.
"
"overhead (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A physical or procedural obstruction to a direct ascent to the surface. Physical overheads include cave, cavern or culvert ceilings, fishing nets, ship hulls, and wreckage. Procedural overheads are generally a decompression obligation.
"
"overrun (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Excessive rotation of a reel or spool by inertia, causing the line to unwind beyond the amount paid out, and lie in loose coils on the spool which can jam or tangle.
"
"overweighting (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § diving heavy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_heavy"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diving heavy</a></span></span></p>
Carrying more ballast weight than is necessary to achieve neutral buoyancy at all times during a dive. In scuba diving usually a dangerous error, but used in surface-supplied diving to stabilise the diver when working on the bottom.
"
"oxygen (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen"" title=""Oxygen"">Oxygen</a></span></p>
Important component gas of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_air"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Atmospheric air"">atmospheric air</a> and essential component of any <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">breathing gas</a>. Required to sustain life.
"
"oxygen analyser (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"oxygen analyzer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_analyzer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Oxygen analyzer"">Oxygen analyzer</a></span></p>
Instrument for measuring the partial pressure of oxygen in a gas mixture
"
"oxygen cell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electro-galvanic_oxygen_sensor"" title=""Electro-galvanic oxygen sensor"">Electro-galvanic oxygen sensor</a> for measuring partial pressure of oxygen in the breathing gas using an oxygen analyser
"
"oxygen clean (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility#Oxygen_cleaning"" title=""Oxygen compatibility"">Oxygen compatibility#Oxygen cleaning</a></span></p>
Cleaned for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_service"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Oxygen service"">oxygen service</a> by appropriate methods and materials and tested for contaminants. Verified that particulates, fibres, oils, greases and other contaminants are absent.<sup id=""cite_ref-ISO13293_7-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ISO13293-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"oxygen clock (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_toxicity#Underwater"" title=""Oxygen toxicity"">Oxygen toxicity#Underwater</a></span></p>
A notional alarm clock, which accumulates hyperbaric oxygen exposure at a rate which increases with higher oxygen partial pressure toward the maximum single exposure limit recommended. This <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_computer#Display_information"" title=""Dive computer"">function is implemented</a> as cumulative oxygen exposure for acute (CNS) oxygen toxicity in some dive computers.
"
"oxygen compatible (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility"" title=""Oxygen compatibility"">Oxygen compatibility</a></span></p>
Made from materials which are suitable for oxygen service. Capable of coexisting with elevated oxygen concentrations and a potential source of ignition without flashing, based on a system’s maximum operating pressure and temperature.<sup id=""cite_ref-ISO13293_7-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ISO13293-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"oxygen compatible air (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Air which has been filtered to reduce contaminants to a level suitable for blending with high pressure oxygen. Air with a reduced level of condensable hydrocarbon mist or vapour.<sup id=""cite_ref-ISO13293_7-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ISO13293-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"oxygen design (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"oxygen service design (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility#Oxygen_service_design"" title=""Oxygen compatibility"">Oxygen compatibility#Oxygen service design</a></span></p> 
Design that minimizes any tendency for heat generation, ignition of particulates, or the accumulation of contaminants for an intended partial pressure of oxygen and temperature.<sup id=""cite_ref-ISO13293_7-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ISO13293-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"oxygen fraction (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas#Classification_by_oxygen_fraction"" title=""Breathing gas"">Breathing gas#Classification by oxygen fraction</a></span></p>
Fraction by volume or pressure of the gas mixture made up by oxygen
"
"Oxygen Pete (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Imaginary monster associated with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_toxicity#History"" title=""Oxygen toxicity"">CNS oxygen toxicity</a>, also a CNS oxygen toxicity seizure.
"
"oxygen rebreather (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Oxygen_rebreathers"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Oxygen rebreathers</a></span></p>
A <span title=""See entry on this page at § closed circuit rebreather"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#closed_circuit_rebreather"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">closed circuit rebreather</a></span> that uses only oxygen as a gas supply.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"oxygen sensor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A component that produces a signal in response to the presence or concentration of oxygen. In diving this is usually a galvanic cell that generates a current and voltage proportional to the partial pressure of oxygen in a breathing gas.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"oxygen service (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See:<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_compatibility#Oxygen_service"" title=""Oxygen compatibility"">Oxygen compatibility#Oxygen service</a></span></p> 
Suitable for operating with significantly higher levels of oxygen than normal atmospheric air. Often implies special cleaning procedures, use of oxygen compatible materials, and design to reduce ignition risk. System or component that has been designed and tested for oxygen use, has been tested as oxygen clean and is oxygen compatible.<sup id=""cite_ref-ISO13293_7-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ISO13293-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"oxygen toxicity (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_toxicity"" title=""Oxygen toxicity"">Oxygen toxicity</a></span></p>
A condition resulting from the harmful effects of breathing molecular oxygen (O<sub>2</sub>) at elevated partial pressures.
"
"oxygen toxicity unit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
Unit of exposure to toxic concentrations of oxygen in breathing gas, primarily in connection with pulmonary oxygen toxicity and oxidative damage to cell membranes. The accumulation of OTUs depends on time and partial pressure of exposure, and dissipation is a function of recovery time at non-toxic partial pressures.
"
"oxygen window (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxygen_window_in_diving_decompression"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Oxygen window in diving decompression"">Oxygen window in diving decompression</a></span></p>
Inherent unsaturation due to metabolic reduction of total gas pressure in the tissues.
"
"panic (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><style data-mw-deduplicate=""TemplateStyles:r1033289096"">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panic"" title=""Panic"">Panic</a></span></p>
A sudden sensation of fear which is so strong as to dominate or prevent reason and logical thinking, replacing it with overwhelming feelings of anxiety and frantic agitation consistent with an animalistic fight-or-flight reaction
"
"parallel compartments (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Perfusion_limited_tissues_and_parallel_tissue_models"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Perfusion limited tissues and parallel tissue models</a></span></p>
A decompression model comprising a group of tissues with varied rates of perfusion, but supplied by blood of approximately equivalent gas concentration. It is assumed that there is no gas transfer between tissue compartments by diffusion. This results in a parallel set of independent tissues, each with its own rate of ingassing and outgassing dependent on the rate of blood flowing through the tissue
"
"partial pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partial_pressure"" title=""Partial pressure"">Partial pressure</a></span></p>
(Abbreviation PP or pp) The pressure that a component gas of a gas mixture would exert if it alone was present in the volume occupied by the gas mixture.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"passive addition (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Passive_addition_semi-closed_circuit"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Passive addition semi-closed circuit</a></span></p>
Feed gas addition system for semi-closed circuit rebreathers which discharges a part of the gas in the breathing circuit. fresh gas is added when the volume of the circuit decreases during inhalation and triggers the addition valve. Compare with <span title=""See entry on this page at § active addition"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#active_addition"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">active addition</a></span>.
"
"patent foramen ovale (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patent_foramen_ovale"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Patent foramen ovale"">patent foramen ovale</a></span></p>
A common form of congenital heart defect that enables blood flow between the left and right atria through a gap in the interatrial septum. In some circumstances this may increase risk of decompression sickness if venous blood carrying gas bubbles is shunted into the arterial system, bypassing the pulmonary capillary network filter.

"
"pendulum rebreather (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""push-pull rebreather""</span></p>
Rebreather with a single breathing hose from the mouthpiece to the scrubber and counterlung. Gas passes through it in both directions, unlike the one-way <span title=""See entry on this page at § breathing loop"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#breathing_loop"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">breathing loop</a></span> configuration. The volume of the hose between the mouthpiece and scrubber is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dead_space_(physiology)#In_breathing_apparatus"" title=""Dead space (physiology)"">dead space</a>
"
"penetration (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penetration_diving"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Penetration diving"">Penetration diving</a></span></p>
Entering a region with no direct vertical access to the surface, such as a cave or the interior of a wreck.
"
"penetration line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § distance line"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#distance_line"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">distance line</a></span></span></p>"
"percolation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Cave diving: Bubbles making their way to the walls and the ceiling of the cave and dislodging silt.<sup id=""cite_ref-x-ray_2-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-x-ray-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"perfusion (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perfusion"" title=""Perfusion"">Perfusion</a></span></p>
The process of delivery of blood to a capillary bed in the biological tissue.<sup id=""cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_3-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"perfusion limited (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Deterministic_models"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Deterministic models</a></span></p>
The assumption in a decompression model that perfusion has the dominant influence on gas uptake and release. Compare with <span title=""See entry on this page at § diffusion limited"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diffusion_limited"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diffusion limited</a></span>.
"
"permanent stamp markings (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"permanent markings (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"stamp markings (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Permanent_stamp_markings"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Permanent stamp markings</a></span></p>
Text stamped into the metal of the shoulder of a diving cylinder providing obligatory and optional information about the cylinder.
"
"personal locator beacon (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""PLB""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergency_locator_beacon"" title=""Emergency locator beacon"">Emergency locator beacon</a></span></p>
Radio beacons for personal use which are intended to indicate a person in distress who is away from normal emergency services.
"
"personal safety equipment (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_protective_equipment"" title=""Personal protective equipment"">Personal protective equipment</a></span></p>
Equipment worn by personnel to reduce risk of injury at sites where it is not practicable to eliminate the hazard, including ear protectors, safety glasses, hard hats, gloves, overalls, respirators etc. Diving suits and underwater breathing apparatus are also personal protective equipment.
"
"PFO (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#patent_foramen_ovale""><span title=""See entry on this page at § patent foramen ovale"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">patent foramen ovale</span></a></span></p>"
"photo quadrat (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § jump camera"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#jump_camera"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">jump camera</a></span></span></p>
A photograph of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrat"" title=""Quadrat"">quadrat</a> taken for later analysis. Common in marine ecological research where in situ counting would be impractical. Quadrats may be identified by rigid frames or by a fixed camera to subject distance.

"
"pig (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pigging#Pipeline_Inspection_Gauge"" title=""Pigging"">Pigging#Pipeline Inspection Gauge</a></span></p>
Pipeline inspection gauge: A tool that is sent through a pipeline and propelled by the pressure of the product in the pipeline itself, for purposes such as cleaning, dewatering, inspecting, measuring, separation of contents, etc.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"pigtail (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Coiled section of pipe to provide greater flexibility.
"
"pillar valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <span title=""See entry on this page at § cylinder valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#cylinder_valve"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">cylinder valve</a></span></span></p>"
"pin index connection (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pin_Index_Safety_System"" title=""Pin Index Safety System"">Pin Index Safety System</a></span></p>
Standard connection type for portable medical oxygen cylinder valves and regulators.
"
"pipeline end manifold (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""PLEM""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pipeline_end_manifold"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pipeline end manifold"">Pipeline end manifold</a></span></p>
