The place where a flexible underwater hose string is attached to connect a seabed pipeline with a single point mooring.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"piston bolt (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § bolt snap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bolt_snap"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">bolt snap</a></span></span></p>"
"placement (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Securing the <span title=""See entry on this page at § guideline"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#guideline"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">guideline</a></span> as it is being run.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;The choice of primary and secondary tie offs of the guideline.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"PLB (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""#personal_locator_beacon""><span title=""See entry on this page at § personal locator beacon"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">personal locator beacon</span></a></span></p>"
"PLEM (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#pipeline_end_manifold""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pipeline end manifold"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pipeline end manifold</span></a></span></p>"
"pneumo breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving_skills#Breathing_from_a_pneumofathometer_hose"" title=""Surface-supplied diving skills"">Surface-supplied diving skills#Breathing from a pneumofathometer hose</a></span></p>
Use of the pneumofathometer hose to supply breathing gas to a surface supplied diver in an emergency. Supply can be from the diver's own pneumo hose or from a standby diver's pneumo hose.
"
"pneumofathometer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""pneumo"", ""Kluge-Pneumo""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pneumofathometer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pneumofathometer"">Pneumofathometer</a></span></p>
Instrument to measure the depth of a diver, which measures the ambient pressure at the diver by measuring the pressure in a hose filled with air with an open end at the diver and with the surface end connected to a gas supply, control valve and pressure gauge calibrated in msw, fsw, or often both.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"pneumothorax (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pneumothorax"" title=""Pneumothorax"">Pneumothorax</a></span></p>
Air or other breathing gas in the chest cavity, outside of the lung, particularly between the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulmonary_pleurae"" title=""Pulmonary pleurae"">pulmonary pleurae</a>, sometimes resulting in a collapsed lung.

"
"pony cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pony_cylinder"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pony cylinder"">pony cylinder</a></span></p>
Relatively small scuba set carried as an independent alternative breathing gas source by a scuba diver.
"
"P-port (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A large bore quick connector fitting designed and used by Draeger on diving and firefighting breathing apparatus, which has been used in rebreathers, particularly modifications.
"
"positive displacement (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
(of compressor) A configuration that compresses gas by reducing the volume of the compression chamber (eg. cylinder) by mechanical means (eg. piston) to produce higher pressure of the contents which flow out via the exhaust valve.
"
"positive pressure breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"positive static lung load (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_physiology_of_underwater_diving#Positive_and_negative_pressure_breathing"" title=""Human physiology of underwater diving"">Human physiology of underwater diving#Positive and negative pressure breathing</a></span></p>
Breathing against an external pressure slightly greater than the relaxed pressure in the lungs. More effort is needed to exhale, less to inhale. This can occur when using a positive pressure mask, front mounted counterlungs on a rebreather, or if in a steep head down position with a single-hose demand valve.
"
"positive pressure mask (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A full-face mask which maintains an internal pressure slightly higher than external ambient pressure, necessitating slight positive pressure breathing, and ensuring that if the mask skirt seal fails, gas will leak out, rather than water leaking in, which provides a more secure airway and provides some protection against contaminated water.
"
"pre-fill external inspection (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Examination of the external condition of a pressure vessel and fittings to ensure that it complies with requirements before accepting for filling.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_6-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"pre-mix (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Nitrox blend with high oxygen content used to mix nitrox by topping up the decanted pre-mix with air.
"
"pressure gradient (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The rate of change of partial pressure of dissolved gas through a solvent, which is the driving mechanism for diffusion through the solvent. Also loosely used to refer to the difference between the dissolved gas pressure in a tissue and ambient pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_3-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"pressure transducer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: pressure sensor</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure_transducer"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pressure transducer"">Pressure transducer</a></span></p>
A component that produces a signal proportional to a pressure input, which can be processed to give an output indicating the pressure. Used in dive computers, electronic pressure gauges, and pressure transmitters, among other uses.
"
"pressure transmitter (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: wireless pressure transmitter</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure_transmitter"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pressure transmitter"">pressure transmitter</a></span></p>
Pressure transducer (q.v.) with a wireless transmitter that sends a coded signal to the diver's dive computer which uses the data to display remaining cylinder pressure, which can in some applications be used to provide other gas management information. 
"
"primary light (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The main light to be used on a dive. Usually the most powerful.
"
"primary regulator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
the regulator which the diver intends to breathe from for most of the dive. Particularly when diving with back-mounted manifolded twin cylinders.
"
"primary tie-off (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
First tie off of the guideline in a penetration dive. This is usually made in a place with free vertical access to the surface.
"
"professional diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional_diving"" title=""Professional diving"">Professional diving</a></span></p>
Diving which is done as part of the diver's employment or professional occupation.
"
"progressive penetration (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
An incremental approach to cave and wreck exploration. Each dive goes a bit further so that the divers develop a familiarity with the environment.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"PRV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure_relief_valve"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pressure relief valve"">Pressure relief valve</a>
"
"psi (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pounds_per_square_inch"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Pounds per square inch"">Pounds per square inch</a>. <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unit_of_measurement"" title=""Unit of measurement"">Unit</a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure"" title=""Pressure"">pressure</a> in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_system"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Imperial system"">Imperial system</a>.
"
"PTT (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Push to talk: Voice communication systems which require the user to press a button to transmit. Used with through water systems to conserve battery power.

"
"public safety diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_safety_diving"" title=""Public safety diving"">public safety diving</a></span></p>
The underwater work conducted by law enforcement, fire department rescue, and search &amp; rescue/recovery dive teams.
"
"pull (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;A relatively long pull on a lifeline when used for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_communications#Commercial_diving_rope_signals"" title=""Diver communications"">rope signals</a>. (see ""bell"" for comparison).
2.&#160;&#160;Part of an ascent between the bottom and a decompression stop, between decompression stops, or to the surface. Possibly deriving from the practice of pulling a surface supplied diver up by the umbilical or lifeline.
"
"pulmonary over-inflation syndrome (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barotrauma"" title=""Barotrauma"">Barotrauma</a></span></p>
Pulmonary barotrauma of ascent. Lung over-pressure injury.
"
"purge (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
To press the purge button on a demand valve to induce a gas flow which is intended to clear the demand valve interior of water or other substances.
"
"purge button (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Button or flexible area on the front or side of a demand valve which allows the user to manually open the second stage valve to provide gas flow without inhalation.
"
"purge valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Non-return valve in snorkel or mask which allows water to drain either under gravity or as a result of exhalation into the air space
"
"push gradient (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Tech diving jargon: Decompress at a high gradient factor, particularly when exceeding the baseline M-value. This will expose the diver to a higher risk of developing decompression sickness while reducing time decompressing in the water.<sup id=""cite_ref-Watts_7-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Watts-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"push-pull rebreather (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#pendulum_rebreather""><span title=""See entry on this page at § pendulum rebreather"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">pendulum rebreather</span></a></span></p>"
"P-valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""Pee-valve""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_suit#The_P-valve"" title=""Dry suit"">Dry suit#The P-valve</a></span></p>
A valved catheter fitted to a dry suit, which enables a diver to urinate at any time without having to get out of the water.
"
"Pyle stops (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Pyle_stops"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Pyle stops</a></span></p>
Named after <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Pyle"" title=""Richard Pyle"">Richard Pyle</a>, an early advocate of deep stops. An additional brief deep decompression stop, typically 2 minutes long and half way between the maximum depth and the first conventional decompression stop.


"
"quick link (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Oval connector shaped like a chain link with a screw gate on one side.
"
"quad (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A group of high pressure gas storage cylinders mounted upright on a frame and manifolded together. Usually in 4, 6, 9, 12, or 16 cylinder arrangements.
"
"quadrat (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrat"" title=""Quadrat"">Quadrat</a></span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <a href=""#photo_quadrat""><span title=""See entry on this page at § photo quadrat"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">photo quadrat</span></a></span></p>
A small, typically rectangular plot used in ecology and geography to isolate a standard unit of area for study of the distribution of an item over a large area. The quadrat is suitable for sampling plants and slow-moving or sessile animals.


"
"rams head (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""cobra guard"", <span title=""See entry on this page at § valve cage"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#valve_cage"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">valve cage</a></span></span></p>
Frame attached to the top of back-mounted scuba cylinders to protect valves, manifold, and regulator first stages from impact with the surroundings.
"
"rapture of the deep (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § nitrogen narcosis"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#nitrogen_narcosis"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">nitrogen narcosis</a></span></span></p>"
"rash guard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"rash vest (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"rashie (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rash_guard"" title=""Rash guard"">rash guard</a></span></p> 
A shirt made of spandex and nylon or polyester, worn to protect against rashes caused by abrasion, and jellyfish stings. These shirts can be worn by themselves, in tropical water, or under a wetsuit.
"
"Rat hat (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Ratcliffe diving helmet, Designed by Bob Ratcliffe, later produced by Oceaneering International. No longer in production.<sup id=""cite_ref-Rat_hat_8-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Rat_hat-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"ratio decompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""ratio deco""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ratio_decompression"" title=""Ratio decompression"">Ratio decompression</a></span></p>
A technique for calculating decompression schedules for scuba divers engaged in deep diving without using dive tables, decompression software or a dive computer.<sup id=""cite_ref-Lewis_2011_9-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Lewis_2011-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-Powell_2012_10-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Powell_2012-10"">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
"
"RDP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#recreational_Dive_Planner""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Recreational Dive Planner"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Recreational Dive Planner</span></a></span></p>
"
"rebreather (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_rebreather"" title=""Diving rebreather"">Diving rebreather</a></span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § gas extender"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#gas_extender"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">gas extender</a></span> and <a href=""#reclaim_system""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reclaim system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reclaim system</span></a></span></p> 
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_breathing_apparatus"" title=""Underwater breathing apparatus"">Underwater breathing apparatus</a> which recycles most of the exhaled gas, removing carbon dioxide and topping up oxygen before the gas is breathed again.
"
"reciprocating compressor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reciprocating_compressor"" title=""Reciprocating compressor"">Reciprocating compressor</a></span></p>
Compressor in which the volume of the compression chamber/s is cyclically changed by reversing linear motion. E.g.: a piston moving back and forth in a cylinder.
"
"reclaim helmet (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving"" title=""Saturation diving"">Saturation diving</a></span></p>
Diving helmet with a reclaim gas regulator allowing exhaled gas to be safely returned to the surface through an additional hose on the umbilical.
"
"reclaim regulator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reclaim_regulator"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Reclaim regulator"">Reclaim regulator</a></span></p>
A diving regulator designed to safely return exhaled gas to a reclaim hose at lower than ambient pressure. Function is similar to a <span title=""See entry on this page at § BIBS"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#BIBS"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">BIBS</a></span> exhaust valve.
"
"reclaim system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving"" title=""Saturation diving"">Saturation diving</a></span></p>
System for recovering helium based breathing gas used by divers and recycling it.
"
"recompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Subjecting a diver to pressure after an ascent from a dive as treatment for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_illness"" title=""Decompression illness"">decompression illness</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Preferably done in a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recompression_chamber"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Recompression chamber"">recompression chamber</a>, but occasionally done as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In-water_recompression"" title=""In-water recompression"">in-water recompression</a>.
2.&#160;&#160;Returning a diver to pressure as the first stage of <span title=""See entry on this page at § surface decompression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#surface_decompression"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">surface decompression</a></span> or <span title=""See entry on this page at § omitted decompression procedure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#omitted_decompression_procedure"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">omitted decompression procedure</a></span> to prevent <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a> from developing.
"
"recompression chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recompression_chamber"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Recompression chamber"">Recompression chamber</a></span></p>
A hyperbaric chamber used to treat divers suffering from certain <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_disorder"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Diving disorder"">diving disorders</a> such as <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a>.
"
"recovery breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""hook breathing""</span></p>
A technique used by freedivers on surfacing to reduce the risk of surface blackout. A partial exhalation is made, followed by a quick inhalation, then the diver closes the airway and pressurises for a few seconds as if about to cough. This is repeated a few times over the first 30 seconds or so on the surface. The aim is to keep thoracic pressure slightly raised to artificially raise arterial oxygen partial pressure or prevent it from dropping in the critical seconds until newly oxygenated blood can reach the brain, and thereby prevent surface blackout. This is the same technique used by pilots during high-g maneuvers, and by mountaineers at high altitude.
"
"recreational diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recreational_diving"" title=""Recreational diving"">Recreational diving</a></span></p>
Recreational diving or sport diving is a type of diving that uses scuba equipment for the purpose of leisure and enjoyment. In some diving circles, the term ""recreational diving"" is used in contradistinction to ""<span title=""See entry on this page at § technical diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#technical_diving"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">technical diving</a></span>"", a more demanding aspect of the sport which requires greater levels of training, experience and equipment. In other circles, technical diving is considered a subset of recreational diving as opposed to ""<a href=""#professional_diving""><span title=""See entry on this page at § professional diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">professional diving</span></a>"", which is done as part of the diver's work.

<span class=""anchor"" id=""recreational_Dive_Planner""></span>"
"Recreational Dive Planner (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""RDP""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recreational_Dive_Planner"" title=""Recreational Dive Planner"">Recreational Dive Planner</a></span></p>
A no-stop decompression table developed by DSAT.
"
"red tide (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § algal bloom"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#algal_bloom"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">algal bloom</a></span></span></p>"
"reduced gradient bubble model (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reduced_gradient_bubble_model"" title=""Reduced gradient bubble model"">Reduced gradient bubble model</a></span></p>
A computationally intensive bubble model decompression algorithm developed by Bruce Wienke.
"
"redundancy (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"redundant (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engineering_redundancy"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Engineering redundancy"">Engineering redundancy</a></span></p>
Technical diving philosophy of ensuring that a spare or backup is available for any item of life-support equipment that would immediately endanger the diver if it were to fail.<sup id=""cite_ref-Mount_2008b_12-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Mount_2008b-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
"
"redundant breathing gas supply (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: redundant gas supply, fully redundant gas supply, redundant air supply etc.</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redundant_breathing_gas_supply"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Redundant breathing gas supply"">Redundant breathing gas supply</a></span></p>
A breathing gas supply, carried by the diver, which is both suitable for the depths at which it may be breathed, and sufficient to allow the diver to make a safe and controlled return to the surface or other place where more breathing gas is available, which is not used during the dive, and is stored in one or more cylinders which are mot the one the diver is breathing from at any given time.
"
"redundant equipment (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
duplicated or spare equipment carried by the diver or team to substitute for vital primary equipment in case of a malfunction. In some cases, such as cave lights, multiple redundancy may be desirable. A redundant breathing gas supply is the most common example.
"
"reel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Mechanism used to store, deploy and recover long lengths of line at low tension.
"
"reference temperature (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Temperature at which a cylinder may be safely and legally filled to the nominal <span title=""See entry on this page at § charging pressure"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#charging_pressure"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">charging pressure</a></span> without corrections.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_6-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"regulator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressure_regulator"" title=""Pressure regulator"">mechanism</a> for controlling the output pressure of a high pressure gas supply.
2.&#160;&#160;As 1, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator"" title=""Diving regulator"">with a demand valve</a> (q.v.) incorporated which provides the diver with breathing gas at ambient pressure.
"
"regulator changeout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"regulator swap-out (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
Scuba emergency skill of swapping a correctly functioning regulator with one that is malfunctioning to gain access to breathing gas in a cylinder while underwater. Usually applied to side- or sling-mounted cylinders.
"
"regulator freeze (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_diving#Regulator_freezing"" title=""Ice diving"">Ice diving#Regulator freezing</a></span></p>
Locking of the regulator mechanism caused by freezing of the water due to expansion cooling of the regulated air. Often causes the mechanism to lock open, causing free flow and further cooling.
"
"reject criteria (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"rejection criteria (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Features, states or conditions which are not acceptable.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_6-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"repetitive dives (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Repetitive_dives"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Repetitive dives</a></span></p>
Any dive which is done while the tissues retain residual inert gas from a previous dive.
"
"repet-up (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Commercial diving term for a type of multilevel dive, in which the depth is decreased over elapsed time, with the purpose of allowing a longer useful dive time and minimising decompression time.<sup id=""cite_ref-Overland_1999_13-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Overland_1999-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Repex (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Method of estimating tolerable repetitive exposure to high partial pressure oxygen.<sup id=""cite_ref-Hamilton_1989_14-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Hamilton_1989-14"">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
"
"rescue tether (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A short lanyard or strap carried by a surface supplied stand-by diver to be used to tether an unresponsive diver to the standby diver during a rescue. It is attached at one end to a D-ring on the stand-by diver's harness, and has a clip at the other end which may be secured to a D-ring on the casualty's harness to allow the rescuer the use of both hands during the return to the bell or surface.
"
"reserve gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Reserve_pressure"" title=""Scuba gas planning"">Scuba gas planning#Reserve pressure</a></span></p>
Gas which is not intended to be used during the dive, and is reserved for contingencies.
"
"reserve valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Cylinder valve with a lever operated bypass valve to release the gas below reserve pressure
"
"residual gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Gas remaining in a cylinder from the previous fill.
"
"residual nitrogen (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Residual_nitrogen_time"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Residual nitrogen time</a></span></p>
Nitrogen in excess of normal atmospheric saturation remaining in the diver's tissues after a dive.
"
"residual nitrogen time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""RNT""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Residual_nitrogen_time"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Residual nitrogen time</a></span></p>
Time penalty in a repetitive dive equivalent to time at depth which would produce the residual nitrogen in the diver at the start of the dive.
"
"residual pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Pressure of the gas remaining in a partly used cylinder from the previous fill.
"
"respiratory minute volume (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""minute ventilation""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Respiratory_minute_volume"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Respiratory minute volume"">Respiratory minute volume</a></span></p> 
The volume of gas inhaled (inhaled minute volume) or exhaled (exhaled minute volume) from a person's lungs in one minute.
"
"respiratory quotient (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Respiratory_quotient"" title=""Respiratory quotient"">Respiratory quotient</a></span></p>
The ratio of carbon dioxide produced as a metabolic product to the oxygen consumed.
"
"restriction (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Section of a cave which is difficult to pass through due to lack of space. A minor restriction is too small for two divers to swim through together, a major restriction requires the diver to remove equipment to fit through.
"
"revalidation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
Certification that an item of equipment continues to be fit for service. Usually after passing the required periodic inspection and testing by an approved or authorised practitioner.
"
"reverse block (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Blockage of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paranasal_sinuses"" title=""Paranasal sinuses"">sinus</a> or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eustachian_tube"" title=""Eustachian tube"">eustachian tube</a> preventing relatively high internal gas pressure from escaping. <sup id=""cite_ref-Dovenbarger_2011_15-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Dovenbarger_2011-15"">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
"
"reverse ear squeeze (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: reverse ear, reverse squeeze, reversed ear.</span></p>
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barotrauma#Ear_barotrauma"" title=""Barotrauma"">Barotrauma of the ear</a> caused by a middle ear gas space pressure greater than ambient pressure, or greater than the pressure in the external autitory canal, causing the eardrum to bulge outwards.<sup id=""cite_ref-Dovenbarger_2011_15-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Dovenbarger_2011-15"">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
"
"reverse jump (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Procedure to cross a <span title=""See entry on this page at § gap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#gap"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">gap</a></span> during an exit which allows the line to be retrieved without returning to the start point. In the event of a line break or removed primary reel, one diver holds the end of the search line at the break point, and the other searches for the other part of the broken line or the exit while laying line from the reel. When the original line or exit is found, the reel handler signals to the static diver with line pulls and the static diver swims in the direction of the line while the reel handler reels it in, recovering the line.<sup id=""cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"reverse profile (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Repetitive dive which is deeper than the previous dive
Multilevel dive in which a later level is deeper than an earlier level.
"
"reverse sinus squeeze (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barotrauma"" title=""Barotrauma"">Barotrauma</a> of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paranasal_sinuses"" title=""Paranasal sinuses"">sinus</a> caused by a relatively high internal pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-Dovenbarger_2011_15-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Dovenbarger_2011-15"">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
"
"RGBM (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#reduced_gradient_bubble_model""><span title=""See entry on this page at § reduced gradient bubble model"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">reduced gradient bubble model</span></a></span></p>
"
"Rimbach system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
System of touch contact signalling used in cave diving. Push forward = go, pull back = back up, squeeze = stop.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"ring bungee (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § bungee (sidemount)"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bungee_(sidemount)"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">bungee (sidemount)</a></span></span></p>
Length of shock cord with metal rings and a clip used to control the position of the top end of a sidemounted cylinder.<sup id=""cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_17-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Differs from a regular bungee in having the rings.<sup id=""cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_17-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> A popular configuration is a bolt snap connected to a ring by a quick link, with a length of bungee from the ring to another quick link which is used to connect the assembly to a D-ring on the back of the harness. The bolt snap is clipped to the shoulder D-ring and the cylinder neck bolt snap is clipped to the ring.
"
"rip current (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rip_current"" title=""Rip current"">Rip current</a></span></p>
A strong localised flow of water to seaward from near the shore, typically through the surf line
"
"riser (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drilling_riser"" title=""Drilling riser"">Drilling riser</a></span></p>
A conduit that provides a temporary extension of a subsea oil well to a surface drilling facility
"
"RMV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#respiratory_minute_volume""><span title=""See entry on this page at § respiratory minute volume"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">respiratory minute volume</span></a></span></p>"
"RNPL (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""/w/index.php?title=Royal_Navy_Physiological_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Royal Navy Physiological Laboratory (page does not exist)"">Royal Navy Physiological Laboratory</a>
"
"RNT (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#residual_nitrogen_time""><span title=""See entry on this page at § residual nitrogen time"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">residual nitrogen time</span></a></span></p>
"
"rock bottom gas management (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning"" title=""Scuba gas planning"">Scuba gas planning</a></span></p>
Retention of a breathing gas reserve based on calculated values for the amount of gas required for a safe ascent from any point in the planned dive profile. Factors such as emergency supply of gas to a buddy, air consumption rates under stress and decompression gas requirements are considered in the calculations.
"
"roll-off (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Closing of a cylinder valve as a result of scraping contact between the valve knob and the overhead or other surroundings. The left hand knob is more likely to roll-off, closing the backup regulator in the standard twins configuration. Roll-off is an emergency if the diver does not have an immediately accessible alternative breathable gas supply.<sup id=""cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"ROV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"ROUV (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remotely_operated_underwater_vehicle"" title=""Remotely operated underwater vehicle"">Remotely operated underwater vehicle</a>&#160;&#8211; A tethered underwater mobile device operated by a remote crew.
"
"roughneck (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Member of the drilling crew who works under the direction of the driller to make or break connections as drillpipe is tripped in or out of the hole.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"roustabout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Any unskilled manual laborer on the rigsite.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>

"
"rule of thirds (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rule_of_thirds_(diving)"" title=""Rule of thirds (diving)"">Rule of thirds (diving)</a></span></p>
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_diving"" title=""Cave diving"">Cave</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wreck_diving"" title=""Wreck diving"">wreck</a> penetration breathing gas management convention where no more than one third of the gas in a cylinder may be used on the inward part of the dive, and the other two thirds is kept for exit: One third for the planned exit, and one third in case of an emergency.
"
"run line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"running line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Unreeling line under light tension while advancing. Usually in the context of laying a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distance_line"" title=""Distance line"">distance line</a>.
"
"run time (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Time elapsed since the start of a dive.
"
"running stop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A pause made during ascent to adjust the average ascent rate to the nominal value. For example a nominal ascent rate of 3&#160;m per minute might use an actual ascent rate of about 5&#160;m per minute and make a stop every 3m until the end of the current minute, resulting in a slightly stepped profile with an overall ascent rate corresponding to the nominal rate.<sup id=""cite_ref-Lewis_2011_9-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Lewis_2011-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
"
"run time schedule (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Decompression schedule and dive plan based on elapsed time from the start of the dive, All waypoints and events are specified in terms of elapsed time with start of descent at zero.
"
"R-valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""positive reserve valve"", ""automatic valve"", or ""calibrated orifice""</span></p>
A cylinder valve which limits the outflow by a calibrated orifice when in the ""on"" position.<sup id=""cite_ref-Basic_Scuba_18-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Basic_Scuba-18"">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>


"
"SAC rate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#surface_air_consumption_rate""><span title=""See entry on this page at § surface air consumption rate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">surface air consumption rate</span></a></span></p>"
"safe air (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Term used for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrox"" title=""Nitrox"">nitrox</a> by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Nitrox_Divers_International"" title=""American Nitrox Divers International"">American Nitrox Divers International</a> (ANDI)
"
"safe second (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Obsolete term for <span title=""See entry on this page at § octopus regulator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#octopus_regulator"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">octopus regulator</a></span>.<sup id=""cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"safety-critical element (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Item of equipment or process with the purpose to prevent or limit the consequences of a high risk hazard, that if realised, could result in the fatality or severe injury of one or more divers or support crew.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"safety reel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Reel with relatively short line for use in an emergency, usually for searches to find a lost buddy or lost guideline or to jump a line break.<sup id=""cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"safety spool (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Spool with relatively short line for use in an emergency, usually for searches to find lost buddy or lost guideline or to jump a line break.<sup id=""cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"safety stop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Safety_stop"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Safety stop</a></span></p>
A voluntary (not required by the decompression schedule) additional decompression stop intended to further reduce risk of decompression sickness.
"
"salt water aspiration syndrome (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_water_aspiration_syndrome"" title=""Salt water aspiration syndrome"">Salt water aspiration syndrome</a></span></p>
A reaction of the lungs to inhalation of a mist of salt water
"
"samba (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Involuntary muscular contractions experienced by breathhold divers when approaching <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypoxic_blackout"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hypoxic blackout"">hypoxic blackout</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-freedivingbiz_19-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-freedivingbiz-19"">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Sasuba (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A shallow water recreational airline diving system using a scuba cylinder on a float towed by the diver.
"
"saturation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Condition where the inert components of the breathing gas dissolved in a diver's tissues are in equilibrium with the gas in the lungs.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
"
"saturation diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving"" title=""Saturation diving"">Saturation diving</a></span></p>
Diving mode where the divers remain pressurised for periods of several days or weeks and decompress only at the end of the period.
"
"saturation diving system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"saturation spread (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving_system"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Saturation diving system"">Saturation diving system</a></span></p>
The combination of equipment and services to operate a saturation diving project. It would include the closed diving bell, the accommodation modules, decompression chamber, life-support systems, gas storage and supply systems, pressurisation equipment, underwater breathing apparatus, and launch and recovery systems. In may also include a hyperbaric evacuation system.

"
"SCBA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-contained_breathing_apparatus"" title=""Self-contained breathing apparatus"">Self-contained breathing apparatus</a> (not for underwater use).
"
"schrader valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schrader_valve"" title=""Schrader valve"">Schrader valve</a></span></p>
Valve using a standard automotive tyre valve insert, common in low pressure inflation hose female connectors and BC inflation valves.<sup id=""cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"scientific diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_diving"" title=""Scientific diving"">Scientific diving</a></span></p>
Diving for purposes of scientific research. The rules and constraints of scientific diving vary in different jurisdictions, but generally allow different options to mainstream commercial diving.
"
"scooter (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_propulsion_vehicle"" title=""Diver propulsion vehicle"">Diver propulsion vehicle</a> used by scuba divers to increase range underwater.<sup id=""cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"scooter ring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
D-ring on scuba harness used to attach to scooter tow line. Usually on front of the harness crotch strap.<sup id=""cite_ref-Gerrard_2015_16-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Gerrard_2015-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"SCR (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-closed_circuit_rebreather"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Semi-closed circuit rebreather"">Semi-closed circuit rebreather</a>: A rebreather (q.v.) which either dumps part of each breath to the environment or continuously adds gas and dumps the excess. Compare with closed circuit rebreather (CCR) (q.v.).
2.&#160;&#160;Surface Consumption Rate - An alternative term with the same meaning as Surface Air Consumption (SAC) (q.v.). Not to be confused with Semi-closed Circuit Rebreather.
"
"screw gate carabiner (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carabiner"" title=""Carabiner"">Carabiner</a></span></p>
A clip mechanism which can be locked in the closed position by turning a threaded barrel.
"
"scrubber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather#Carbon_dioxide_scrubber"" title=""Rebreather"">Rebreather#Carbon dioxide scrubber</a></span></p>
Canister containing material (sorb) which chemically combines with carbon dioxide to remove it from the gas passed through the canister.
"
"scuba (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"SCUBA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_set"" title=""Scuba set"">Scuba set</a></span></p>
Self-contained underwater breathing apparatus. May be open or closed circuit.
"
"scuba orienteering (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_orienteering"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Scuba orienteering"">Scuba orienteering</a></span></p>
Competitive underwater sport in which scuba divers attempt to swim a circuit marked by buoys, without surfacing, using compass navigation and mechanical distance measurement. Points are awarded for time and accuracy according to the specific course definition and length.
"
"scuba replacement (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Mobile <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">surface-supplied diving</a> equipment using portable gas storage cylinders for primary and reserve <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_gas"" title=""Breathing gas"">breathing gas</a> supply. Preferred to scuba for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_diving"" title=""Commercial diving"">commercial diving</a> applications due to lower perceived risk compared to scuba, and because equipment and procedures are otherwise identical to surface supplied diving using compressors for air supply. Used when logistical constraints or air quality issues preclude use of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_air_compressor"" title=""Diving air compressor"">compressor</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"S-drill (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Safety drill. An air sharing exercise based on deploying the long hose primary regulator.

"
"search line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_searches"" title=""Underwater searches"">Underwater searches</a></span></p>
Cord used to indicate the transect for a search. The diver moves along the line, searching by sight or feel on one or both sides of the line. After the transect has been searched, the line is moved to the next transect. usually a short distance offset from the previous position, at a distance which depends on the visibility and the size of the target.
"
"search pattern (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_searches"" title=""Underwater searches"">Underwater searches</a></span></p>
Systematic procedure for covering the search area sufficiently to be reasonably sure of finding a given target if it is there. Several patterns are in general use for underwater searches, depending on the target, the terrain, and available facilities.
"
"secondary drowning (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secondary_drowning"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Secondary drowning"">Secondary drowning</a></span></p>
A complication of aspiration of water or other fluids into the lungs.
"
"secondary regulator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § backup regulator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#backup_regulator"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">backup regulator</a></span></span></p>"
"second stage (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § demand valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#demand_valve"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">demand valve</a></span></span></p>
The part of a diving regulator which provides pressure reduction from intermediate pressure to ambient pressure on demand. Demand valve.
"
"self-propelled hyperbaric lifeboat (SPHL) (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""hyperbaric lifeboat"" (HLB), ""hyperbaric rescue vessel"" (HRV)</span></p>
A pressure vessel adapted for use as a means of hyperbaric evacuation, and fitted to a conventional lifeboat hull.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"semi-dry suit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_suit#Semi-dry_suit"" title=""Diving suit"">Diving suit#Semi-dry suit</a></span></p>
A wet suit with wrist and ankle seals, and usually a more watertight zipper than usual, to reduce flushing of water through the suit.
"
"separator (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vapor%E2%80%93liquid_separator"" title=""Vapor–liquid separator"">Vapor–liquid separator</a></span></p>
Device which facilitates the separation of liquid particles from the compressed gas, usually with a drain to periodically remove accumulated liquid from the system.
"
"serial compartments (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Diffusion_limited_tissues_and_the_&quot;tissue_slab&quot;,_and_series_models"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Diffusion limited tissues and the ""tissue slab"", and series models</a></span></p>
A decompression model based on the assumption that diffusion is the limiting mechanism of dissolved gas transport in the tissues, in which there is perfusion transport for one compartment, and diffusion between a series of compartments,
"
"serial number (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serial_number"" title=""Serial number"">Serial number</a></span></p>
1.&#160;&#160;Number stamped on the cylinder by the manufacturer in the shoulder area which identifies the cylinder. In combination with the manufacturer’s identification this will be unique to the cylinder.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_6-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;Character string, including number, marked on an item of equipment by the manufacturer to uniquely identify it.
"
"setpoint (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"set-point (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"set point (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather_diving#Set-points"" title=""Rebreather diving"">Rebreather diving#Set-points</a></span></p>
Reference value for oxygen partial pressure in an electronically controlled closed circuit rebreather. The control system monitors the real time value of oxygen partial pressure in the breathing loop and automatically adjusts the composition by adding gas to keep the concentration between the upper and lower set-points.
"
"SGC (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <a href=""#sAC""><span title=""See entry on this page at § SAC"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">SAC</span></a></span></p>
Surface Gas Consumption

<h3><span class=""mw-headline"" id=""Sh"">Sh</span><span class=""mw-editsection""><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">[</span><a href=""/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18"" title=""Edit section: Sh"">edit</a><span class=""mw-editsection-bracket"">]</span></span></h3>
"
"shallow water blackout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Loss of consciousness during a dive associated with occurrence at a shallow depth. Used for several different mechanisms, depending on context, therefore often leading to confusion.
1.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shallow-water_blackout_(disambiguation)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Shallow-water blackout (disambiguation)"">Shallow-water blackout</a><br />
Loss of consciousness caused by cerebral hypoxia towards the end of a breath-hold dive in water typically shallower than five metres (16 feet), when the swimmer does not necessarily experience an urgent need to breathe and has no other obvious medical condition that might have caused it.<sup id=""cite_ref-Boyd_et_al_2015_20-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Boyd_et_al_2015-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freediving_blackout#Terminology"" title=""Freediving blackout"">Freediving blackout#Terminology</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latent_hypoxia"" title=""Latent hypoxia"">latent hypoxia</a><br />
Loss of consciousness caused by cerebral hypoxia at the end of a deep breath-hold dive during the latter part of the ascent or immediately after surfacing due to lowered pO<sub>2</sub> caused by reduction in ambient pressure, see also latent hypoxia.
3.&#160;&#160;Loss of consciousness while ascending on a rebreather due to sudden drop of pO<sub>2</sub> in the breathing loop, usually associated with manual CCR and SCR.
"
"shark pod (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"shark shield (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
Electrical device carried by a diver intended to repel sharks by electrical field pulses.<sup id=""cite_ref-sharkshield_21-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-sharkshield-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"shock cord (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bungee_cord"" title=""Bungee cord"">bungee cord</a></span></p>"
"shore diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Diving from a shore entry point.
"
"shot line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_shot"" title=""Diving shot"">Diving shot</a></span></p>
A rope between a float at the surface, and a sufficiently heavy weight holding the rope approximately vertical.<sup id=""cite_ref-DR_2001_22-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-DR_2001-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>"
"sidemount (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
