<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Terminology"" title=""Sidemount diving"">Sidemount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
A scuba diving equipment configuration which has diving cylinders mounted alongside the diver, below the shoulders and along the hips, instead of on the back of the diver.
"
"sidemount staging (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Terminology"" title=""Sidemount diving"">Sidemount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
The practice of using sidemount configuration (bungee loops and/or <span title=""See entry on this page at § butt-plate"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#butt-plate"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">butt-plate</a></span> rails) as a means for stowing stage/deco cylinders when otherwise diving in <span title=""See entry on this page at § backmount"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#backmount"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">back-mounted</a></span> scuba
"
"silent entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries"" title=""Scuba skills"">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
An entry technique which minimises noise and splash, suitable for entry from a low platform. The diver sits with feet dangling over or into the water, turns their torso sideways, takes their weight on their hands, then swings off the surface and drops feet first into the water, slowed by their arms, and lets go with the hands when in the water.<sup id=""cite_ref-BSAC_Diving_Manual_1982_23-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BSAC_Diving_Manual_1982-23"">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup class=""reference nowrap""><span title=""Page / location: 251"">&#58;&#8202;251&#8202;</span></sup>
"
"silica gel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silica_gel"" title=""Silica gel"">Silica gel</a></span></p>
A desiccant filter medium used to adsorb water.
"
"silt out (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silt_out"" title=""Silt out"">Silt out</a></span></p>
A situation when underwater visibility is rapidly reduced to zero, usually when a diver disturbs silt deposits.
"
"silt screw (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_diving#Equipment"" title=""Cave diving"">Cave diving#Equipment</a></span></p>
Device which is inserted into silt or sand to provide an anchor point, such as for a tie-off on a cave line.<sup id=""cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_17-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Silt screws are generally stakes made from small bore plastic (PVC) pipe with a sharpened end.
"
"simultaneous operations (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Two or more potentially clashing operations occurring, for example, at the same time and same location.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"single point mooring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_buoy_mooring"" title=""Single buoy mooring"">Single buoy mooring</a></span></p>
A loading buoy anchored offshore, that serves as a mooring point and interconnect for tankers loading or offloading gas or liquid products. SPMs are the link between geostatic subsea manifold connections and weathervaning tankers. They are capable of handling any size ship, even very large crude carriers (VLCC) where no alternative facility is available<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"sinkhole (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinkhole"" title=""Sinkhole"">Sinkhole</a></span></p>
A natural depression or hole in the Earth's surface caused by karst processes — the chemical dissolution of carbonate rocks - or suffosion processes for example in sandstone
"
"sintered (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sintering"" title=""Sintering"">Sintering</a></span></p>
Particulate or granular material bonded together by the application of pressure and sufficient heat to partially melt the surface of the particles and weld them together. The product is usually porous.
"
"siphon (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Place where water from a stream flows into the ground. also ""swallow hole""<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_5-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"skandalopetra (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skandalopetra_diving"" title=""Skandalopetra diving"">Skandalopetra diving</a></span></p>
A flat stone, usually of marble or granite, weighing between 8 and 14&#160;kg, with rounded corners and edges, and tied to a rope, historically used by Greek sponge free-divers to assist descent. When the diver wishes to ascend the rope is used to signal the tender on the boat who then pulls in the rope. Currently skandalopetra diving is a competitive sport.
"
"skin (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"skins (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § dive skins"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#dive_skins"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">dive skins</a></span></span></p>"
"skip breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypercapnia#Skip_breathing"" title=""Hypercapnia"">Hypercapnia#Skip breathing</a></span></p>
Breathing pattern where the diver holds each breath a while to conserve breathing gas, which can cause <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypercapnia"" title=""Hypercapnia"">hypercapnia</a> which can lead to headaches, aggravate nitrogen narcosis, increase risk of oxygen toxicity, and reduce physiological reserves in an emergency.
"
"S-lay (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Submarine_pipeline#The_S-lay_system"" title=""Submarine pipeline"">Submarine pipeline#The S-lay system</a></span></p>
Method of laying undersea pipelines by welding the sections together on the lay barge and deploying them from the stern horizontally guided by a ""stinger"" - a structure that supports the pipe string to control its bend radius.<sup id=""cite_ref-huismanequipment1_24-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-huismanequipment1-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The term refers to the shape of the bend in the pipe which transitions from roughly horizontal onboard where the sections are welded together, to angled downward  over the stinger, to roughly horizontal again as it settles on the seabed.
"
"slate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Rigid plastic tablet used for writing messages or notes.
"
"sling cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Open-circuit"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Open-circuit</a></span></p>
Independent cylinders with their own regulators carried clipped to the harness at the side of the diver.
"
"slingshot valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § Y-valve"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#Y-valve"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">Y-valve</a></span></span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Other_distinguishing_features"" title=""Scuba cylinder valve"">Scuba cylinder valve#Other distinguishing features</a></span></p>
A cylinder valve with two valved outlets angled to left and right of the centreline
"
"slob knob (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Flexible extension used for operating valve knobs on a manifold
"
"SMB (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#surface_marker_buoy""><span title=""See entry on this page at § surface marker buoy"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">surface marker buoy</span></a></span></p>"
"snag line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Line used for underwater search intended to snag on the target. May be dragged by boats or by divers. May be weighted if dragged over a smooth bottom.
"
"snap shackle (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shackle#Snap_shackle"" title=""Shackle"">Shackle#Snap shackle</a></span></p>
A clip connector mechanism which locks when closed, can be operated without tools, and can usually be released under load.
"
"snoopy loop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubber_band#Snoopy_loop"" title=""Rubber band"">Rubber band#Snoopy loop</a></span></p>
A heavy duty elastic band made from a slice of inner tube.
"
"snoot (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|" 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_photography#Snoot"" title=""Underwater photography"">Underwater photography#Snoot</a></span></p>
Accessory for a photographic strobe which limits illumination of the subject to a very small area, leaving the background datk, and virtually eliminating backscatter.
"
"snorkel (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snorkel_(swimming)"" title=""Snorkel (swimming)"">Snorkel (swimming)</a></span></p>
Tube with a bend and mouthpiece used for breathing air from above the water surface when the wearer's mouth and nose are submerged.
"
"snorkeling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"snorkelling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snorkeling"" title=""Snorkeling"">Snorkeling</a></span></p>
Swimming at the surface of the water while breathing through a snorkel. the snorkeller is almost always equipped with a diving mask or swim goggles, and usually swimfins.
"
"snorkel keeper (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snorkel_(swimming)#Construction"" title=""Snorkel (swimming)"">Snorkel (swimming)#Construction</a></span></p> 
Device to hold a snorkel in place at the side of a diving mask by fixing it to the mask strap.
"
"Snuba (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § airline"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#airline"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">Hookah</a></span></span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snuba"" title=""Snuba"">Snuba</a></span></p>
Snuba is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portmanteau"" title=""Portmanteau"">portmanteau</a> of ""snorkel"" and ""scuba"", referring to a proprietary recreational surface supplied underwater breathing system supplied from a cylinder mounted on a small raft towed by the diver.

"
"solo diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solo_diving"" title=""Solo diving"">Solo diving</a></span></p>
The practice of scuba diving alone, without a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddy_diving"" title=""Buddy diving"">dive buddy</a> or in-water <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standby_diver"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Standby diver"">standby diver</a> .
"
"sonic orifice (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choked_flow"" title=""Choked flow"">Choked flow</a></span></p>
Metering device to provide constant mass flow of a gas.
"
"sorb (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""sodasorb"", ""sodalime"" and ""sofnolime""</span></p>
Carbon dioxide absorbent material used in rebreather or life support system scrubber to remove carbon dioxide from the breathing gas so it may be recycled.

"
"speargun (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speargun"" title=""Speargun"">Speargun</a></span></p>
Hunting weapon for shooting fish underwater which propels a barbed steel spear a short distance forward using stored energy from stretched rubber strips or compressed air behind a captive piston.
"
"spearo (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Slang term for breathhold spearfisher.
"
"speech unscrambler (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""helium unscrambler"" and ""unscrambler""</span></p>
An electronic device to render words spoken in a hyperbaric helium environment intelligible.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-7"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"speleogen (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speleogen"" title=""Speleogen"">Speleogen</a></span></p>
Dissolution features in bedrock.
"
"speleothem (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speleothem"" title=""Speleothem"">Speleothem</a></span></p>
Also known as a cave formation: A secondary mineral deposit formed in a cave.
"
"SPG (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#submersible_pressure_gauge""><span title=""See entry on this page at § submersible pressure gauge"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">submersible pressure gauge</span></a></span></p>"
"SPHL (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#self-propelled_hyperbaric_lifeboat""><span title=""See entry on this page at § Self-propelled hyperbaric lifeboat"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">Self-propelled hyperbaric lifeboat</span></a></span></p>"
"spider (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full-face_diving_mask#Straps"" title=""Full-face diving mask"">Full-face diving mask#Straps</a></span></p>
Mask strap system for full-face masks with three or more straps. (commonly 5)
"
"spitcock (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_diving_dress#Helmet"" title=""Standard diving dress"">Standard diving dress#Helmet</a></span></p>
A valve in the side of a copper diving helmet which could be used by the diver to suck in a mouthful of seawater to spit onto the inside face of a viewport to wash off condensation droplets to improve their view.
"
"SPM (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#single_point_mooring""><span title=""See entry on this page at § single point mooring"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">single point mooring</span></a></span></p>"
"spool (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distance_line#Reels_and_spools"" title=""Distance line"">Distance line#Reels and spools</a></i><br />
Circular device for storing line, comprising a short tubular section with a relatively large flange at each end. No moving parts. A small, compact, economical and reliable alternative to a reel for relatively short lines.
2.&#160;&#160;Short, straight section of pipe or tube with a flange at each end.
"
"spread (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The topside base for (usually) surface supplied commercial diving operations. Also ""<span title=""See entry on this page at § air spread"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#air_spread"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">air spread</a></span>"" and ""<a href=""#saturation_spread""><span title=""See entry on this page at § saturation spread"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">saturation spread</span></a>"" (q.v.) depending on the diving mode.<sup id=""cite_ref-25"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-25"">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
"
"spring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spring_(hydrology)"" title=""Spring (hydrology)"">Spring (hydrology)</a></span></p>
Place where a concentrated flow of water emerges from the ground.
"
"spring strap (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See:<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swimfin#Attachment"" title=""Swimfin"">Swimfin#Attachment</a></span></p>
Fin strap using a stainless steel spring to secure the fin to the foot.
"
"spring suit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wetsuit"" title=""Wetsuit"">wetsuit</a> that covers the torso and has short sleeves and long or short legs
"
"spud can (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The foot on a leg of a <span title=""See entry on this page at § Jack-up rig"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#Jack-up_rig"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O"">Jack-up rig</a></span> oil platform designed to spread the load so that the rig does not sink too deeply into the sea-bed.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"SPUMS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Pacific_Underwater_Medicine_Society"" title=""South Pacific Underwater Medicine Society"">South Pacific Underwater Medicine Society</a>
"
"square profile (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dive_profile#Square_profile"" title=""Dive profile"">Dive profile#Square profile</a></span></p>
Dive profile where the diver descends continuously to the maximum depth and stays there for the duration of the dive before ascending directly at a stedy rate to the surface or first decompression stop. This profile provides worst case exposure for gas absorption by the body tissues for a given depth and bottom time, and is assumed for most decompression planning using decompression tables.
"
"squeeze (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § barotrauma"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#barotrauma"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">barotrauma</a></span></span></p>
Injury or discomfort caused by increase or decrease in volume of gas space in the diver's body or equipment due to a change in ambient pressure.
"
"SSDE (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving"" title=""Surface-supplied diving"">Surface-supply diving equipment</a>.

"
"stabilisor jacket (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"stab jacket (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#buoyancy_compensator""><span title=""See entry on this page at § buoyancy compensator"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">buoyancy compensator</span></a></span></p>"
"stage (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § diving stage"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_stage"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diving stage</a></span></i>
2.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href=""#stage_cylinder""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stage cylinder"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stage cylinder</span></a></i>
3.&#160;&#160;Part of a dive in which gas is breathed from a specific stage cylinder
"
"stage cylinder (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;A cylinder used for a stage of a long penetration dive, also known as drop cylinder, which is placed on the distance line to be collected on the return.
2.&#160;&#160;Also generically used to refer to decompression gas cylinders carried as <a href=""#sling_cylinder""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sling cylinder"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sling cylinders</span></a> (q.v.)
"
"staged decompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The practice of making decompression stops.
"
"stage-drop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Placing a <a href=""#stage_cylinder""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stage cylinder"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stage cylinder</span></a> at the <span title=""See entry on this page at § distance line"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#distance_line"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">distance line</a></span> for planned later use.
"
"stage-only diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Terminology"" title=""Sidemount diving"">Sidemount diving#Terminology</a></span></p>
The use of standard deco/stage cylinder configuration, without back-mounted cylinders, on an otherwise standard, or partially modified tec/rec BCD. The cylinders are attached to waist and shoulder D-Rings by direct bolt-snap, and no bungee cord is used in the upper attachment. Similar to, and may be confused with <a href=""#sidemount""><span title=""See entry on this page at § sidemount"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">sidemount</span></a>
"
"standard diving dress (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"standard dress (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""heavy gear""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_diving_dress"" title=""Standard diving dress"">Standard diving dress</a></span></p>
Early free flow surface supplied diving equipment using a heavy rubberised canvas suit, copper helmet and <span title=""See entry on this page at § corselet"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#corselet"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">corselet</a></span>, and weighted boots. Still in use in some parts of the world.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
"
"standard operating procedure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_operating_procedure"" title=""Standard operating procedure"">Standard operating procedure</a></span></p> 
Procedure compiled by an organisation prescribing the processes to be followed when performing specified tasks.
"
"standby diver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"stand-by diver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standby_diver"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Standby diver"">Standby diver</a></span></p> 
(Professional) diver functioning as a safety backup to the working diver. Often on the surface at the dive control point, but ready to enter the water at very short notice on the instruction of the supervisor. In bell diving the stand-by diver would be the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bellman_(diving)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Bellman (diving)"">bellman</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"static apnea (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"static apnoea (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Static_apnea"" title=""Static apnea"">Static apnea</a></span></p>
Underwater breath-holding without changing location
"
"static lung load (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""hydrostatic imbalance"", ""SLL""</span></p>
The pressure difference between gas inside the lungs and the gas inside the mouthpiece of the breathing apparatus or inside the helmet. In most rebreathers this is the hydrostatic pressure at depth of the counterlung. In ballasted bellows counterlungs the pressure is modified by the force exerted by the ballast weight.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_26-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
"
"steamer (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A full one piece <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wetsuit"" title=""Wetsuit"">Wetsuit</a> that covers the torso and the full length of the arms and legs.
"
"stinger (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
An overboard extension at the stern of an offshore pipe lay barge used to provide additional support at the over bend of an S-lay during offshore construction.<sup id=""cite_ref-huismanequipment1_24-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-huismanequipment1-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
"
"stop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § decompression stop"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#decompression_stop"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">decompression stop</a></span></span></p>"
"living depth (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#storage_depth""><span title=""See entry on this page at § storage depth"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">storage depth</span></a></span></p>"
"storage depth (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""living depth""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving#Accommodation"" title=""Saturation diving"">Saturation diving#Accommodation</a></span></p>
Depth pressure in a saturation system at which divers live between compression and decompression when not locked out on a dive.<sup id=""cite_ref-NORSOK_U100_27-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-NORSOK_U100-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
"
"stride entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""giant stride entry""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries"" title=""Scuba skills"">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
Entry technique from a platform a small to moderate distance above the water surface, which is suitable to stand on before entry. The diver faces the water and steps out with the leading foot, pushing away from the platform with the back foot, and drops into the water while maintaining a vertical posture until fully submerged. It is usually advisable to hold loose equipment against the body, particularly the mask and DV, and if there is no crotch strap, the buoyancy compensator is held to prevent it riding up the torso on impact. The feet can be brought together after initial impact to limit depth of immersion in moderately shallow water, by applying fin thrust downwards.<sup id=""cite_ref-BSAC_Sport_Diving_1985_28-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BSAC_Sport_Diving_1985-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"stroke (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Derogatory term used by <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doing_It_Right_(scuba_diving)"" title=""Doing It Right (scuba diving)"">DIR</a> zealots to describe divers who do not follow DIR procedures and use DIR approved equipment and configurations.

"
"subcutaneous emphysema (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subcutaneous_emphysema"" title=""Subcutaneous emphysema"">Subcutaneous emphysema</a></span></p>
Gas under the skin resulting from lung overpressure injury.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_29-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-29"">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
"
"submersible compression chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"submersible decompression chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § closed bell"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#closed_bell"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">closed bell</a></span></span></p>
A closed diving bell, used for transferring divers under pressure to and from the worksite. Particularly if used fpr decompressio.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_1-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
"
"submersible pressure gauge (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""SPG""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Submersible_pressure_gauge"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Submersible pressure gauge"">Submersible pressure gauge</a></span></p>
Gauge attached to the first stage regulator and used to monitor pressure remaining in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder"" title=""Diving cylinder"">diving cylinder</a>.
"
"suicide clip (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Derogatory term for clip mechanisms which are capable of clipping onto a line or other object without the active and intentional intervention of a user.
"
"suit blowup (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_skills#Dry_suit_blowup"" title=""Scuba skills"">Scuba skills#Dry suit blowup</a></span></p>
Excessive inflation of a dry suit leading to uncontrolled ascent.
"
"sump (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sump_(cave)"" title=""Sump (cave)"">Sump (cave)</a></span></p>
A passage in a cave that is submerged under water.
"
"sump pack (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Tough waterproof bag with watertight seal used to carry dry equipment in caves, including through water filled passages.<sup id=""cite_ref-Side_Mount_Profiles_17-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Side_Mount_Profiles-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
"
"superoxide scrubber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Rebreather scrubber which not only removes carbon dioxide from the exhaled air, but also replenishes the oxygen by chemical reaction.
"
"supersaturation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A temporary and thermodynamically unstable condition of a solvent containing more dissolved gas than it can hold in solution over the long term for the prevailing conditions.
"
"supersaturation limit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The theoretical pressure ratio between tissue gas concentration and ambient pressure above which the probability of bubble formation is unacceptably high.<sup id=""cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_3-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Supervised Diver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_Diver"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Supervised Diver"">Supervised Diver</a></span></p>
EN 14153-1 / ISO 24801-1 standard competence for recreational scuba diver. The level 1 ""Supervised Diver"" has sufficient knowledge, skill and experience to dive, in open water, to a recommended maximum depth of 12&#160;m, which do not require in-water decompression stops, under the direct supervision of a dive leader, in groups of up to four level 1 scuba divers per dive leader provided the dive leader is capable of establishing physical contact with all level 1 scuba divers at any point during the dive, only when appropriate support is available at the surface, and under conditions that are equal or better than the conditions where they were trained.<sup id=""cite_ref-EUF_1_30-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EUF_1-30"">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
"
"supervisor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § diving supervisor"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diving_supervisor"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diving supervisor</a></span></span></p>"
"supply lock (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Small lock on a saturation life support habitat for transfer of relatively small items.
"
"support diver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Support_diver"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Support diver"">Support diver</a></span></p>
A voluntary member of a <span title=""See entry on this page at § technical diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#technical_diving"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z"">technical diving</a></span> team who acts as a <a href=""#stand-by_diver""><span title=""See entry on this page at § stand-by diver"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">stand-by diver</span></a> to the primary dive team, or provides in-water logistical support for a dive.
"
"SurD (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#surface_decompression""><span title=""See entry on this page at § surface decompression"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">surface decompression</span></a></span></p>"
"surf (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breaking_wave"" title=""Breaking wave"">Breaking wave</a></span></p>
The mass or line of broken water formed by waves breaking on a shore or reef
"
"surface air consumption rate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A measure of air consumption in units of pressure over time, usually psi/minute, adjusted to surface pressure, used to estimate air endurance of a cylinder of specific size. Useful for those who work in imperial units.<sup id=""cite_ref-NOAA_4th_ed_31-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-NOAA_4th_ed-31"">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> SAC has a constant value for a given diver and represents gas used on the surface at rest.<sup id=""cite_ref-SDI_Solo_IG_32-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SDI_Solo_IG-32"">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Surface gas consumption (SGC) is an alternative term referring to alternative breathing gas mixtures. Occasionally also termed surface consumption rate (SCR)<sup id=""cite_ref-divetalking_33-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-divetalking-33"">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-Scuba_diving_34-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Scuba_diving-34"">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
"
"surface compression chamber (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A hyperbaric chamber for surface use for routine decompression or therapeutic recompression.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
"
"surface decompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Surface_decompression"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Surface decompression</a></span></p>
A procedure in which some or all of the staged decompression obligation is done in a decompression chamber immediately after surfacing instead of in the water.
"
"surface detection aids (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Equipment, such as flags, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface_marker_buoy"" title=""Surface marker buoy"">surface marker buoys</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flare"" title=""Flare"">flares</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EPIRB"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""EPIRB"">EPIRBs</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_beacon"" title=""Radio beacon"">radio beacons</a> mirrors, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whistle"" title=""Whistle"">whistles</a>,  carried by divers to maintain contact with dive boats or attract rescue when lost at sea.
"
"surface equivalent volume (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § free gas volume"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#free_gas_volume"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">free gas volume</a></span></span></p> 
Gas volume calculated as expanded to surface pressure.
"
"surface interval (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Surface_interval"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Surface interval</a></span></p>
The time spent by a diver at surface pressure after a dive during which inert gas which was still present at the end of the dive is further eliminated from the tissues.
"
"surface marker buoy (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""SMB""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface_marker_buoy"" title=""Surface marker buoy"">Surface marker buoy</a></span></p>
A buoy towed by a diver to indicate the diver's position to people at the surface.
"
"surface orientated diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Any diving operation in which the diver is decompressed to surface pressure after the dive. Compare to <a href=""#saturation_diving""><span title=""See entry on this page at § saturation diving"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">saturation diving</span></a> .<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_11-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
"
"SURG (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Southern Underwater Research Group. An organisation based in Cape Town, which publishes marine ecology field guides, dive travel guides and underwater maps.<sup id=""cite_ref-SURG_35-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SURG-35"">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
"
"surge (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waves_and_shallow_water"" title=""Waves and shallow water"">Waves and shallow water</a></span></p>
Reciprocating water movement parallel to the bottom surface caused by the passing of a wave overhead, by analogy with the transient linear motion of a ship in the direction of travel also called surge.
"
"sustained load cracking (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sustained_load_cracking"" title=""Sustained load cracking"">Sustained load cracking</a></span></p>
The development of cracks in a material subjected over long term to static stress significantly less than the yield stress. There is a low but significant risk of this mode of failure in pressure vessels of AA6351 aluminium alloy.<sup id=""cite_ref-Luxfer_support_36-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Luxfer_support-36"">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
"
"swell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swell_(ocean)"" title=""Swell (ocean)"">Swell (ocean)</a></span></p>
A series of surface gravity waves that is not generated by the local wind.
"
"swim line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Line used to space divers across the search area for a swim line search. Each diver holds the line at a distance from the previous diver of somewhat less than twice the visibility distance. The line is used to keep the divers spaced evenly across the search area while swimming perpendicular to the line.
"
"swimthrough (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"swim-through (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A submerged arch or short tunnel that a diver can swim through without needing to remove equipment. It is usually possible to see natural light at the far end in good visibility and illumination. Usually refers to a natural formation. Technically an overhead environment, but usually with no risk of getting lost, though entrapment may be possible.

"
"tank factor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><style data-mw-deduplicate=""TemplateStyles:r1033289096"">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § baseline"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#baseline"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">baseline</a></span></span></p>"
"taravana (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taravana"" title=""Taravana"">Taravana</a></span></p>
A form of decompression sickness originally observed among Polynesian island natives who habitually did multiple repetitive deep breath-hold dives.<sup id=""cite_ref-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-1"">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"task loading (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Task_loading"" title=""Task loading"">Task loading</a></span></p>
A multiplicity of responsibilities leading to an increased risk of failure on the part of the diver to undertake some key basic function which would normally be routine for safety
"
"taut wire system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A constant tension wire from a vessel to a weight on the seabed used as a reference to detect movement of a dynamically positioned vessel from the reference point.<sup id=""cite_ref-Bevan_2005_3-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Bevan_2005-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>

"
"technical diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technical_diving"" title=""Technical diving"">Technical diving</a></span></p>
An extension of the scope of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recreational_diving"" title=""Recreational diving"">recreational scuba diving</a> to applications with greater technical complexity and higher inherent risk. Definitions vary, but diving with multiple breathing gases, helium based gases, closed circuit rebreathers, or under extensive overheads are generally considered as technical diving. There is no sharp distinction from other forms of recreational diving.
"
"tech ring (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-ring"" title=""D-ring"">D-ring</a> welded to a <span title=""See entry on this page at § belt slide"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#belt_slide"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">belt slide</a></span> so that it can not fold down against the webbing. Intended to make it easier to fit and remove snaps.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"temperature stick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"tempstick (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""thermal profile monitor"", ""TPM""</span></p>
An array of temperature sensors mounted in a rebreather scrubber canister along the path of gas flow to monitor the temperature as an indication of the advance of the exothermic reaction front of the scrubber, providing an indication of scrubber depletion.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"tension leg rig (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tension-leg_platform"" title=""Tension-leg platform"">Tension-leg platform</a></span></p>
A vertically moored floating structure normally used for the offshore production of oil or gas, particularly suited for water depths between 300 and 1500 meters. The platform is permanently moored by means of tethers at each of the structure's corners and virtually all vertical motion of the platform is eliminated.
"
"test of pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Diagnostic procedure for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a>. The diver is recompressed, and if the symptoms reduce, it may be assumed that the diver has decompression sickness and hyperbaric treatment will be effective. The test is not entirely reliable<sup id=""cite_ref-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
"
"test pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Pressure at which a gas storage cylinder will be hydrostatically tested for revalidation. Usually 1.5 or 1.67 x working pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"tethered ascent (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_skills#Emergency_ascents"" title=""Scuba skills"">Scuba skills#Emergency ascents</a></span></p>
Ascent controlled by a line from the diver to a fixed point at the bottom. This may be used to control depth and rate of ascent when the diver has inadvertently lost complete control of buoyancy due to loss of ballast weight, so cannot attain neutral buoyancy at some point during the ascent, and needs to do decompression. CMAS require this skill for their Self-Rescue Diver certification.<sup id=""cite_ref-CMAS_SRDTP_8-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-CMAS_SRDTP-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"
"tethered diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Diving with a lifeline between the diver and a surface tender.
"
"Thalmann algorithm (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <a href=""#vVAL18""><span title=""See entry on this page at § VVAL18"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">VVAL18</span></a></span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thalmann_algorithm"" title=""Thalmann algorithm"">Thalmann algorithm</a></span></p>
The Exponential/linear decompression algorithm used in the 2008 US Navy decompression tables
"
"therapeutic recompression (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperbaric_medicine"" title=""Hyperbaric medicine"">Hyperbaric medicine</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_practice#Therapeutic_decompression"" title=""Decompression practice"">Decompression practice#Therapeutic decompression</a>, and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness#Treatment"" title=""Decompression sickness"">Decompression sickness#Treatment</a></span></p>
A procedure for treating decompression sickness by recompressing the diver, thus reducing bubble size, and allowing the gas bubbles to re-dissolve, then decompressing slowly enough to avoid further formation or growth of bubbles, or eliminating the inert gases by breathing oxygen under pressure
"
"therapeutic schedule (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Procedure for hyperbaric treatment involving recompression to relieve symptoms, followed by decompression at a rate unlikely to cause a relapse. Use of special breathing gas, particularly oxygen, to increase the rate of elimination of inert gases is common.<sup id=""cite_ref-EDTC_2017_9-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EDTC_2017-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
"
"thermal profile monitor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#temperature_stick""><span title=""See entry on this page at § temperature stick"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">temperature stick</span></a></span></p>"
"thermocline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermocline"" title=""Thermocline"">Thermocline</a></span></p>
A thin but distinct layer in a large body of fluid, in which temperature changes more rapidly with depth than it does in the layers above or below
"
"thermodynamic decompression model (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#The_no-supersaturation_approach"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#The no-supersaturation approach</a></span></p>
Hypothesis that bubble formation during decompression will not occur provided absolute ambient pressure exceeds the total of the partial gas tensions in the tissue for each gas.
"
"thirds (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § rule of thirds"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#rule_of_thirds"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">rule of thirds</a></span></span></p>"
"three part shackle (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""bolt and nut shackle"", ""bolt shackle""</span></p>
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shackle"" title=""Shackle"">shackle</a> which uses a bolt as the pin, secured with a nut. The nut may be locked with a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Split_pin"" title=""Split pin"">split pin</a> for greater security. The bolt may rotate in the shackle under load without great risk of unscrewing the pin
"
"through-water communications (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Wireless voice communications transmitted through the water
"
"thumb the dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Terminate the dive by signalling exit to surface at a time or place other than the planned turning point.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"thunderflash (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Friction initiated noisy but relatively harmless pyrotechnic device designed for military exercises, with civilian use for diver recall.<sup id=""cite_ref-thunderflashes1_10-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-thunderflashes1-10"">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-thunderflashes2_11-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-thunderflashes2-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>

"
"time to fly (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The surface interval necessary after diving to reduce tissue gas concentrations to a level where the risk of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_sickness"" title=""Decompression sickness"">decompression sickness</a> due to the pressure reduction experienced in normal commercial airliners is acceptable.<sup id=""cite_ref-USNDM_R6_12-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-USNDM_R6-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
"
"tinnitus (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tinnitus"" title=""Tinnitus"">Tinnitus</a></span></p>
The perception of sound within the ear in the absence of corresponding external sound. Usually a constant tone.
"
"tissue compartments (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Tissue_compartments"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Tissue compartments</a></span></p>
Hypothetical body tissues which are designated as fast and slow to describe the rate of saturation.
"
"tissue half times (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_theory#Tissue_half_times"" title=""Decompression theory"">Decompression theory#Tissue half times</a></span></p>
The time it takes for the tissue to take up or release 50% of the difference in dissolved gas capacity at a changed partial pressure.
"
"TNT (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Total Nitrogen Time: Equivalent time of hyperbaric exposure for a repetitive dive used with some decompression tables.
2.&#160;&#160;<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trinitrotoluene"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Trinitrotoluene"">Trinitrotoluene</a>, a high explosive

"
"toolbox talk (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""TBT""</span></p>
A meeting held at the start of each shift or prior to any project critical operation, where the diving supervisor or the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_supervisor"" title=""Diving supervisor"">diving supervisor</a>’s delegate and shift personnel discuss the forthcoming tasks or jobs and the potential risks and necessary precautions to be taken.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"top up (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § air top"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#air_top"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">air top</a></span></span></p>
To reconnect a partially filled cylinder and add gas until the pressure is within tolerance of the required charging pressure when corrected for temperature.
"
"touch contact signals (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § Rimbach system"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#Rimbach_system"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">Rimbach system</a></span></span></p>"
"Toynbee manoeuvre (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ear_clearing"" title=""Ear clearing"">Ear clearing</a></span></p>
Method of equalising the middle ears by pinching the nose and swallowing.
"
"trait anxiety (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anxiety#Trait"" title=""Anxiety"">Anxiety#Trait</a></span></p>
A tendency to respond with anxiety in the anticipation of threatening situations.
"
"transect (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transect"" title=""Transect"">Transect</a></span></p>
A path along which one counts and records occurrences of the phenomena of study.
"
"transfill (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""decant""</span></p>
Fill cylinder with gas by transfer from a cylinder with higher pressure.
"
"transfill whip (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
High pressure hose and end fittings used to <span title=""See entry on this page at § decant"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#decant"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">decant</a></span> between cylinders. Usually includes purge valve and may include pressure gauge.
"
"trauma shears (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""bandage scissors"" or ""paramedic shears""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trauma_shears"" title=""Trauma shears"">Trauma shears</a></span></p>
Blunt tipped slightly serrated shears with angled blades sometimes used by divers as a safety cutting implement in place of a knife or line cutter.
"
"travel gas (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Gas mixture used for descent and ascent when the <span title=""See entry on this page at § bottom gas"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bottom_gas"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">bottom gas</a></span> is not suitable for breathing at shallower depths.
"
"traverse (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Pass through a cave by entering at one point and exiting at another.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
