"treatment table (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A depth, time and breathing gas profile designed to treat a diver for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_illness"" title=""Decompression illness"">decompression illness</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"tremie (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tremie"" title=""Tremie"">Tremie</a></span></p>
A pipe, through which concrete is placed below water level. The top of the tremie is above water and open, and the bottom end is kept below the surface of the poured concrete.
"
"triangular profile (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A triangular dive profile is one in which, after a descent at constant rate, and a short bottom time at maximum depth, the diver maintains a constant, slow ascent to the surface or first decompression stop. A plot of depth against elapsed time takes a triangular shape.
"
"triglide (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § belt slider"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#belt_slider"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">belt slider</a></span></span></p>"
"trilam (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Material used for dry suit shells made of a layer of waterproof rubber laminated between two layers of woven textile.
"
"trimix (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)"" title=""Trimix (breathing gas)"">Trimix (breathing gas)</a></span></p>
Mixture of three gases for breathing. Oxygen, nitrogen and helium are the gases used.<sup id=""cite_ref-ISO13293_14-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-ISO13293-14"">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The gas fractions will usually be specified.
"
"trim weight (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_weighting_system#Trim"" title=""Diving weighting system"">Diving weighting system#Trim</a></span></p>
Ballast weight placed to improve a diver's <a href=""#trim""><span title=""See entry on this page at § trim"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">trim</span></a>.
"
"tripping line (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A line attached to the top of an open parachute lifting bag and at the other end to an anchor point. Its purpose is to invert and thus empty the bag if it becomes detached from the load.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"try-dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Guided dive using unfamiliar equipment as a marketing technique, in the hope of convincing the diver that the product is worth buying. Some instruction or guidance on the use and characteristics of the product is usual. Similar in concept to test driving a motor vehicle, and similarly, generally offered to qualified operators, except for rebreathers, where one qualifies on a specific type.

"
"tube (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""Kelly tubes"" or ""Kellys""</span></p> 
A seamless transportable compressed gas container, with a water capacity exceeding 150 litres (5.3&#160;cu&#160;ft) but not more than 3,000 litres (110&#160;cu&#160;ft);<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Often mounted horizontally in manifolded groups on a trailer or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intermodal_container"" title=""Intermodal container"">intermodal container</a> frame.<sup id=""cite_ref-Kelly_15-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Kelly-15"">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
"
"TUP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturation_diving#Transfer_under_pressure"" title=""Saturation diving"">Transfer Under Pressure</a>: Transfer of personnel between hyperbaric environments, usually between a closed bell and a saturation system, or between a portable recompression chamber and a multi-occupant chamber
"
"turbidity (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turbidity"" title=""Turbidity"">Turbidity</a></span></p>
The cloudiness or haziness of a fluid caused by individual particles (suspended solids) that may be invisible to the naked eye, similar to smoke in air
"
"turn the dive (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Start the return on a dive which has reached the planned turning point in terms of depth, time, gas supply or distance.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"twilight zone (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Deeper than 60&#160;m in the sea, or the part of a cave or cavern that has dim but discernible ambient light.
"
"type 1 wet bell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell#Type_1_wet_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">Diving bell#Type 1 wet bell</a></span></p>
Wet diving bell (q.v.) with no direct supply of gas and services to the bell. Diver umbilicals lead directly to the surface control point.
"
"type 2 wet bell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell#Type_2_wet_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">Diving bell#Type 2 wet bell</a></span></p>
Wet diving bell (q.v.) with umbilical supply of gas and other services to the bell, from which they are distributed to the divers umbilicals from a control panel in the bell.


"
"UBA (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Underwater Breathing Apparatus: Equipment used to supply breathing gas to an underwater diver. Usually refers to the part of the system carried underwater by the diver.
"
"UDT vest (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Underwater Demolition Team vest, An inflatable surface life-jacket worn by underwater demolition teams. Similar in style and a precursor to the horse-collar style buoyancy compensator.
"
"UHMS (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Undersea_and_Hyperbaric_Medical_Society"" title=""Undersea and Hyperbaric Medical Society"">Undersea and Hyperbaric Medical Society</a>
"
"umbilical (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"umbilical cable (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umbilical_cable#Diver"" title=""Umbilical cable"">Umbilical cable#Diver</a></span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § bell umbilical"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bell_umbilical"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">bell umbilical</a></span>, <span title=""See entry on this page at § diver umbilical"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diver_umbilical"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">diver umbilical</a></span>, <span title=""See entry on this page at § excursion umbilical"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#excursion_umbilical"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">excursion umbilical</a></span>, and <span title=""See entry on this page at § ROV umbilical"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#ROV_umbilical"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">ROV umbilical</a></span></span></p> 
Life support hose and cable bundle connection to a surface supplied diver or diving bell. Comprises gas supply hoses, pneumofathometer, a <a href=""/w/index.php?title=Strength_member&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Strength member (page does not exist)"">strength member</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diver_communications#Voice_communications"" title=""Diver communications"">communications</a> cable, and may also include gas reclaim hose, hot water hose and hoses for hydraulic or pneumatic power, and electrical and optical cables for ancillary equipment. Underwater television cameras and cabling can also be carried as a component part of the umbilical or can be taped or banded to it on a temporary basis. Also refers to the power, control and instrument cable for a ROV.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"umbilical changeout (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Emergency procedure to disconnect the umbilical and connect a replacement in situ during the dive. Usually only used when a delay in recovering the diver or bell is likely.
"
"umbilical cutter (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
mechanism fitted to a closed bell which allows the occupants to sever the bell umbilical from inside the sealed and pressurised bell in the event of an umbilical snag that prevents bell recovery. The device is typically hydraulically operated using a hand pump inside the bell, and can shear the umbilical at or just above the point where it is fastened to the top of the bell.<sup id=""cite_ref-16"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-16"">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
"
"undertow (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Undertow_(water_waves)"" title=""Undertow (water waves)"">Undertow (water waves)</a></span></p>
A subsurface flow of water returning seaward from shore as result of wave action
"
"underwater blackout syndrome (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""hyperventilation-induced blackout""</span></p>
Loss of consciousness due to hypoxia during a breath-hold submersion preceded by hyperventilation where alternative causes of blackout have been excluded.<sup id=""cite_ref-Pearn_et_al_2015_17-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Pearn_et_al_2015-17"">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id=""cite_ref-Pollock_2014_18-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Pollock_2014-18"">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
"
"unscrambler (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § speech unscrambler"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#speech_unscrambler"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">speech unscrambler</a></span></span></p>"
"upline (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""Jersey upline""</span></p>
A fairly substantial natural fibre rope which is deployed from the bottom using a small lift bag to provide the equivalent of a shotline. The lower end is tied off to the bottom, usually on a wreck, and the diver ascends on the line to avoid being swept away from the site by currents. After reaching the surface, the last diver cuts the line and it sinks back down, Natural fibre is used so the line rots away over a few years.<sup id=""cite_ref-shipwreckexpo_19-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-shipwreckexpo-19"">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
"
"upstream (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Against the flow.
"
"upstream valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_regulator#Upstream_vs_downstream"" title=""Diving regulator"">Diving regulator#Upstream vs downstream</a></span></p>
Valve, (usually regulator first stage or demand valve), where the valve mechanism moves against the flow when opening, and the pressure difference over the valve tends to close it.
"
"upwelling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upwelling"" title=""Upwelling"">Upwelling</a></span></p>
An oceanographic phenomenon that involves wind-driven motion of dense, cooler, and usually nutrient-rich water towards the ocean surface, replacing the warmer, usually nutrient-depleted surface water


"
"Valsalva maneuver (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valsalva_maneuver"" title=""Valsalva maneuver"">Valsalva maneuver</a></span></p>
Technique for equalising the middle ear by moderately forceful attempted exhalation against a closed mouth and blocked nose
"
"valve cage (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Valve_cage"" title=""Scuba cylinder valve"">Scuba cylinder valve#Valve cage</a></span></p> 
Structure or frame fitted to scuba cylinder to protect the cylinder valve or manifold and regulator first stage from impact damage and <span title=""See entry on this page at § roll-off"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#roll-off"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S"">roll-off</a></span> .
"
"valve drill (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Safety exercise in which the diver shuts down, tests regulators and re-opens the manifold valves on a twin set in a specific order.
"
"valve guard (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
protective structure or frame fitted to the top of a bulk storage cylinder to protect the cylinder valve from mechanical damage.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"van (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Enclosed portable compartment with diving spread support equipment. Often built into an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intermodal_container"" title=""Intermodal container"">intermodal container</a>. 
Exanples: 
<ul><li>DDC van, containing control panels for deck decompression chamber operation,</li>
<li>Machinery van, containing hydraulic power pack, compressor, air banks or similar equipment</li></ul>
"
"Van der Waals equation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_der_Waals_equation"" title=""Van der Waals equation"">Van der Waals equation</a></span></p>
Thermodynamic equation of state for a real (non-ideal) gas.
"
"vasoconstriction (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vasoconstriction"" title=""Vasoconstriction"">Vasoconstriction</a></span></p>
The narrowing of blood vessels resulting from contraction of the muscular wall of the vessels, particularly the large arteries and small arterioles.
"
"vasodilation (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vasodilation"" title=""Vasodilation"">Vasodilation</a></span></p>
The widening of blood vessels resulting from relaxation of smooth muscle cells within the vessel walls, particularly in the large veins, large arteries, and smaller arterioles.

"
"venous gas embolism (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decompression_(diving)#Bubble_formation,_growth_and_elimination"" title=""Decompression (diving)"">Decompression (diving)#Bubble formation, growth and elimination</a></span></p>
Inert gas bubbles formed in the venous circulation.
"
"venting breath (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Breathing pattern intended to vent gas from a rebreather loop, usually by exhaling through the nose.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"vertical entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"vertical drop entry (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries"" title=""Scuba skills"">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
An entry technique for relatively high drops, up to and sometimes exceeding 3&#160;m. The feet are overlapped and the legs kept straight. The body and head are kept vertical and the mask and DV held against the face with one or both hands, elbows tucked in. The intention is to hit the water vertically, with the least likelihood of knocking off or damaging vital equipment.<sup id=""cite_ref-BSAC_Diving_Manual_1982_20-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-BSAC_Diving_Manual_1982-20"">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup class=""reference nowrap""><span title=""Page / location: 249"">&#58;&#8202;249&#8202;</span></sup>
"
"vertigo (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertigo"" title=""Vertigo"">Vertigo</a></span></p>
A type of dizziness, where there is a feeling of motion when one is stationary.
"
"VGE (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""#venous_gas_embolism""><span title=""See entry on this page at § venous gas embolism"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">venous gas embolism</span></a></span></p>
"
"viewport (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
1.&#160;&#160;Glass or plastic window on a diving helmet or mask.
2.&#160;&#160;Window on a hyperbaric chamber or manned submersible .
"
"VIP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Visual Inspection Programme (US). Annual visual internal inspection of a scuba cylinder.
"
"visibility (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"viz (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_vision#Visibility"" title=""Underwater vision"">Underwater vision#Visibility</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turbidity"" title=""Turbidity"">turbidity</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nephelometry"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Nephelometry"">nephelometry</a></span></p>
The distance through the water at which an object can just be seen against the background. Often defined as the distance at which a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secchi_disc"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Secchi disc"">Secchi disc</a> perpendicular to the sight line can first be seen when moving towards it. It can vary depending on direction illumination, and depth.
"
"visual gap (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<span title=""See entry on this page at § gap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#gap"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G"">Gap</a></span> between guidelines which is small enough that each line can be seen from the other.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"visual jump (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
The procedure of crossing a <a href=""#visual_gap""><span title=""See entry on this page at § visual gap"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id="""">visual gap</span></a> (q.v.) without the use of a jump line.<sup id=""cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_4-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
"
"visual inspection (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Internal and external inspection of a pressure vessel as part of revalidation procedure<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Visual Plus (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddy-current_testing"" title=""Eddy-current testing"">Eddy-current testing</a></span></p>
Crack detection test of parallel neck threads of aluminium cylinders
"
"Viton (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viton"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Viton"">Viton</a></span></p>
Synthetic elastomer suitable for oxygen service O-rings.
"
"volume tank (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A pressure vessel connected to the outlet of a gas supply and used as a gas reservoir.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"voting algorithm (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"voting logic (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redundancy_(engineering)#Voting_logic"" title=""Redundancy (engineering)"">Redundancy (engineering)#Voting logic</a>, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebreather_diving#Managing_cell_failure_in_an_electronic_rebreather_control_system"" title=""Rebreather diving"">Rebreather diving#Managing cell failure in an electronic rebreather control system</a></span></p>
The logical procedure in which rebreather electronics compare output from multiple sensors when sensors produce significantly different values, suggesting that one or more are faulty, and choose which signals should be ignored, assuming <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_independence"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Statistical independence"">statistical independence</a> of the sensors, which may not be valid.<sup id=""cite_ref-Heinerth_5-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Heinerth-5"">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
"
"VPM (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Varying_Permeability_Model"" title=""Varying Permeability Model"">Varying Permeability Model</a></span></p>
(also Variable permeability model). A decompression model and associated algorithms based on bubble dynamics.
"
"VVAL18 (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""E-L algorithm"", ""Exponential-Linear algorithm"", ""Thalmann algorithm""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thalmann_algorithm"" title=""Thalmann algorithm"">Thalmann algorithm</a></span></p>
Exponential-Linear algorithm used for the 2008 US Navy tables, which assumes exponential ingassing and a combination of linear and exponential outgassing rates.


"
"wall diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underwater_diving#Diving_environment"" title=""Underwater diving"">Underwater diving#Diving environment</a></span></p>
Recreational scuba diving along the face of a near vertical cliff wall, particularly if the bottom is below the range of the diver's equipment and certification. This requires good buoyancy control.
"
"water capacity (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Of a cylinder: The internal volume. The amount of water it would hold at ambient pressure at 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F)<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"water trap (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Mechanism to trap liquid water carried by compressed gas.

"
"weight belt (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_weighting_system#Weight_belt"" title=""Diving weighting system"">Diving weighting system#Weight belt</a></span></p> 
Ballasted waist belt worn by divers to compensate for excess buoyancy. For scuba and freediving, usually easily removed to establish positive buoyancy in an emergency.
"
"weight harness (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_weighting_system#Weight_harness"" title=""Diving weighting system"">Diving weighting system#Weight harness</a></span></p>
Webbing strap system to support diving weights, usually suspended from the shoulders and fastened around the waist. The harness may carry the weights directly, or they may be carried in pockets on the harness. For scuba diving the weights may be arranged for easy shedding.
"
"weighting system (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_weighting_system"" title=""Diving weighting system"">Diving weighting system</a></span></p>
Weights, generally made of lead, to counteract the buoyancy of other diving equipment, and the belts, pockets or harnesses used to support them.
"
"weight slider (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"weight stop (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <span title=""See entry on this page at § belt slider"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#belt_slider"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">belt slider</a></span></span></p>"
"welding shield (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Cover for the viewport area of a helmet or mask to filter excessive light and UV when welding or oxy-arc cutting.
"
"wellhead (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wellhead"" title=""Wellhead"">Wellhead</a></span></p>
The assembly at the surface of an oil or gas well that provides the structural and pressure-containing interface for the drilling and production equipment.
"
"wet bell (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_bell#Structure_of_a_typical_wet_bell"" title=""Diving bell"">Diving bell#Structure of a typical wet bell</a></span></p>
A mobile platform used to deploy and recover divers to and from working depth fitted with an air dome and on board emergency gas supply for use as safe haven in emergencies. There may be a main supply umbilical from the surface providing breathing gas to a manifold inside the wet bell and diver excursion umbilicals terminated at the wet bell, or the divers' umbilicals may be direct from the surface.<sup id=""cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13"">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
"
"wet filling (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Temperature_change_during_filling"" title=""Diving cylinder"">Diving cylinder#Temperature change during filling</a></span></p> 
Filling scuba cylinders using a water bath for cooling the cylinders.<sup id=""cite_ref-Dry_filling_21-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Dry_filling-21"">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
"
"wet notes (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A small notebook of waterproof paper carried by some divers<sup id=""cite_ref-Jablonski_2006_22-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Jablonski_2006-22"">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
"
"wet pot (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Water filled hyperbaric chamber, generally for experimental work or training.
"
"wetsuit (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wetsuit"" title=""Wetsuit"">Wetsuit</a></span></p>
A close fitting, thermally-insulating, foam <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neoprene"" title=""Neoprene"">neoprene</a> diving suit that allows a limited volume and movement of water inside the suit.
"
"whip (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Flexible high pressure gas hose with connector at the free end, used for temporary connections. The other end may be permanently connected to an installation or other equipment, or may also have a temporary connector. Whips are commonly named for their intended use, e.g. filling whip, for filling cylinders, decanting, transfill or transfer whip for decanting between cylinders, oxygen whip for oxygen transfer, blending whip, for decanting gases when blending gas, etc. Accessories may include a flow control valve, bleed valve, pressure gauge, and/or whip check.<sup id=""cite_ref-Oxyhacker_23-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Oxyhacker-23"">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
"
"whip check (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A cable or webbing strap connecting a hose end to the attachment point in addition to the hose end fitting, which restrains the movement of the hose if the connection is broken under pressure. Whip checks connecting two hose ends may also be attached to an anchor point to limit motion further if this is practicable.<sup id=""cite_ref-EGIS_2013_24-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-EGIS_2013-24"">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
"
"whip sock (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: <span title=""See entry on this page at § containment grip"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#containment_grip"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">containment grip</a></span><sup id=""cite_ref-Whipchecks_25-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Whipchecks-25"">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></span></p>Whip check device which contains a short section of the whip within a braided tube which reduces wear and point loading on the hose, and constrains motion of the hose end more than a standard whip check in case of disconnection under pressure.<sup id=""cite_ref-Whipsocks_26-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Whipsocks-26"">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>"
"wing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backplate_and_wing"" title=""Backplate and wing"">Backplate and wing</a></span></p>
Back inflation <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buoyancy_compensator_(diving)"" title=""Buoyancy compensator (diving)"">buoyancy compensator</a> cell.
"
"WKPP (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woodville_Karst_Plain_Project"" title=""Woodville Karst Plain Project"">Woodville Karst Plain Project</a>, a project to survey subterranean aquifers in Florida.

"
"woolly bear (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A wool or synthetic pile thermal under-suit worn under a diving <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_suit"" title=""Dry suit"">dry suit</a>, particularly with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_diving_dress"" title=""Standard diving dress"">standard diving dress</a>, often one-piece.<sup id=""cite_ref-Rey_2012_27-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Rey_2012-27"">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
"
"working pressure (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""charging pressure""</span></p> 
Maximum filling pressure rating for the cylinder at standard temperature.<sup id=""cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-5"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-SANS_10019-7"">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
"
"work of breathing (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""WOB""</span></p>
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Work_of_breathing"" title=""Work of breathing"">Work of breathing</a></span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See also: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breathing_performance_of_regulators"" title=""Breathing performance of regulators"">Breathing performance of regulators</a></span></p>
The effort expended in inhaling and exhaling the breathing gas.
"
"wreck diving (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wreck_diving"" title=""Wreck diving"">Wreck diving</a></span></p>
Recreational or technical diving on and inside of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shipwreck"" title=""Shipwreck"">shipwrecks</a>.
"
"wrist slate (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A small plastic writing surface attached to the diver's wrist



"
"yoke adaptor (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A fitting used to connect a regulator or filling whip with a DIN thread connection to a  <span title=""See entry on this page at § CGA 850"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#CGA_850"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">CGA 850</a></span> ""international"" connection cylinder valve.<sup id=""cite_ref-Harlow_1999_28-0"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Harlow_1999-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"yoke fitting (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A fitting used to connect a regulator or filling whip to a diving cylinder using the <span title=""See entry on this page at § CGA 850"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#CGA_850"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">CGA 850</a></span> ""international"" connection.<sup id=""cite_ref-Harlow_1999_28-1"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Harlow_1999-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"yoke valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
A valve used to connect a regulator or filling whip to a diving cylinder using the <span title=""See entry on this page at § CGA 850"" class=""glossary-link-internal"" style=""border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;"" id=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#CGA_850"" title=""Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C"">CGA 850</a></span> ""international"" connection, mostly used in the US and countries where US diving tourists are economically important.<sup id=""cite_ref-Harlow_1999_28-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""#cite_note-Harlow_1999-28"">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
"
"Y-valve (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""slingshot valve""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">See: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuba_cylinder_valve#Dual_outlet_valves"" title=""Scuba cylinder valve"">Scuba cylinder valve#Dual outlet valves</a></span></p>
Cylinder valve body with two outlets and two valve mechanisms which can be independently controlled so that two regulator first stages can be fitted. Similar to H-valve but in Y configuration.


"
"ZHL-8 (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|""
"ZHL-16 (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%BChlmann_decompression_algorithm"" title=""Bühlmann decompression algorithm"">Bühlmann decompression algorithms</a>. Also ZHL-16a, b and c
"
"zip tie (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Also: ""cable tie"", ""tie wrap""</span></p> 
<p class=""glossary-hatnote""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096""/><span role=""note"" class=""hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref"">Main article: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cable_tie"" title=""Cable tie"">Cable tie</a></span></p>
Self-locking plastic strip used to connect objects together.
"
"Z-knife (Wikipedia Glossary of Underwater Diving Terminology)"|"
Line cutting tool with a replaceable blade in a slot.
"
